# Changelog

This changelog tracks the per-file diff compared to upstream commit [`2aa11ae076e9fc8251756431e5a4bf940054d0ef`](https://github.com/pingdotgg/t3code/commit/2aa11ae076e9fc8251756431e5a4bf940054d0ef).

Scope note: this review skips direct test files (`*.test.*`, `*.spec.*`, `*.integration.*`, and browser test fixtures such as `*.browser.*`) and markdown files (`*.md`, `*.MD`), then records the remaining per-file deltas, inferred feature intent, and dependency impact as a file-by-file maintenance knowledge base.

Second-pass feature taxonomy: unless a file clearly does not fit, each `Feature` line is framed around one of the five user-facing themes in this fork compared to upstream: `Kiro Integration`, `Remote SSH Support`, `Multi-Repo Support`, `Debugability and Stability`, or `Extra Customization`.

Reading rule: treat each `Dependency impact` line as the local maintenance map for that file. It should tell you which contracts, projections, adapters, and UI surfaces the file plugs into, plus the user flows that deserve retesting when the file changes.

## Files 1-25

### `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/bug_report.yml`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Whole file
This file has three relevant file-touching commits in its current history: `790fda1a` created the original automatic-triage form, `5b8bd728` removed most of the process-heavy triage fields, and `7a3165e3` added back explicit `validations.required: false` plus `validations.description` on the `attachments` upload block. The live delta against upstream is therefore one main simplification pass plus one small attachment-upload follow-up.

#### `Lines 4-55`
The form dropped the `needs-triage` label from the top-level `labels` array, removed the entire `body` block with `type: checkboxes` / `id: checks`, removed `dropdown` / `id: impact`, removed `input` / `id: version`, removed `input` / `id: environment`, removed `textarea` / `id: workaround`, and removed most `validations.required: true` clauses from `area`, `steps`, `expected`, and `actual`. It also changed the opening markdown copy from "Search existing issues first and keep the report focused on one problem." to "Add only the details that will be useful later." and changed `steps.attributes.description` from "Provide a minimal, deterministic repro." to "Add a repro if you have one."

#### `Lines 57-65`
The `attachments` upload block is a separate follow-up change set. Upstream only kept `attributes.description` and `accept`. The fork now also sets `validations.required: false` and duplicates the attachment help text into `validations.description`. Current blame ties these lines to `7a3165e3`.
- Feature:
#### Whole file
This file does not map cleanly to the five fork product features. It is a repository-maintenance change: the GitHub Issue Form was narrowed from a contributor-process-heavy triage workflow to a smaller single-maintainer intake form whose authoritative body fields are now `area`, `steps`, `expected`, `actual`, `logs`, and `attachments`.

#### `Lines 4-55`
Changed the issue form so the authoritative bug-report structure is now a small debugging payload instead of a full triage questionnaire. The form now asks for only the fields that are directly useful during later investigation, which is the actual repository-intake behavior change introduced by `5b8bd728`.

#### `Lines 57-65`
Changed the `attachments` upload field metadata so screenshot or log uploads are explicitly optional and carry a clearer prompt in the validation payload as well as in the visible field description. This is still part of the same repository-intake simplification, but it is a distinct commit-sized follow-up for attachment handling.
- Dependency impact:
#### Whole file
There is no application runtime dependency here. The only contract is GitHub Issue Forms YAML itself, and the only user flow is issue submission in GitHub. There is no fallback path in app code if this template is wrong; the failure mode is a broken or misleading issue form in the GitHub UI.

#### `Lines 4-55`
This change is coupled only to GitHub's issue-form field parser and to maintainer triage habits. The important fields that must keep rendering are `area`, `steps`, `expected`, `actual`, and `logs`; the removed fields are `checks`, `impact`, `version`, `environment`, and `workaround`. If this block is wrong, the breakage is visible in GitHub issue creation: missing fields, invalid form schema, or a form that asks for process metadata the fork no longer wants to maintain.

#### `Lines 57-65`
The only dependency here is GitHub's upload-field schema for Issue Forms. The authoritative field remains `id: attachments`, and the follow-up clarifies how `description`, `validations.required`, and `accept` are interpreted. If this block is wrong, the likely failures are GitHub rejecting the YAML schema or presenting the attachment field with confusing upload requirements.

### `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/feature_request.yml`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Whole file
The live delta is dominated by `5b8bd728` (`Simplify issue templates for single-maintainer use`). The current form removes the top-level `needs-triage` label, deletes the `body` block with `type: checkboxes` / `id: checks`, deletes the `textarea` blocks with `id: value`, `id: scope`, `id: alternatives`, and `id: tradeoffs`, removes `validations.required: true` from the remaining `area`, `problem`, and `proposal` fields, and rewrites several labels and descriptions in place.

#### `Lines 4-45`
The current template keeps `labels: [enhancement]` and the four remaining body fields, but removes the `needs-triage` label and all contributor-process-heavy fields. Specifically, upstream had `checks`, `value`, `scope`, `alternatives`, and `tradeoffs`; the fork deletes all of them. It also changes `problem.attributes.label` from `Problem or use case` to `Problem or idea`, `problem.attributes.description` from "What are you trying to do? What is hard, slow, or impossible today?" to "What do you want to change?", `proposal.attributes.label` from `Proposed solution` to `Proposed change`, `proposal.attributes.description` from "Describe the behavior, API, or UX you want." to "How should it work?", and `references.attributes.label` / `description` from examples-oriented wording to `Notes or references` plus an explicitly optional description.
- Feature:
#### Whole file
This file also sits outside the five fork product features. It is a repository-maintenance change: the authoritative feature-intake fields are now `area`, `problem`, `proposal`, and `references`, and the form is intentionally lighter than the upstream contributor-triage version.

#### `Lines 4-45`
Changed the feature-request form so the authoritative maintenance payload is now the narrow set of fields needed to capture a concrete request without forcing extra justification or contribution metadata. That is the actual intake behavior change introduced by the single-maintainer simplification pass.
- Dependency impact:
#### Whole file
There is no runtime application dependency. The only contract is GitHub Issue Forms YAML, and the only user flow is feature-request submission in GitHub. There is no in-app fallback path if this schema is wrong; the failure mode is a broken or misleading GitHub form.

#### `Lines 4-45`
This block depends only on GitHub rendering the remaining field IDs exactly as written: `area`, `problem`, `proposal`, and `references`. The removed fields are the old upstream scoping and maintenance-cost prompts. If this block is wrong, the visible breakage is either invalid GitHub Issue Forms YAML or a form that still asks for upstream-style contributor workflow detail the fork no longer wants.

### `.mise.toml`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Whole file
The live delta is two change sets. `0b6e734c` changed the authoritative `mise` runtime keys from exact pins to broader channels by rewriting `[tools].node` from `"24.13.1"` to `"24"` and `[tools].bun` from `"1.3.9"` to `"latest"`, then added six new CLI bootstrap keys: `[tools]."npm:turbo"`, `[tools]."npm:tsdown"`, `[tools]."npm:typescript"`, `[tools]."npm:oxfmt"`, `[tools]."npm:oxlint"`, and `[tools]."npm:node-gyp"`. `02ba9363` later added `[tools]."npm:@anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk"` plus `[tools]."npm:anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk"`. Upstream only carried the three-line file with pinned `node` and `bun`.

#### `Lines 2-9`
`0b6e734c` rewrote `[tools].node = "24.13.1"` to `[tools].node = "24"` and `[tools].bun = "1.3.9"` to `[tools].bun = "latest"`, then added six new keys: `[tools]."npm:turbo"`, `[tools]."npm:tsdown"`, `[tools]."npm:typescript"`, `[tools]."npm:oxfmt"`, `[tools]."npm:oxlint"`, and `[tools]."npm:node-gyp"`. Those keys occupy current lines 4-9, and blame ties the whole block to the remote-worktree series around `0b6e734c`.

#### `Lines 10-11`
`02ba9363` appended two Claude SDK bootstrap keys with no upstream equivalent: `[tools]."npm:@anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk"` and `[tools]."npm:anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk"`. The current file therefore carries both the scoped package name and an extra unscoped install key.
- Feature:
#### Whole file
This file now mixes two fork themes: the runtime/CLI bootstrap expansion is for `Remote SSH Support`, and the Claude SDK bootstrap add-on fits `Extra Customization`. In both cases the file is part of the local toolchain bootstrap component, because it defines which binaries a fresh machine gets before any repo script runs.

#### `Lines 2-9`
Changed `mise` from a narrow runtime pin file into the authoritative bootstrap surface for the repo’s core CLI toolchain so a new remote machine can run the same build, lint, format, and bundle commands without hand-installing binaries first. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and is part of the remote-worktree/bootstrap component that sits underneath SSH project prep, remote bundle builds, and first-run environment bring-up.

#### `Lines 10-11`
Changed the bootstrap tool list so a fresh machine can provision Claude SDK packages alongside the rest of the repo toolchain without a separate manual install step. This fits `Extra Customization` and is part of the provider-development bootstrap component for non-upstream provider work in this fork.
- Dependency impact:
#### Whole file
`.mise.toml` is not a runtime contract, but it is the first bootstrap contract for clean machines. If these keys drift, the main breakage is not in application logic; it is in environment bring-up. The important downstream consumers are root `package.json` scripts that call `turbo`, `oxfmt`, and `oxlint`; package build scripts that call `tsdown`; native dependency installs that may need `node-gyp`; and Claude-provider development flows that assume the SDK exists after `mise install`. The fallback path is manual global installation or relying on package-manager-installed binaries instead of `mise`, so changes here should trigger fresh-machine setup retests rather than only app-level smoke tests.

#### `Lines 2-9`
The authoritative variables are now `[tools].node`, `[tools].bun`, and the six `[tools]."npm:*"` entries. The old contract they replaced was "only Node and Bun are provisioned by `mise`; everything else is assumed to exist globally or arrive indirectly through package installs." The practical fallback path is still manual/global installation plus `bun install`, but that fallback is no longer the preferred path. This block hooks into root [package.json](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/package.json) script names `build`, `start`, `typecheck`, `lint`, `fmt`, and `build:desktop`; package-local `tsdown` build scripts in [apps/server/package.json](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/package.json), [apps/desktop/package.json](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/desktop/package.json), and [packages/contracts/package.json](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/packages/contracts/package.json); and the remote-worktree series that touched [apps/server/src/sshCommand.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/sshCommand.ts), [apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitCore.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitCore.ts), and [apps/web/src/threadEnvMode.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/threadEnvMode.ts). If this block is wrong, the user-visible failures are remote setup stalls, missing `turbo`/`oxfmt`/`oxlint`/`tsdown` binaries, or native package install failures that surface before the app even starts. Retest `mise install`, remote SSH project prep, and clean-machine `bun fmt` / `bun lint` / `bun typecheck`.

#### `Lines 10-11`
The authoritative runtime import still uses the old package contract `@anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk` in [apps/server/src/provider/Layers/ClaudeAdapter.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/provider/Layers/ClaudeAdapter.ts). The old `.mise` contract it replaced was "Claude SDK is not provisioned here at all." The extra unscoped key does not replace the runtime import path; it is a bootstrap fallback/compatibility path at install time. This block intersects [apps/server/package.json](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/package.json), [scripts/package.json](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/scripts/package.json), and `bun.lock` resolution for the Claude SDK. If these lines are wrong, the breakage shows up as failed local provider bootstrap or missing-module errors during Claude adapter development/probes rather than as a generic UI regression. Retest fresh `mise install` plus any local Claude provider startup or probe workflow that assumes the SDK is already present.

### `.tmp/xcrun_db`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Whole file (binary artifact)`
`ec26109c` added `.tmp/xcrun_db` as a `100644` binary blob of `491` bytes. There is no line-level source diff because the entire file is opaque binary data. The payload starts with the `XR1L` header and embeds local Apple SDK paths such as `/Library/Developer/CommandLineTools/SDKs/MacOSX.sdk`, which identifies it as cached `xcrun` / Command Line Tools state rather than as an application-owned asset or schema. The authoritative delta is simply the presence of this generated blob at `.tmp/xcrun_db`; the old contract it replaced was upstream having no file at this path. There is no application fallback path because no code in the repo reads this file.
- Feature:
#### `Whole file (binary artifact)`
No intentional user feature. This file does not implement `Kiro Integration`, `Remote SSH Support`, `Multi-Repo Support`, `Debugability and Stability`, or `Extra Customization`; it is machine-local cache residue that was committed alongside unrelated work.
- Dependency impact:
#### `Whole file (binary artifact)`
No runtime, persistence, WS/native API, or UI dependency chain was found. `rg` shows no references to `.tmp/xcrun_db` or `xcrun_db` anywhere else in the repo, so changing or deleting it does not require product retesting. The only practical impact is source-control noise during rebases, release diffs, and cleanup.

### `apps/desktop/src/main.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Whole file
The live delta in this file is three distinct contract sets layered on top of the upstream desktop shell. `64173a3e` introduced `DesktopAppCloseBehavior`, persisted desktop/backend state files (`desktop-settings.json`, `desktop-backend.json`), background-backend adoption, runtime control POSTs, and asynchronous quit preparation. `86e7b460` replaced the old `T3CODE_STATE_DIR` contract with `BASE_DIR = process.env.T3CODE_HOME?.trim() || Path.join(OS.homedir(), ".t3")` and derived `STATE_DIR = Path.join(BASE_DIR, "userdata")`. `64e2926e` then removed env-based secret delivery (`T3CODE_PORT`, `T3CODE_AUTH_TOKEN`, `T3CODE_DESKTOP_WS_URL`) in favor of `--bootstrap-fd 3`, a one-shot bootstrap JSON payload, and a sync IPC channel `desktop:get-ws-url`. In effect, the fork turned this file from a simple Electron launcher into the authoritative desktop backend supervisor.

#### `Lines 62-63, 1207-1211`
`86e7b460` changed the desktop data-root contract from a single `T3CODE_STATE_DIR` path to a base/root pair: `BASE_DIR = process.env.T3CODE_HOME?.trim() || Path.join(OS.homedir(), ".t3")` and `STATE_DIR = Path.join(BASE_DIR, "userdata")`. The same change set also moved the value sent to the backend from a raw state-dir env var to the base-dir key `t3Home: BASE_DIR` in the bootstrap payload. The authoritative variable is now `BASE_DIR`; the old variable/contract it replaced was `T3CODE_STATE_DIR`.

#### `Lines 61, 215-230, 245-253, 1132-1218, 1431-1434, 1690-1699`
`64e2926e` changed how the desktop process provisions backend connection state. `setBackendConnection()` no longer writes `process.env.T3CODE_DESKTOP_WS_URL`; `backendChildEnv()` now explicitly strips `T3CODE_PORT`, `T3CODE_AUTH_TOKEN`, `T3CODE_MODE`, `T3CODE_NO_BROWSER`, `T3CODE_HOST`, and `T3CODE_DESKTOP_WS_URL` from the child environment; `startBackend()` now spawns the server with `--bootstrap-fd 3` and writes a one-shot JSON envelope `{ mode, noBrowser, port, t3Home, authToken }` to fd `3`; `registerIpcHandlers()` adds the sync IPC responder `desktop:get-ws-url`; and `bootstrap()` now chooses between `adoptPersistedBackendIfAvailable()` and `reserveNewBackendConnection()` before starting or reusing the backend. The old contract it replaced was env-plumbing of sensitive runtime values into both the backend child and the renderer.

#### `Lines 60, 81-98, 124-230, 1364-1479, 1705-1780`
`64173a3e` introduced the new close-behavior contract end to end. The file now imports `DesktopAppCloseBehavior`, defines `DEFAULT_DESKTOP_APP_CLOSE_BEHAVIOR = "terminate_all_agents"`, persists `appCloseBehavior` in `desktop-settings.json`, persists backend connection metadata in `desktop-backend.json`, exposes IPC `desktop:app-close-behavior:set`, adds `requestBackendControl()` for `GET`/`POST` runtime control, implements `applyAppCloseBehavior()` with the three authoritative cases `terminate_all_agents`, `terminate_local_agents_only`, and `terminate_no_agents`, and replaces direct `before-quit` / `SIGINT` / `SIGTERM` shutdown with `prepareForQuitAndExit(reason)`. The old behavior it replaced was effectively a single unconditional shutdown path: clear timers, `stopBackend()`, and quit.
- Feature:
#### Whole file
This file primarily mixes `Debugability and Stability` with `Extra Customization`. The stability side is the secure bootstrap/runtime handoff plus persisted backend adoption and guarded quit flow. The customization side is the user-selectable desktop close behavior. Together they form the desktop supervisor/runtime-lifecycle component.

#### `Lines 62-63, 1207-1211`
Changed desktop state resolution so the desktop shell and server can share a relocatable top-level home directory rather than hard-coding everything around one userdata path. This fits `Extra Customization` and is part of the desktop/server data-root bootstrap component.

#### `Lines 61, 215-230, 245-253, 1132-1218, 1431-1434, 1690-1699`
Changed desktop backend bootstrap from ambient environment propagation to explicit one-shot bootstrap plus runtime IPC lookup. This supports `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the desktop bootstrap/runtime handoff component.

#### `Lines 60, 81-98, 124-230, 1364-1479, 1705-1780`
Changed desktop shutdown semantics so the user can choose whether app exit kills all agents, only local agents, or no agents while still preserving a guarded quit path. This fits `Extra Customization` and is part of the desktop shutdown/session-lifecycle component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Whole file
This file now sits on the contract chain between Electron main-process IPC, the desktop preload bridge, the server bootstrap parser, and the desktop runtime control endpoint. The authoritative variables and fields are `BASE_DIR`, `STATE_DIR`, `DESKTOP_SETTINGS_PATH`, `DESKTOP_BACKEND_STATE_PATH`, `desktopAppCloseBehavior`, the bootstrap payload keys `mode`, `noBrowser`, `port`, `t3Home`, `authToken`, the sync IPC method `desktop:get-ws-url`, and the POST actions `shutdown-server` / `stop-local-sessions`. The old contracts it replaced were `T3CODE_STATE_DIR`, `process.env.T3CODE_DESKTOP_WS_URL`, and unconditional `stopBackend()` on quit. Important fallback paths are preserved in code: stale persisted backend state is discarded if health probing fails, missing local-only shutdown support falls back to full shutdown, and a missing bootstrap pipe kills the child and schedules restart. Retest desktop cold start, relaunch with an already-running detached backend, each close-behavior mode, update install quit flow, and renderer bootstrap of the WS URL.

#### `Lines 62-63, 1207-1211`
This block feeds every desktop-owned path under `STATE_DIR`, including `logs`, `desktop-settings.json`, and `desktop-backend.json`, and it must stay aligned with [apps/server/src/main.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/main.ts#L404), where `--home-dir` / `T3CODE_HOME` is the server-side authoritative input. The fallback path is the default `~/.t3` root when `T3CODE_HOME` is unset. If this block is wrong, the failures are misplaced desktop state, server data written under the wrong root, or migrations/logs/settings splitting across different directories. Retest desktop launch with and without `T3CODE_HOME`, then verify desktop settings, logs, and backend-owned state all land under the same base directory.

#### `Lines 61, 215-230, 245-253, 1132-1218, 1431-1434, 1690-1699`
This block depends directly on [apps/desktop/src/preload.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/desktop/src/preload.ts#L15), which calls `ipcRenderer.sendSync("desktop:get-ws-url")`; [apps/server/src/main.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/main.ts#L422), which declares the `--bootstrap-fd` flag and consumes `T3CODE_HOME`; and [apps/server/src/bootstrap.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/bootstrap.ts), which decodes the inherited bootstrap envelope. The health-probe side of adoption also depends on the desktop runtime route in [apps/server/src/wsServer.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/wsServer.ts#L574). Fallback paths are explicit: if the persisted backend fails the GET probe, the saved backend state is deleted and a new port/token pair is reserved; if fd `3` is unavailable, the child is terminated and restart is scheduled. If this block is wrong, the renderer can boot with no WS URL, the backend can inherit secrets it should not see through env, or desktop relaunch can fail to adopt a healthy detached backend. Retest first launch, relaunch against persisted backend state, and renderer startup before the first websocket connection.

#### `Lines 60, 81-98, 124-230, 1364-1479, 1705-1780`
The authoritative contract starts in [packages/contracts/src/ipc.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/packages/contracts/src/ipc.ts#L76), where `DesktopAppCloseBehavior` and `DesktopBridge.setAppCloseBehavior()` are defined; continues through [apps/desktop/src/preload.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/desktop/src/preload.ts#L14), which exposes the setter to the renderer; and is driven from desktop settings UI code in [apps/web/src/routes/_chat.settings.tsx](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/routes/_chat.settings.tsx#L86) and [apps/web/src/routes/__root.tsx](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/routes/__root.tsx#L340). The runtime control actions `stop-local-sessions` and `shutdown-server` are served by [apps/server/src/wsServer.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/wsServer.ts#L589). The explicit fallback path is important: if `terminate_local_agents_only` cannot stop sessions cleanly over HTTP, the code logs the failure and falls back to full backend shutdown. If this block is wrong, the user-visible failures are desktop exits that kill the wrong sessions, background agents that survive when they should not, or update/quit flows that double-run or hang because `quitPrepared` / `quitPreparationPromise` are out of sync. Retest all three close-behavior settings, detached-backend survival after app exit, and update install while quitting.

### `apps/desktop/src/preload.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Whole file
The live preload delta is two small but important bridge changes. `64173a3e` added the new IPC channel constant `desktop:app-close-behavior:set` and exposed `desktopBridge.setAppCloseBehavior(behavior)`. `64e2926e` then removed the static preload-time environment capture `const wsUrl = process.env.T3CODE_DESKTOP_WS_URL ?? null`, added `const GET_WS_URL_CHANNEL = "desktop:get-ws-url"`, and rewired `desktopBridge.getWsUrl()` to call `ipcRenderer.sendSync(GET_WS_URL_CHANNEL)` instead. The authoritative bridge contract is therefore now runtime IPC, not inherited process env.

#### `Lines 14, 25`
`64173a3e` added `const APP_CLOSE_BEHAVIOR_SET_CHANNEL = "desktop:app-close-behavior:set"` and the new bridge method `setAppCloseBehavior: (behavior) => ipcRenderer.invoke(APP_CLOSE_BEHAVIOR_SET_CHANNEL, behavior)`. Upstream had no close-behavior bridge method in preload.

#### `Lines 15, 18-21`
`64e2926e` replaced `const wsUrl = process.env.T3CODE_DESKTOP_WS_URL ?? null` with `const GET_WS_URL_CHANNEL = "desktop:get-ws-url"` and changed `getWsUrl()` to call `ipcRenderer.sendSync(GET_WS_URL_CHANNEL)` and type-check the response. The authoritative variable is now the sync IPC channel response; the old variable was the preload-captured env string `wsUrl`.
- Feature:
#### Whole file
This file mixes `Extra Customization` with `Debugability and Stability`: it exposes the desktop close-behavior preference setter and hardens renderer bootstrap so the websocket URL is fetched from Electron main at runtime instead of being frozen into preload env. It is part of the desktop renderer-bridge component.

#### `Lines 14, 25`
Changed the desktop preload bridge to expose the user-configurable app-close-behavior control from renderer to Electron main. This fits `Extra Customization` and is part of the desktop settings-to-main-process bridge component.

#### `Lines 15, 18-21`
Changed websocket bootstrap so the renderer asks Electron main for the live desktop backend websocket URL instead of trusting a secret-bearing env var injected at process start. This supports `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the secure desktop bootstrap bridge.
- Dependency impact:
#### Whole file
The authoritative bridge methods are `getWsUrl()` and `setAppCloseBehavior()`. The old contract they replaced was `getWsUrl` reading `process.env.T3CODE_DESKTOP_WS_URL` and no close-behavior setter at all. This file depends directly on [apps/desktop/src/main.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/desktop/src/main.ts), which registers both IPC channels; on [packages/contracts/src/ipc.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/packages/contracts/src/ipc.ts#L111), which types `DesktopBridge`; and on the renderer settings sync in [apps/web/src/routes/__root.tsx](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/routes/__root.tsx#L340). The fallback path in `getWsUrl()` is to return `null` if the sync IPC response is not a string. If this bridge drifts, the renderer will either boot with no websocket endpoint or silently fail to push the app-close-behavior setting down to the main process.

#### `Lines 14, 25`
This bridge method must stay aligned with [packages/contracts/src/ipc.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/packages/contracts/src/ipc.ts#L111), [apps/desktop/src/main.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/desktop/src/main.ts#L1471), and the settings UI in [apps/web/src/routes/_chat.settings.tsx](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/routes/_chat.settings.tsx#L898). The old contract it replaced was "desktop close behavior is not configurable from the renderer." If this line is wrong, changing the setting in the UI will not persist or apply.

#### `Lines 15, 18-21`
This method depends on [apps/desktop/src/main.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/desktop/src/main.ts#L1431), where `desktop:get-ws-url` is registered, and on the bootstrap-fd handoff in [apps/desktop/src/main.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/desktop/src/main.ts#L1180) that creates `backendWsUrl` in the first place. The fallback path is explicit in preload: non-string responses become `null`. If this block is wrong, the renderer cannot connect to the backend after secure bootstrap, especially when the backend is adopted or restarted at runtime rather than launched with a fixed inherited env.

### `apps/server/src/checkpointing/Layers/CheckpointDiffQuery.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Whole file
This file has two fork-specific change sets on top of upstream. `0ae86206` (`feat(remote): enable git, diff, terminal, and workspace flows over SSH`) added `Option`, `ProjectionTurnRepository`, `isProviderDiffCheckpointRef(checkpointRef.startsWith("provider-diff:"))`, rewrote the lookup from `const toCheckpointRef = ...?.checkpointRef` to `const toCheckpoint = ...; const toCheckpointRef = toCheckpoint?.checkpointRef;`, and introduced a provider-diff fast path that loads `ProjectionTurnRepository.getByTurnId({ threadId: input.threadId, turnId: toCheckpoint.turnId })` and returns `turnRowOption.value.checkpointDiff` instead of diffing two filesystem checkpoints. `fcd79049` (`Guard remote checkpoint diffs and validate workspace git state`) then added `const supportedFromTurnCount = Math.max(0, input.toTurnCount - 1)` so `provider-diff:*` refs can only serve a single-turn diff, and inserted `checkpointStore.isGitRepository(workspaceCwd)` before `hasCheckpointRef` / `diffCheckpoints` so remote or missing workspaces fail with `CheckpointUnavailableError` instead of falling through to git operations that cannot succeed.

#### `Lines 2-26, 94-150`
`0ae86206` added `ProjectionTurnRepository` beside `ProjectionSnapshotQuery` and `CheckpointStore`, introduced `isProviderDiffCheckpointRef = (checkpointRef: string) => checkpointRef.startsWith("provider-diff:")`, and changed the target-checkpoint lookup from a bare `toCheckpointRef` string into the full `toCheckpoint` object so the code can use both `toCheckpoint.checkpointRef` and `toCheckpoint.turnId`. The new provider path checks `isProviderDiffCheckpointRef(toCheckpoint.checkpointRef)`, calls `projectionTurnRepository.getByTurnId({ threadId: input.threadId, turnId: toCheckpoint.turnId })`, reads `turnRowOption.value.checkpointDiff`, validates the returned object with `isTurnDiffResult`, and returns `{ threadId, fromTurnCount, toTurnCount, diff }` without touching git checkpoint refs at all.

#### `Lines 106-159`
`fcd79049` added two explicit guards around the remote/provider path. First, it computes `supportedFromTurnCount = Math.max(0, input.toTurnCount - 1)` and rejects any provider-diff request where `input.fromTurnCount !== supportedFromTurnCount`, which blocks the old `getFullThreadDiff({ fromTurnCount: 0, ... })` style call from pretending that a provider-emitted single-turn diff can answer a multi-turn range. Second, after `workspaceCwd = resolveThreadWorkspaceCwd(...)` but before `checkpointStore.hasCheckpointRef(...)`, it calls `checkpointStore.isGitRepository(workspaceCwd)` and returns `CheckpointUnavailableError("Turn diffs are unavailable because workspace ... is missing or is not a git repository.")` when the resolved workspace is absent or non-git.
- Feature:
#### Whole file
Changed the checkpoint diff query so the authoritative diff source can be either a projected per-turn `checkpointDiff` string or the older git-checkpoint diff path, depending on the `checkpointRef` shape. That behavior is primarily `Remote SSH Support`, because remote/provider-backed turns may only have a provider-emitted diff instead of two local git checkpoint refs, and secondarily `Debugability and Stability`, because the query now rejects unsupported provider-diff ranges and non-git workspaces with explicit contract errors instead of noisy downstream git failures. This file is part of the checkpoint diff query and projection-backed turn-diff component.

#### `Lines 2-26, 94-150`
Changed the turn-diff source selection so `provider-diff:*` checkpoints resolve through projected turn state rather than filesystem checkpoint pairs. Concretely, this changed the query from "derive a diff from two checkpoint refs in a git repository" to "if the turn came from a provider diff event, use the persisted `checkpointDiff` payload keyed by the target turn." That is a detailed `Remote SSH Support` change and is part of the provider-backed checkpoint diff component that lets remote/provider sessions surface diffs even when the server cannot materialize both sides as local git checkpoints.

#### `Lines 106-159`
Changed the defensive contract around diff lookup so provider-backed turns only answer the exact range they actually represent, and git-backed turns only proceed when the resolved workspace can satisfy git operations. This is primarily `Debugability and Stability`, because it narrows the supported API surface to the ranges and workspace states the backend can prove are real, and it also supports `Remote SSH Support`, because remote workspaces and provider diffs are the cases that most often violate the old local-git assumptions.
- Dependency impact:
#### Whole file
The authoritative provider-diff value is now `ProjectionTurns.checkpointDiff`, looked up by `toCheckpoint.turnId`; the old contract it partially replaces was "all turn diffs come from `CheckpointStore.hasCheckpointRef` plus `CheckpointStore.diffCheckpoints` against a git cwd." The fallback path is still present: non-`provider-diff:` refs continue through the filesystem checkpoint path, while provider-diff refs return `CheckpointUnavailableError` when the projected turn row is missing, `checkpointDiff` is not a string, or the caller asks for anything other than `fromTurnCount === Math.max(0, toTurnCount - 1)`. This file is coupled to `ProjectionTurnRepositoryLive` wiring in `apps/server/src/serverLayers.ts`, `checkpointDiff` persistence in `apps/server/src/persistence/Layers/ProjectionTurns.ts`, projection updates in `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionPipeline.ts`, provider-diff ref creation in `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProviderRuntimeIngestion.ts`, workspace resolution in `apps/server/src/checkpointing/Utils.ts`, and WS/native API handlers in `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts`. If this contract drifts, the user-visible breakage lands in turn diff fetch, full-thread diff fetch, remote workspace diff requests, and any UI/runtime flow that expects provider turns to show diffs without local git checkpoints.

#### `Lines 2-26, 94-150`
The authoritative variables are now `toCheckpoint`, `toCheckpoint.turnId`, `toCheckpoint.checkpointRef`, and `turnRowOption.value.checkpointDiff`. The old variables/contract it replaced were the narrower `toCheckpointRef` string and the assumption that `hasCheckpointRef` / `diffCheckpoints` are always the source of truth. This change depends on `ProjectionTurnRepository.getByTurnId`, `checkpoint_diff_text AS "checkpointDiff"` in `apps/server/src/persistence/Layers/ProjectionTurns.ts`, `checkpointDiff` carry-forward logic in `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionPipeline.ts`, and `CheckpointRef.makeUnsafe(\`provider-diff:${event.eventId}\`)` in `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProviderRuntimeIngestion.ts`. If this block is wrong, provider-backed turns lose their diff, full-thread and turn-diff endpoints can report an empty or invalid payload, and the UI path driven from `orchestrationGetTurnDiff` / `orchestrationGetFullThreadDiff` in `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` stops matching what the provider runtime actually emitted.

#### `Lines 106-159`
The authoritative guard variables are `supportedFromTurnCount`, `input.fromTurnCount`, `input.toTurnCount`, `workspaceCwd`, and `checkpointStore.isGitRepository(workspaceCwd)`. The old behavior it replaced was an implicit fallback path where provider diffs were treated like generic checkpoints and non-git workspaces still reached `hasCheckpointRef` / `diffCheckpoints`. The remaining fallback path is explicit: provider-diff requests outside the one-turn window now fail fast, and filesystem diffs only run after the git-repo check passes. This guard chain depends on `resolveThreadWorkspaceCwd` in `apps/server/src/checkpointing/Utils.ts`, `CheckpointStore.isGitRepository` in `apps/server/src/checkpointing/Layers/CheckpointStore.ts`, and WS callers in `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` that expose both turn and full-thread diff methods. If this block is wrong, the API can claim multi-turn diffs it cannot compute, remote/non-git workspaces can fail deeper in git execution with harder-to-debug errors, and UI diff panels can flap between "missing diff" and transport failure depending on whether the bad workspace path reaches git.

### `apps/server/src/checkpointing/Utils.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Whole file
This helper has one real fork feature change plus one small follow-up cleanup. `efd5f211` (`feat: add multi-repo git discovery and worktree support`) changed the `thread` input contract from `worktreePath: string | null` to `projectPath: string`, replaced `const worktreeCwd = input.thread.worktreePath ?? undefined` with `const projectPath = input.thread.projectPath.trim()`, and changed the fast-path branch to `if (projectPath.length > 0) return projectPath;`. `033511d9` (`feat(git): add project-level multi-repo discovery state`) then rewrote the fallback from an inline `input.projects.find((project) => project.id === input.thread.projectId)?.workspaceRoot` into `const project = input.projects.find((entry) => entry.id === input.thread.projectId); return project?.workspaceRoot;`. Upstream still resolves checkpoint cwd from a single nullable `worktreePath`; the fork resolves it from the thread’s selected `projectPath` first and only falls back to the owning project row.

#### `Lines 12-16`
`efd5f211` changed the `input.thread` shape from `{ projectId, worktreePath: string | null }` to `{ projectId, projectPath: string }`. That is the exact type-level delta on current lines 13-16.

#### `Lines 22-24`
Upstream used `const worktreeCwd = input.thread.worktreePath ?? undefined; if (worktreeCwd) return worktreeCwd;`. The fork now uses `const projectPath = input.thread.projectPath.trim(); if (projectPath.length > 0) return projectPath;`. The explicit variable rename from `worktreeCwd` to `projectPath` and the added `trim()` are both part of `efd5f211`.

#### `Lines 27-28`
`033511d9` changed the fallback from an inline `return input.projects.find((project) => project.id === input.thread.projectId)?.workspaceRoot;` to `const project = input.projects.find((entry) => entry.id === input.thread.projectId); return project?.workspaceRoot;`.
- Feature:
#### Whole file
Changed the checkpoint workspace resolver so checkpoint diff and checkpoint revert follow the thread-selected repository path inside a multi-repo project instead of assuming a project has one authoritative worktree path. Concretely, the file now treats `thread.projectPath` as the first-class cwd, trims it before use, and only falls back to `project.workspaceRoot` when thread-level repo context is absent. This is a detailed `Multi-Repo Support` change and is part of the thread-to-project workspace resolution component used by checkpointing.

#### `Lines 12-16`
Changed the `resolveThreadWorkspaceCwd` input contract so checkpoint code receives a thread-scoped repository path instead of a single nullable worktree path. The practical behavior change is that the helper can now distinguish two threads under one project that point at different repos, which is the low-level checkpointing requirement for `Multi-Repo Support`.

#### `Lines 22-24`
Changed the authoritative workspace selection path from "first non-null worktree path" to "trimmed thread project path." That matters because the thread may now point at a repository root or worktree chosen out of a multi-repo project, and the helper must preserve that exact selection instead of collapsing everything back to one nullable worktree field. This is the behavioral core of the `Multi-Repo Support` divergence in this file, with a smaller `Debugability and Stability` benefit because blank strings are rejected before they can masquerade as a usable cwd.

#### `Lines 27-28`
This is a smaller but still real `Multi-Repo Support` change. The helper now names the fallback project row explicitly because project-level git discovery state became a first-class part of the projection model before every thread had a stable repo-specific path. In other words, the file keeps a project-level escape hatch for older or incomplete thread context instead of assuming thread-level repo selection is always present.
- Dependency impact:
#### Whole file
The authoritative variable is now `input.thread.projectPath`; the old contract it replaced was `input.thread.worktreePath`. The fallback path is explicit: if `projectPath.trim()` is empty, the helper uses `const project = input.projects.find((entry) => entry.id === input.thread.projectId)` and returns `project?.workspaceRoot`. This helper depends on the thread/project projection chain that now persists `projectPath`, `branch[]`, and `worktreePath[]`, and it is consumed directly by checkpoint diff/revert code. If this contract drifts, checkpoint diff and restore can silently target the wrong repository in multi-repo projects, especially when a project exposes several repos under one workspace root.

#### `Lines 12-16`
This line only works because the surrounding contract chain changed with it. `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts` now makes `projectPath` authoritative on `OrchestrationThread` and converts `branch` / `worktreePath` to arrays; `apps/server/src/persistence/Layers/ProjectionThreads.ts` persists `project_path`, `branch_json`, and `worktree_path_json`; `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts` hydrates `projectPath` back into the read model; `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionPipeline.ts` upserts `projectPath` from thread create/update events; and `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/CheckpointReactor.ts` now expects `{ projectId, projectPath }` when resolving checkpoint cwd. If this type drifts, thread hydration and checkpoint execution disagree about which repo a thread belongs to.

#### `Lines 22-24`
These lines make `input.thread.projectPath` the first-class source of truth for checkpoint cwd resolution. That couples this helper to thread event producers and consumers, not just storage: `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionPipeline.ts` must keep projecting `projectPath`, `apps/web/src/store.ts` must keep updating `projectPath` alongside `worktreePath[]`, `packages/shared/src/threadGit.ts` must keep the array-based thread git helpers aligned with the single selected `projectPath`, and both `apps/server/src/checkpointing/Layers/CheckpointDiffQuery.ts` and `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/CheckpointReactor.ts` must keep treating the returned cwd as the repo-specific checkpoint target. If this block is wrong, checkpoint diff or revert can run against the project root or the wrong sibling repo while the UI still thinks the thread is scoped elsewhere.

#### `Lines 27-28`
The fallback variable is now the explicit `project` row, and the fallback value is still `project?.workspaceRoot`. This ties the helper to the project-projection side of the multi-repo series: `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts` added `gitMode` / `gitRepos`, `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts` now discovers or hydrates project repo lists, and `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` gates some git APIs based on project-level multi-repo state. If this fallback changes, retest empty `projectPath` handling, migration or resume scenarios that still rely on project-level workspace roots, and checkpoint operations on projects where repo discovery succeeded but the thread-specific repo path has not been written yet.

- Feature:
#### Whole file
Changed the Codex app-server broker so Codex sessions can launch against SSH-backed projects with host-scoped binary, PATH, and `CODEX_HOME` overrides, while also hardening shutdown and startup observability around session reuse and adapter teardown. The primary feature theme is `Remote SSH Support`, because this file now decides whether Codex launches locally or via `ssh -T <hostAlias> sh -lc ...`; the secondary themes are `Extra Customization`, because per-host binary/home overrides are honored here, and `Debugability and Stability`, because stop-event suppression, reconnect wording, and startup logging all live here. This file is the Codex session broker and process-launch component.

#### `Lines 11, 24-27, 157-159, 429-443, 559-619, 1642-1868`
Changed Codex startup from a local-process-only contract to a remote-aware process broker that can launch on a specific SSH host with host-scoped executable and home-directory overrides. The detailed behavior change is that `providerOptions.codex.remote.hostAlias` now becomes part of both version checking and process startup, `pathEnv` captured from the host login shell becomes authoritative for remote command resolution, and the runtime forces `tools.web_search=false` into Codex app-server startup. This is the core `Remote SSH Support` divergence in the file, with `Extra Customization` layered on top because the host-specific `binaryPath` and `homePath` settings only matter if this launch path honors them.

#### `Lines 623-640, 745-750, 1021-1065`
Changed Codex session lifecycle handling so shutdown and reconnect events reflect the real runtime path instead of always looking like a fresh local start or user-visible close. This is a `Debugability and Stability` change: the file now records the raw startup payloads that explain account/model mismatches, marks resume paths as reconnects, and lets adapter teardown suppress synthetic `session/closed` events that would otherwise pollute recovery flows.

#### `Lines 844-847`
Changed Codex turn-start plumbing so only Codex-supported interaction modes are serialized into the `collaborationMode` payload. The practical behavior is that Codex no longer blindly mirrors whatever higher-level provider interaction mode happened to be present once `Kiro Integration` added more provider-specific session logic around mode handling. This is a small but real `Kiro Integration` and `Debugability and Stability` change inside the Codex broker.

The old contract it replaced was "Codex always launches locally with `spawn(codexBinaryPath, [\"app-server\"], { cwd, env: { ...process.env, CODEX_HOME? } })` and version checks always run with a local `spawnSync(binaryPath, [\"--version\"])`." The fallback paths are explicit: if `remote` is absent the manager still uses the local spawn/version-check path; if `readRemoteEnvironmentFromLoginShell(...)` fails it returns `{}` and the SSH launch continues without exported PATH; if SSH is missing or the remote version check exits non-zero the session start fails before app-server startup; and when unsupported interaction-mode values reach Codex turn start the manager now omits `collaborationMode` instead of forwarding an invalid mode. This file is coupled to `ProviderStartOptions.codex.remote` in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, provider option assembly in `apps/web/src/appSettings.ts`, chat launch wiring in `apps/web/src/components/ChatView.tsx`, provider dispatch in `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProviderCommandReactor.ts`, adapter teardown in `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/CodexAdapter.ts`, and shell env helpers in `packages/shared/src/shell.ts`. If this contract drifts, the visible failures are remote Codex sessions that never start, host-scoped overrides that appear saved but are ignored at runtime, ghost `session/closed` events during teardown, or Codex turns started with the wrong collaboration-mode payload.

#### `Lines 11, 24-27, 157-159, 429-443, 559-619, 1642-1868`

This file remains part of the Codex git text-generation component.

#### `Lines 259-265`

#### Whole file
The authoritative variable is now `input.systemPrompt` at the `buildCommitMessagePrompt(...)` call site. The old contract it replaced was effectively "the shared `generateCommitMessage(...)` input carries `systemPrompt`, but the Codex implementation ignores it." The fallback path still lives in `buildCommitMessagePrompt(...)`: blank or missing system prompts are trimmed away and produce no extra instruction block. This line depends on `systemPrompt?: string | null` in `apps/server/src/git/Services/TextGeneration.ts`, settings-to-systemPrompt mapping in `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts`, prompt assembly in `apps/server/src/git/Prompts.ts`, and provider dispatch in `apps/server/src/git/Layers/RoutingTextGeneration.ts`. If this one line is removed or changed, the immediate regression is that Codex commit-message generation stops honoring the configured commit prompt even though the UI and service contract still imply that it should.

### `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitCore.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 48-50, 499-863, 865-1552, 1841-2079`
This block is the merged result of the remote-SSH series plus the later `Flatten Git service layer and switch server paths to base dir (#1255)` refactor. The old contract was "call the separate `GitService.execute(...)` layer with a local `cwd` and let everything else assume one local repo." The authoritative execution contract is now `ExecuteGitWithRemoteInput = ExecuteGitInput & { remote?: GitExecutionContext["remote"] }`, with `execute: GitCoreShape["execute"] = (input) => executeWithRemote(input)`. `executeWithRemote(...)` normalizes `input.env` into `normalizedEnv`, then either runs `runProcess("ssh", buildSshExecArgs({ hostAlias: remote.hostAlias, command: "git", args: commandInput.args, cwd: commandInput.cwd, env: normalizedEnv, localCwd: process.cwd() }))` when `remote?.kind === "ssh"` or spawns local `ChildProcess.make("git", commandInput.args, { cwd, env })` otherwise. `StatusUpstreamRefreshCacheKey` gained `remoteHostAlias`, so `refreshStatusUpstreamIfStale(...)` and `fetchUpstreamRefForStatus(...)` no longer share one cache bucket across local repos and SSH hosts that happen to use the same `cwd` string. The same `remote` value is now threaded through `branchExists`, `resolveAvailableBranchName`, `resolveCurrentUpstream`, `fetchUpstreamRef`, `resolveDefaultBranchName`, `remoteBranchExists`, `originRemoteExists`, `resolvePushRemoteName`, `resolveBaseBranchForNoUpstream`, `computeAheadCountAgainstBase`, `statusDetails`, `status`, `prepareCommitContext`, `commit`, `pushCurrentBranch`, `pullCurrentBranch`, `readRangeContext`, `readConfigValue`, `fetchPullRequestBranch`, `fetchRemoteBranch`, `setBranchUpstream`, `removeWorktree`, `renameBranch`, `createBranch`, `checkoutBranch`, `initRepo`, and `listLocalBranchNames`. The authoritative variables for branch/upstream state are now `upstreamRef`, `remoteName`, `upstreamBranch`, `remoteHostAlias`, `publishRemoteName`, and `baseBranch`; the old local-only fallback of reading config and refs from whatever checkout happened to be on disk has been replaced by explicit remote-aware reads. The fallback paths are: local execution when `remote` is absent, `allowNonZeroExit` preserving non-zero git results for callers that intentionally probe refs/config, and `computeAheadCountAgainstBase(...)` using `branch.<name>.gh-merge-base`, remote HEAD, then `main`/`master` when no upstream is configured.

#### `Lines 43-47, 56-60, 278-496, 564-605, 1303-1348`
Added `TraceTailState`, `Trace2Monitor`, `trace2ChildKey(...)`, `Trace2Record`, and `createTrace2Monitor(...)`, and extended `ExecuteGitOptions` with `progress?: ExecuteGitProgress`. The old contract was "collect stdout/stderr buffers and return when git exits," which made pre-commit and other hooks opaque. `createTrace2Monitor(...)` now allocates a temp trace file, watches it with `fs.watch(...)`, tails appended JSON through `traceTailState`, parses each record with `decodeJsonResult(Trace2Record)`, and correlates hook lifecycle through `hookStartByChildKey`. Local git execution injects `GIT_TRACE2_EVENT` into `trace2Monitor.env`, then `collectOutput(...)` uses `lineBuffer` to emit `onStdoutLine` / `onStderrLine` only after complete lines are available, and `trace2Monitor.flush` runs before the command returns so final hook events are not dropped. `commit(...)` maps the higher-level `GitCommitOptions.progress.onOutputLine` callback into low-level `onStdoutLine` / `onStderrLine` and forwards `onHookStarted` / `onHookFinished`, so the authoritative variables for commit progress are now `progress`, `hookName`, `exitCode`, `durationMs`, `stream`, and `text`. The fallback paths are explicit: if no hook callbacks are registered, `createTrace2Monitor(...)` returns `{ env: {}, flush: Effect.void }`; if trace JSON is malformed, the line is logged at debug level and ignored; and the SSH execution branch still returns buffered stdout/stderr but does not currently parse remote trace2 hook events because remote commands are executed through `runProcess(...)`.

#### `Lines 1096-1231, 1554-1839, 1903-1930`
This block is the merged result of `Enable remote worktree prep for SSH projects`, `feat: added configurable base directory. (#826)`, and `feat: add multi-repo git discovery and worktree support`. In `listBranches(...)`, `branchRecencyPromise` now calls `readBranchRecency(input.cwd, input.remote)`, every branch/remote/worktree probe carries `input.remote`, and `worktreeMap` is built from `git worktree list --porcelain`. The authoritative branch metadata fields are now `branchLastCommit`, `defaultBranch`, and `worktreePath`; the old contract it replaced was local-only branch listing that could only trust `fileSystem.stat(candidatePath)` against the local disk. For SSH repos, `candidatePath` now skips `fileSystem.stat(...)` and is treated as existing because the local machine cannot stat a remote worktree path. `createWorktree(...)` no longer derives every path from one home-dir rule; the authoritative variables are `targetBranch`, `sanitizedBranch`, `repoName`, `remoteHomeDir`, `defaultWorktreeRoot`, `worktreePath`, and `remoteTarget`. The old path contract was `path.join(homeDir, ".t3", "worktrees", repoName, sanitizedBranch)` with remote worktrees previously rejected as unavailable. The new fallback chain is: `readRemoteHomeDir({ hostAlias, localCwd }) ?? "/tmp"` for SSH projects, `ServerConfig.worktreesDir` for local projects, `nodePath.posix.isAbsolute(...)` / `nodePath.posix.join(...)` for remote `input.path`, local `path.isAbsolute(...)` / `path.join(...)` for local `input.path`, and `mkdir -p ${quotePosixShell(parentDirectory)}` over SSH before `git worktree add`. `removeWorktree(...)` now passes `input.remote` through instead of failing fast for remote projects.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 48-50, 499-863, 865-1552, 1841-2079`
Changed GitCore to execute every low-level git primitive against the resolved `(cwd, remote)` pair instead of a single implicit local checkout so `Remote SSH Support` can run status, fetch, checkout, commit, push, pull, PR materialization, and config reads directly on an SSH-backed repository, and so `Multi-Repo Support` can keep each action bound to the exact repo selected by `repoPath` instead of collapsing sibling repos into one project-wide git context. This is part of the git execution and repo-routing component. Concretely, `remoteHostAlias` differentiates identical repo-relative paths on different hosts, `statusDetails(cwd, remote)` computes ahead/behind data against the selected repo's refs, and `pushCurrentBranch(...)` / `pullCurrentBranch(...)` / `readRangeContext(...)` stop accidentally mixing local state with SSH project state.

#### `Lines 43-47, 56-60, 278-496, 564-605, 1303-1348`
Changed local git execution to stream hook lifecycle and hook output line-by-line through `ExecuteGitProgress` so `Debugability and Stability` can surface long-running commit hooks during stacked git actions instead of looking hung or only failing at the end with a giant buffered stderr block. This is part of the git action progress telemetry component. Concretely, `hookStartByChildKey` preserves the active hook identity across trace2 `child_start` / `child_exit` records, `durationMs` is derived from `startedAtMs`, and `commit(...)` now translates raw git stdout/stderr into `{ stream, text }` progress events that can be rendered incrementally.

#### `Lines 1096-1231, 1554-1839, 1903-1930`
Changed branch/worktree discovery and worktree placement so `Multi-Repo Support` can keep worktrees namespaced under the correct repo root and selected synthetic parent path, and so `Remote SSH Support` can create, list, and remove worktrees using remote POSIX paths instead of local filesystem assumptions. This is part of the worktree placement and branch projection component. Concretely, `input.path` can now be relative to a repo-specific `defaultWorktreeRoot`, `nodePath.posix` prevents local path separators from corrupting remote paths, and the `worktreePath` attached to each listed branch stays stable even when the worktree only exists on the remote host.
- Dependency impact:
#### `Lines 48-50, 499-863, 865-1552, 1841-2079`
The authoritative caller inputs are now `repoPath` at the RPC layer and `cwd` + `remote` inside `GitCore`; the old contract they replaced was local-only `cwd` plus the separate `GitService` execution abstraction. This depends on `packages/contracts/src/git.ts` carrying `repoPath` on every git RPC; `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` `resolveGitOperationTarget(...)` mapping `{ projectId, repoPath }` into `{ cwd, remote }`; `apps/server/src/git/Services/GitCore.ts` exposing `GitExecutionContext`, `GitStatusExecutionInput`, `GitListBranchesExecutionInput`, and `GitCreateWorktreeExecutionInput`; `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts` forwarding `input.remote` into `gitCore.statusDetails(...)`, `gitCore.pushCurrentBranch(...)`, `gitCore.pullCurrentBranch(...)`, `gitCore.readRangeContext(...)`, `gitCore.readConfigValue(...)`, `gitCore.fetchPullRequestBranch(...)`, and `gitCore.checkoutBranch(...)`; and `apps/server/src/sshCommand.ts` `buildSshExecArgs(...)` constructing the SSH command line. If this contract is wrong, the breakage shows up as git actions running in the wrong repo, SSH projects accidentally invoking local git, ahead/behind caches bleeding across hosts, PR resolution reading the wrong `remote.origin.url`, and stacked actions pushing or checking out the wrong branch. Retest repo-scoped status, no-upstream branch status, push/pull, checkout, PR resolution, and detached-HEAD flows for both local and SSH projects.

#### `Lines 43-47, 56-60, 278-496, 564-605, 1303-1348`
This block depends on `apps/server/src/git/Services/GitCore.ts` exposing `ExecuteGitProgress`, `GitCommitProgress`, and `GitCommitOptions.progress`; `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts` building and publishing action progress during `runStackedAction(...)`; `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` forwarding those payloads on `WS_CHANNELS.gitActionProgress`; `packages/contracts/src/git.ts` defining `GitActionProgressKind` values like `hook_started`, `hook_output`, and `hook_finished`; and the web consumers in `apps/web/src/wsNativeApi.ts`, `apps/web/src/lib/gitReactQuery.ts`, and `apps/web/src/components/GitActionsControl.tsx`. If this block is wrong, the user-visible failures are stacked actions appearing frozen, missing or duplicated hook names, hook output arriving after completion, or action failures with no incremental context. Retest commit-only and commit/push/PR actions with pre-commit hooks, stdout-heavy hooks, stderr-heavy hooks, and repos with no hooks.

#### `Lines 1096-1231, 1554-1839, 1903-1930`
This block depends on `ServerConfig.worktreesDir`; `apps/server/src/sshCommand.ts` `readRemoteHomeDir(...)`, `quotePosixShell(...)`, and `buildSshExecArgs(...)`; `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` `ensureSyntheticParentExtras(...)`, `resolveProjectRepoRelativePath(...)`, and `gitCreateWorktree` / `gitRemoveWorktree` handlers; `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts` using `gitCore.createWorktree(...)` during PR-thread preparation; `packages/contracts/src/git.ts` `GitCreateWorktreeInput.path` plus `GitBranch.worktreePath`; and multi-repo discovery/projection files such as `apps/server/src/git/projectRepos.ts` that define the repo-relative paths the UI selects. If this is wrong, the failures are duplicate worktree directories across sibling repos, SSH worktrees created under the wrong base dir, missing `worktreePath` badges in branch lists, PR-thread worktree preparation targeting the wrong repo, or remote worktree removal operating on the wrong path. ### `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitHubCli.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 4-5, 180-207, 226-227, 252-253, 270-271, 284-301, 306-307, 318-319`
This block is the merged result of `feat(remote): enable git, diff, terminal, and workspace flows over SSH` plus the follow-on settings work. The old execution contract was "always run local `gh` in `input.cwd` and rely on a local temp file for PR bodies." The authoritative execution target is now `input.remote`, with `execute(...)` branching to `runProcess("ssh", buildSshExecArgs({ hostAlias: input.remote.hostAlias, command: executable, args: input.args, cwd: input.cwd, localCwd: process.cwd() }))` whenever `input.remote?.kind === "ssh"`. That `remote` field is now threaded through `listOpenPullRequests`, `getPullRequest`, `getRepositoryCloneUrls`, `createPullRequest`, `getDefaultBranch`, and `checkoutPullRequest`, so every GitHub CLI call stays bound to the same remote repo context that `GitCore` uses. `createPullRequest(...)` also replaced the old `--body-file input.bodyFile` contract with `--body input.body`; the authoritative variable is now the inline `body` string, because a local temp-file path is meaningless once the command runs on a remote host. The fallback paths are: local `runProcess(executable, input.args, { cwd: input.cwd })` when `input.remote` is absent, the existing schema-decoding path for CLI JSON responses, and the inherited GitHub CLI auth / PR-not-found error normalization when the command itself succeeds but returns a domain error.

#### `Lines 15-36, 183-206, 226, 252, 270, 299, 306, 318`
Added `DEFAULT_GITHUB_CLI_BIN = "gh"`, `GITHUB_CLI_BIN_ENV = "T3_GH_BIN"`, and `resolveGitHubCliBin(override?: string | null)`. The old contract was "GitHub CLI must be available as `gh` on PATH." The authoritative binary-selection chain is now `input.executablePath?.trim()` first, then `process.env.T3_GH_BIN`, then the default `"gh"`. `normalizeGitHubCliError(...)` now receives the resolved `executable` name so the missing-binary error reports the actual path or alias that failed, not a hard-coded `gh`. That same `executablePath` is threaded into every operation method, so the chosen binary is stable across `pr list`, `pr view`, `repo view`, `pr create`, `defaultBranch` lookup, and `pr checkout`. The fallback path is explicit: if neither `input.executablePath` nor `T3_GH_BIN` is set, the layer still executes plain `gh`.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 4-5, 180-207, 226-227, 252-253, 270-271, 284-301, 306-307, 318-319`
Changed GitHub CLI command dispatch to run against the resolved remote repository and to send PR bodies inline so `Remote SSH Support` can list PRs, resolve PR metadata, inspect repository clone URLs, create PRs, read default branches, and checkout PR branches without relying on local filesystem state. This is part of the GitHub integration execution component. Concretely, `buildSshExecArgs(...)` keeps the remote `cwd` authoritative, and `--body input.body` avoids the old local-only temp-file assumption that would break remote PR creation.

#### `Lines 15-36, 183-206, 226, 252, 270, 299, 306, 318`
Changed GitHub CLI process resolution so `Extra Customization` can honor a per-request or environment-level GitHub CLI override without changing the rest of the git workflow contract. This is part of the GitHub CLI settings component. Concretely, `resolveGitHubCliBin(...)` lets the fork point GitHub operations at a non-default binary path while preserving the same remote/local execution logic and the same JSON response parsing.

If this contract is wrong, the failures are remote PR lookups querying the local machine instead of the remote repo, PR creation failing because the body file exists only locally, `gh repo view` returning metadata for the wrong checkout, or PR checkout mutating the wrong repository. ### `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 429-548, 574-776, 1094-1235`
This block is the merged result of the PR-thread/fork-PR series (`Fix cross-repo PR detection and push remote selection (#788)`, `Preserve fork PR upstreams when preparing local and worktree threads`, `Add pull-request thread setup for local and worktree modes`) plus the later remote-SSH follow-ups. The authoritative PR-head mapping variables are now `localBranch`, `remoteName`, `headRepositoryNameWithOwner`, `headRepositoryOwnerLogin`, `isCrossRepository`, `headSelectors`, and `preferredHeadSelector`. The old contract was "treat the checked-out branch name as the only PR head selector, assume `origin`, and attach upstream to `pullRequest.headBranch` directly." `resolveLocalBranchName(...)` now makes `localBranch` explicit, `configurePullRequestHeadUpstream(...)` and `materializePullRequestHeadBranch(...)` take object inputs with `localBranch?`, `remote?`, and `settings?`, and `resolveBranchHeadContext(...)` builds a selector chain from `branch.<branch>.remote`, `remote.<name>.url`, owner login, and upstream ref parsing. `findOpenPr(...)` / `findLatestPr(...)` now probe `owner:branch`, `remoteAlias:branch`, `details.branch`, and upstream-derived `headBranch` instead of querying just one branch string. `resolveBaseBranch(...)` changed from a mostly local-only branch heuristic to the fallback chain `branch.<branch>.gh-merge-base` -> upstream branch when not cross-repo -> `gh repo view` default branch -> `"main"`. `preparePullRequestThread(...)` now reuses existing worktrees when `result.branches[*].worktreePath` already points at the PR branch, compares `canonicalizeExistingPath(...)` against `rootWorktreePath` to avoid duplicating the main checkout, and after `0b6e734c` no longer fails fast with `"PR worktree preparation is unavailable for remote projects."` The fallback paths are important here: if clone-url-based fork materialization fails, `materializePullRequestHeadBranch(...)` falls back to `gitCore.fetchPullRequestBranch(...)`; if `repositoryNameWithOwner` cannot be derived, the manager fetches by PR number directly; and if an existing secondary worktree already owns the branch, it is reused rather than creating a new one.

#### `Lines 28-34, 316-338, 443-447, 502-506, 648-768, 778-825, 1002-1023, 1079-1124, 1199-1204, 1245-1264, 1337-1404`
Added the `GitOperationSettings` bundle with `githubBinaryPath`, `commitPrompt`, and `textGenerationModelSelection?`, plus the helper mappers `toGitHubCliInputOptions(settings)`, `toTextGenerationOptions(settings)`, and `toCommitGenerationOptions(settings)`. The authoritative customization variables are now `settings.githubBinaryPath`, `settings.commitPrompt`, the explicit `modelSelection` argument, and optional `filePaths`; the old contract was "always use the default `gh` binary, default prompt, and full staged diff." `resolveCommitAndBranchSuggestion(...)` now takes `remote?`, `filePaths?`, and `settings?`, passes the staged subset through `gitCore.prepareCommitContext(input.cwd, input.filePaths, input.remote)`, and forwards `systemPrompt` into `textGeneration.generateCommitMessage(...)`. `runPrStep(...)` likewise forwards `systemPrompt` into `generatePrContent(...)` and replaced the old temp-file PR-body flow with `gitHubCli.createPullRequest({ ..., body: generated.body, ...toGitHubCliInputOptions(settings) })`. The authoritative provider selection in this file is still the explicit `modelSelection` parameter threaded through `resolveCommitAndBranchSuggestion(...)`, `runFeatureBranchStep(...)`, `runCommitStep(...)`, and `runPrStep(...)`; `settings.textGenerationModelSelection` is typed through the settings bundle, but it is resolved by the caller before the request reaches this layer. The fallback paths are: blank `githubBinaryPath` / `commitPrompt` collapse to `null`, `parseCustomCommitMessage(input.commitMessage ?? "")` bypasses generation entirely when the user entered a manual commit message, missing `filePaths` means GitCore stages the whole working tree, and `resolveBaseBranch(...)` still falls back to `"main"` when neither git config nor GitHub metadata yields a better base.

#### `Lines 36-39, 227-235, 406-427, 828-945, 1296-1433`
Added `COMMIT_TIMEOUT_MS`, `MAX_PROGRESS_TEXT_LENGTH`, `GitActionProgressPayload`, `sanitizeProgressText(...)`, and `createProgressEmitter(...)`, and expanded `runCommitStep(...)` / `runStackedAction(...)` to accept `GitRunStackedActionOptions`. The old contract was "run the stacked action and return one final result object," which made long-running commits and hook failures look opaque. `createProgressEmitter(...)` now generates the authoritative `actionId` from `options?.actionId ?? randomUUID()`, binds every emitted payload to `{ actionId, cwd, action }`, and no-ops when no `progressReporter` is attached. `runCommitStep(...)` now emits `phase_started` for both "Generating commit message..." and "Committing...", forwards `gitCore.commit(...)` hook callbacks as `hook_started`, `hook_output`, and `hook_finished`, truncates long output through `sanitizeProgressText(...)`, and applies `timeoutMs: COMMIT_TIMEOUT_MS`. `runStackedAction(...)` computes the `phases` array from `featureBranch` and `action`, emits `action_started`, `phase_started`, `action_finished`, and on failure `action_failed` with the current `phase` and `error.message`. The fallback paths are explicit: if no `progressReporter` exists the emitter is inert, lines longer than `MAX_PROGRESS_TEXT_LENGTH` are trimmed instead of flooding the UI, and if `currentHookName` is still set after a successful commit the manager emits a synthetic final `hook_finished` with `exitCode: 0` and `durationMs: null` so the UI does not remain stuck on an open hook.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 429-548, 574-776, 1094-1235`
Changed pull-request branch discovery, upstream wiring, and PR-thread preparation so `Multi-Repo Support` and `Remote SSH Support` can materialize the right PR head inside the exact selected repo, preserve fork identity, and reuse existing secondary worktrees instead of treating every PR as an `origin/<branch>` case on one local checkout. This is part of the pull-request branch materialization and thread-worktree mapping component. Concretely, `headSelectors` now probe owner-qualified and remote-qualified branch selectors, while `resolvePullRequestWorktreeLocalBranchName(...)` and `resolveLocalBranchName(...)` keep cross-repo PR branches stable when the user moves between local mode and worktree mode.

#### `Lines 28-34, 316-338, 443-447, 502-506, 648-768, 778-825, 1002-1023, 1079-1124, 1199-1204, 1245-1264, 1337-1404`
Changed GitManager to honor per-request git settings and selected-file commit context so `Extra Customization` can override the commit-generation system prompt, point PR flows at a custom GitHub CLI binary, and generate commit or PR text from exactly the chosen staged files while keeping explicit `modelSelection` as the authoritative provider/model choice. This is part of the git request settings and AI text-generation configuration component. Concretely, `toGitHubCliInputOptions(...)` controls the `gh` executable, `toTextGenerationOptions(...)` controls the git-writing prompt contract, and `filePaths` now narrows both commit generation and feature-branch naming to the selected changes.

#### `Lines 36-39, 227-235, 406-427, 828-945, 1296-1433`
Changed stacked git orchestration to stream stable phase and hook progress with per-action identity so `Debugability and Stability` can show exactly where a commit/push/PR action is running or failing, including pre-commit hook output and concurrent action separation. This is part of the stacked git action telemetry component. Concretely, `currentPhase` lets failure events identify whether the action died in branch preparation, commit, push, or PR creation, and `actionId` keeps overlapping git actions from overwriting each other's progress in the client.

#### `Lines 36-39, 227-235, 406-427, 828-945, 1296-1433`
