### `apps/server/src/git/Layers/RoutingTextGeneration.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 14-16, 22-68`
Added a dedicated routing layer that introduces the internal service tags `CodexTextGen` and `ClaudeTextGen` so both concrete `TextGenerationShape` implementations can coexist in the layer graph at the same time. The authoritative dispatch field is now `input.modelSelection.provider`: `generateCommitMessage(...)`, `generatePrContent(...)`, and `generateBranchName(...)` all call `route(input.modelSelection.provider)` before delegating to the concrete implementation. The old contract it replaced was effectively "there is one ambient `TextGeneration` service for all git-writing flows," which could not support multiple providers in the same server. The later `eff6a100` follow-up deliberately widened `route(provider?: string)` from `TextGenerationProvider` to `string`, so this layer keeps working even when the shared `ModelSelection.provider` schema is centralized or expanded elsewhere. The fallback path is explicit: any provider other than `"claudeAgent"` falls through to the Codex implementation.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 14-16, 22-68`
Implemented provider-based git text-generation routing so `Extra Customization` can switch commit-message, PR-content, and branch-name generation between Codex and Claude on a per-request basis without changing the higher-level git workflow contract. This is part of the git text-generation provider selection component. Concretely, the router treats `modelSelection.provider` as the only authoritative selector and keeps the rest of the generation inputs untouched.
- Dependency impact:
#### `Lines 14-16, 22-68`
This block depends on `apps/server/src/git/Services/TextGeneration.ts` carrying `modelSelection: ModelSelection` on every generation input; `apps/server/src/git/Layers/CodexTextGeneration.ts` and `apps/server/src/git/Layers/ClaudeTextGeneration.ts` both satisfying the same `TextGenerationShape`; `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts` passing explicit `modelSelection` into commit/PR/branch generation; and the client-side selection path in `apps/web/src/components/GitActionsControl.tsx` / `apps/web/src/appSettings.ts` that resolves the chosen git-writing model. If this contract is wrong, git-writing requests will always hit the wrong provider, new provider enum values may crash routing instead of falling back, or only one provider layer will remain reachable. Retest commit message generation, PR content generation, and feature-branch naming with both Codex and Claude selections, plus fallback behavior for unexpected provider values.

### `apps/server/src/git/Prompts.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 18-24, 26-52`
The live fork delta in this file is the `4add5fbe` follow-up on top of the earlier shared prompt-builder extraction from `aa8e627c`. `CommitMessagePromptInput` now carries `systemPrompt?: string | null | undefined` as an additional authoritative input field beside the existing `branch`, `stagedSummary`, `stagedPatch`, and `includeBranch` fields. In `buildCommitMessagePrompt(...)`, the prompt array now conditionally injects `["", "Additional user instructions:", input.systemPrompt.trim()]` immediately after the fixed rule `"- capture the primary user-visible or developer-visible change"`. The old upstream contract was that commit-message generation was driven only by the fixed prompt rules plus branch, staged file summary, and staged patch. The new contract extends that prompt with a trimmed user-supplied instruction block while leaving the JSON output schema unchanged: `includeBranch` still controls whether the returned `outputSchema` contains `branch`, and `limitSection(input.stagedSummary, 6_000)` / `limitSection(input.stagedPatch, 40_000)` still bound the staged context exactly as before. The fallback path is explicit in the prompt builder: if `input.systemPrompt` is `null`, `undefined`, empty, or whitespace-only, no additional section is added and upstream behavior is preserved byte-for-byte for the rest of the prompt.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 18-24, 26-52`
Changed commit-message prompt construction to support `Extra Customization` by extending the shared git text-generation contract with a dedicated `systemPrompt` field that appends user commit instructions directly into the generated commit-message prompt. Concretely, this lets fork-specific commit guidance from settings shape the generated `subject` and `body` without changing the provider-facing JSON schema or the staged diff context window. This is part of the git prompt-building component that sits between git action settings and the provider-specific Codex or Claude text-generation backends.
- Dependency impact:
#### `Lines 18-24, 26-52`
This prompt contract is part of the git text-generation pipeline rooted in `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts`, where `settings.commitPrompt` is trimmed and normalized into the authoritative `systemPrompt` value inside `toCommitGenerationOptions(...)`. That field then flows through `apps/server/src/git/Services/TextGeneration.ts` into both `apps/server/src/git/Layers/CodexTextGeneration.ts` and `apps/server/src/git/Layers/ClaudeTextGeneration.ts`, each of which now forwards `input.systemPrompt` into `buildCommitMessagePrompt(...)`. The old contract it extends is the shared prompt-builder surface introduced with the Claude provider series in `aa8e627c`; the new fork-only dependency chain is therefore `GitManager settings.commitPrompt -> TextGeneration CommitMessageInput.systemPrompt -> Prompts.buildCommitMessagePrompt(...) -> provider JSON parse result`. If this file drifts, the main failure modes are: custom commit instructions silently stop affecting generated commit messages; user instructions are appended in the wrong position and overpower or conflict with the fixed rules; blank prompts stop falling back cleanly; or the commit-message path diverges between Codex and Claude. Retest generated commit messages with and without a custom commit prompt, with `includeBranch` both true and false, and through both provider backends so the shared prompt surface remains aligned.

### `apps/server/src/git/Services/GitCore.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 49-52, 54-94, 125-182, 197-199, 204-215, 231-243, 249-253, 265-341`
The remote-execution change set comes from the `0ae86206` SSH series and threads `ProjectRemoteTarget` through the low-level git service contract. The authoritative remote variable is now `remote?: ProjectRemoteTarget | null`, introduced first in `GitExecutionContext` and then added to every git primitive that may run against an SSH-backed repository: `GitCommitOptions.remote`, `GitRenameBranchInput.remote`, `GitFetchPullRequestBranchInput.remote`, `GitEnsureRemoteInput.remote`, `GitFetchRemoteBranchInput.remote`, `GitSetBranchUpstreamInput.remote`, `statusDetails(cwd, remote?)`, `prepareCommitContext(cwd, filePaths?, remote?)`, `pushCurrentBranch(cwd, fallbackBranch, remote?)`, `readRangeContext(cwd, baseBranch, remote?)`, `readConfigValue(cwd, key, remote?)`, `pullCurrentBranch(cwd, remote?)`, and `listLocalBranchNames(cwd, remote?)`. The execution-input wrappers `GitStatusExecutionInput`, `GitListBranchesExecutionInput`, `GitCreateWorktreeExecutionInput`, `GitRemoveWorktreeExecutionInput`, `GitCreateBranchExecutionInput`, `GitCheckoutExecutionInput`, and `GitInitExecutionInput` also gained the same `remote` field so branch, worktree, checkout, and init operations can be routed over SSH instead of assuming a local filesystem process. The old contract was local-only: these service methods either accepted only `cwd` or input objects with no remote identity at all, and `GitCommitOptions` only carried `timeoutMs` plus `progress`. The fallback path remains explicit everywhere in the interface: when `remote` is omitted or `null`, the layer implementation should keep using the local process execution path for the provided `cwd`.

#### `Lines 54-94, 197-199, 258-275, 306-334`
The later `b200dc0b` multi-repo routing pass changed the service-layer execution inputs so they no longer inherit `repoPath` directly from the transport schemas in `packages/contracts/src/git.ts`. The authoritative service inputs are now `GitStatusExecutionInput`, `GitListBranchesExecutionInput`, `GitCreateWorktreeExecutionInput`, `GitRemoveWorktreeExecutionInput`, `GitCreateBranchExecutionInput`, `GitCheckoutExecutionInput`, and `GitInitExecutionInput`, each defined as `Omit<...Input, "repoPath">` and then rebuilt with `cwd: string`, `repoPath?: string`, and `remote?: ProjectRemoteTarget | null`. The old contract that this replaces was the direct reuse of transport-level input types like `GitStatusInput`, `GitListBranchesInput`, `GitCreateWorktreeInput`, `GitCheckoutInput`, and `GitInitInput`, where `repoPath` was a required string and implicitly carried both repository identity and execution location. The new service contract separates those concerns: `cwd` is now the authoritative process working directory, while `repoPath` is an optional logical repo selector for multi-repo projects. The fallback path is the single-repo case: when `repoPath` is absent, callers rely on `cwd` alone and the service behaves like the old one-repository flow.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 49-52, 54-94, 125-182, 197-199, 204-215, 231-243, 249-253, 265-341`
Changed the low-level git service contract to support `Remote SSH Support` by making remote host and project identity a first-class input on every primitive used for status, staged diff capture, commit execution, push/pull, PR head fetch, upstream wiring, branch creation, checkout, worktree lifecycle, and branch listing. In practical terms, this is the contract that lets the fork reuse the same git orchestration APIs for both local workspaces and SSH-backed workspaces without forking the higher-level git manager flow.

#### `Lines 54-94, 197-199, 258-275, 306-334`
Changed the git service execution boundary to support `Multi-Repo Support` by decoupling the selected repository path coming from the WebSocket/native API layer from the concrete working directory used to launch git. This lets the fork preserve absolute per-repo paths in multi-repo projects while still exposing a stable server-side execution contract for status, branch, checkout, init, and worktree operations.
- Dependency impact:
#### `Lines 49-52, 54-94, 125-182, 197-199, 204-215, 231-243, 249-253, 265-341`
This remote contract is consumed directly by [`apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitCore.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitCore.ts), which uses the shared `GitExecutionContext["remote"]` shape to choose local `git` subprocesses versus SSH command execution. Up the stack, it feeds [`apps/server/src/git/Services/GitManager.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Services/GitManager.ts), [`apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts), [`apps/server/src/git/projectRepos.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/projectRepos.ts), and [`apps/server/src/wsServer.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/wsServer.ts), which all need a stable `remote` field name to keep remote git actions aligned with project identity. If this contract is wrong, remote git actions silently fall back to the local machine, run against the wrong host, or fail to find the selected repository. Retest SSH-backed status refresh, branch listing, commit generation context, commit/push/pull, PR branch materialization, remote upstream wiring, checkout, and worktree creation or removal.

#### `Lines 54-94, 197-199, 258-275, 306-334`

On the user-facing side, this contract feeds the repo-selector-driven flows in the branch toolbar, diff panel, git actions control, PR dialog, sidebar, and git React Query clients. If this file drifts, the common breakage is that multi-repo actions execute in the wrong repository, absolute repo paths get collapsed back to project roots, or single-repo callers break because `repoPath` stops being optional at the service layer. ### `apps/server/src/git/Services/GitHubCli.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 10, 40-46, 51-57, 62-77, 82-99, 104-110`
The `0ae86206` remote-execution series widened the `GitHubCliShape` request contract so every `gh` operation can carry `remote?: ProjectRemoteTarget | null`. That field was added to `execute`, `listOpenPullRequests`, `getPullRequest`, `getRepositoryCloneUrls`, `createPullRequest`, `getDefaultBranch`, and `checkoutPullRequest`, with the new import at line 10 making `ProjectRemoteTarget` part of the service surface. The same change set also replaced `createPullRequest`'s old `bodyFile: string` contract with the authoritative inline payload `body: string`. The old service contract assumed all `gh` work happened on the local machine and that PR creation could point the CLI at a local temporary file path. The new contract treats the PR body itself as the transport value and treats `remote` as the selector for where `gh` should execute. The fallback path is still local execution: if `remote` is absent, callers keep using the local repository checkout, and the inline `body` text is passed directly without any remote file-materialization step.

#### `Lines 44, 55, 65, 75, 88, 97, 108`
The `be9f7119` settings pass added `executablePath?: string | null` to every `GitHubCliShape` request variant: `execute`, `listOpenPullRequests`, `getPullRequest`, `getRepositoryCloneUrls`, `createPullRequest`, `getDefaultBranch`, and `checkoutPullRequest`. The old contract hard-coded binary selection inside the implementation layer; there was no service-level field for per-request binary override. The new authoritative variable is `input.executablePath`, which gives the caller a stable way to select a non-default `gh` binary without changing command arguments. The fallback path is explicit in the optional type: when `executablePath` is `null`, `undefined`, or blank after higher-level normalization, the implementation falls back to its default CLI resolution chain.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 10, 40-46, 51-57, 62-77, 82-99, 104-110`
Changed the GitHub CLI service interface to support `Remote SSH Support` by making remote project identity explicit on every `gh` operation and by replacing file-path-based PR body transport with inline markdown text that can be forwarded safely to an SSH-hosted `gh pr create` invocation. This is part of the GitHub CLI execution contract that lets PR discovery, clone URL lookup, default-branch lookup, checkout, and PR creation work against remote repositories instead of assuming a local filesystem-only flow.

#### `Lines 44, 55, 65, 75, 88, 97, 108`
Changed the GitHub CLI service interface to support `Extra Customization` by exposing a per-request `executablePath` override for git actions. This is the contract layer that lets fork settings choose a custom GitHub CLI binary for PR and repository operations without cloning the entire GitHub CLI service implementation.
- Dependency impact:

Upstream callers in [`apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts) must keep forwarding `input.remote` and the generated PR markdown body consistently into this service, especially for PR list, PR lookup, clone URL resolution, PR creation, default-branch resolution, and PR checkout. If this contract drifts, the common failures are remote `gh` commands running locally, PR creation failing because the code still tries to hand the service a file path, or remote PR flows losing access to the selected SSH target. #### `Lines 44, 55, 65, 75, 88, 97, 108`

### `apps/server/src/git/Services/GitManager.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 19, 25-35, 41-57, 71-95`

Instead, it now defines `GitStatusExecutionInput`, `GitPullRequestRefExecutionInput`, `GitPreparePullRequestThreadExecutionInput`, and `GitRunStackedActionExecutionInput`, each built as `Omit<...Input, "repoPath">` plus `cwd: string`, `repoPath?: string`, and `remote?: ProjectRemoteTarget | null`. The old contract was the direct use of `GitStatusInput`, `GitPullRequestRefInput`, `GitPreparePullRequestThreadInput`, and `GitRunStackedActionInput`, where `repoPath` remained a required transport field and there was no remote project identity in the service surface. The new authoritative execution variables are `cwd` for the actual working directory, `repoPath?` for the selected repository within a multi-repo project, and `remote?` for the SSH target. The fallback path is the local single-repo flow: when `repoPath` and `remote` are both omitted, callers effectively get the old one-repository local execution behavior.

#### `Lines 10, 37-39, 59-61, 93-95`
The `242fe064` stacked-action telemetry change set imported `GitActionProgressEvent`, added the `GitActionProgressReporter` interface with `publish(event: GitActionProgressEvent)`, added `GitRunStackedActionOptions` with `actionId?: string` and `progressReporter?: GitActionProgressReporter`, and widened `runStackedAction` from `runStackedAction(input)` to `runStackedAction(input, options?)`. The old service contract had no stable action identifier and no structured way for callers to observe hook, stdout, stderr, or phase progress while a stacked action was running. The new authoritative progress variables are `options.actionId` and `options.progressReporter`, and the fallback path is still supported because `options` remains optional: callers that do not care about streamed progress can invoke the method exactly as before.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 19, 25-35, 41-57, 71-95`
Changed the GitManager service boundary to support both `Multi-Repo Support` and `Remote SSH Support` by separating transport-level repo selection from server-side execution context while still exposing one orchestration API for status reads, pull-request resolution, pull-request-thread materialization, and stacked commit or PR actions. Concretely, this is what lets a selected repository inside a multi-repo project be executed from its resolved absolute `cwd`, and lets the same operation be forwarded to an SSH-backed project without forking the service shape.

#### `Lines 10, 37-39, 59-61, 93-95`
Changed stacked git orchestration to support `Debugability and Stability` by giving the service layer a first-class progress publishing contract for long-running `commit`, `commit_push`, and `commit_push_pr` workflows. In practice, this is the interface that lets the fork attach a stable action ID to a run and stream deterministic lifecycle or hook events instead of treating stacked actions as opaque background work.

If this file drifts, status requests, PR resolution, imported PR threads, and stacked actions can all target the wrong repository or the wrong machine because `cwd`, `repoPath`, and `remote` stop meaning the same thing across the service chain. Retest selected-repo status, PR lookup, PR-thread creation, commit/push/PR actions, and the local single-repo fallback path.

### `apps/server/src/git/Services/TextGeneration.ts`

- Status: `Modified`

#### `Lines 24, 46, 61`

One important implementation detail is that the contract is wider than the current prompt usage: [`apps/server/src/git/Prompts.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Prompts.ts) currently injects `systemPrompt` only into `buildCommitMessagePrompt(...)`, while PR and branch prompt builders do not yet consume their `systemPrompt` fields. The fallback path is therefore twofold: `null` or blank values behave like upstream everywhere, and even non-empty `systemPrompt` currently has an effect only on commit-message generation.

#### `Lines 11, 20, 40, 58`

#### `Lines 24, 46, 61`

#### `Lines 11, 20, 40, 58`
This field is threaded primarily by [`apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts), which passes the selected project remote alongside prepared commit or diff context. The provider implementations do not currently branch much on `input.remote` directly, so this field is mostly a contract-alignment requirement between git orchestration and future or remote-aware provider execution. If it drifts, SSH-backed git actions lose the project host context at the text-generation boundary and later remote-provider work has no stable field to hook into. Retest SSH-backed commit, PR, and branch-generation flows from the GitManager entrypoints, even if the immediate prompt generation logic remains host-agnostic.

#### `Lines 24, 46, 61`
This field is produced in [`apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts) from git settings, forwarded by [`apps/server/src/git/Layers/CodexTextGeneration.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Layers/CodexTextGeneration.ts) and [`apps/server/src/git/Layers/ClaudeTextGeneration.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/git/Layers/ClaudeTextGeneration.ts), and ultimately consumed only where the prompt builders support it. If this contract drifts, custom commit instructions are silently lost, or callers assume PR and branch generation honor a setting that the prompt builders still ignore. Retest custom prompt propagation for commit-message generation explicitly, and treat PR or branch `systemPrompt` behavior as an implementation gap to verify before depending on it.

### `apps/server/src/git/projectRepos.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 9, 22-49, 107-125, 155-225`
This file does not exist upstream, so the entire project-level git-topology discovery contract is fork-only. The initial `033511d9` introduction established three authoritative return values through `DiscoveredProjectRepos`: `gitMode: ProjectGitMode`, `gitRepos: ProjectGitRepo[] | null`, and a cache keyed by `cacheKey(workspaceRoot, remote?)`. The cache key itself encodes remote host identity as `ssh:${remote.hostAlias}` versus `"local"`, which means the same `workspaceRoot` can resolve to different cached repo topologies depending on the host. Local discovery first uses `isLocalRepoRoot(workspaceRoot)` and returns `{ gitMode: "single", gitRepos: null }` when the project root itself is the repository root. Remote discovery is built around a generated shell script that normalizes `~` paths, resolves `pwd -P`, checks `root_repo=$(git -C "$resolved_path" rev-parse --show-toplevel ...)`, and returns a NUL-delimited protocol where the first token is `"single"`, `"multi"`, or `"none"` and later tokens come in `repoPath`, `displayName` pairs. `discoverProjectRepos(...)` becomes the authoritative entrypoint and dispatches between local and SSH discovery via `input.remote?.kind === "ssh"`, while `clearProjectRepoDiscoveryCache(...)` gives callers a way to invalidate stale topology state. The old upstream contract it replaces is simply the absence of a discovery helper: there was no dedicated place to compute project-level `gitMode` / `gitRepos` from a workspace root, so project snapshots and UI flows had no canonical repo-topology source.

#### `Lines 2, 10-20, 56-104, 107, 123-151, 191-196`
The very next file-touching commit, `efd5f211`, materially changed how repo discovery works. Local discovery no longer scans only direct children of `workspaceRoot`; it now imports `fs` eagerly, introduces `MAX_DISCOVERY_DEPTH = 5`, introduces `IGNORED_DIRECTORY_NAMES` for `.git`, `node_modules`, `.next`, `.turbo`, `dist`, `build`, `out`, and `.cache`, and replaces the one-level loop with a breadth-first `pending` queue of `{ absolutePath, depth }`. Instead of returning `repoPath: child`, the authoritative local repo identity is now `path.relative(workspaceRoot, absolutePath).split(path.sep).join("/")`, and `displayName` is derived from `path.basename(repoPath)` so nested repositories preserve their relative path while still rendering a short label. The remote script was also rewritten: the old direct-child `for child_path in "$resolved_path"/*` probe is replaced with `find "$resolved_path" -mindepth 2 -maxdepth 6 -name .git`, path filtering through `grep -Eq "/(node_modules|\\.next|\\.turbo|dist|build|out|\\.cache)/"`, stable ordering via `LC_ALL=C sort -u`, and nested-path deduplication using `last_kept` so child worktrees or nested repos do not produce duplicate parent-prefixed entries. `buildRemoteDiscoveryScript(...)` also becomes an exported helper, and both local and remote discovery now sort the final `ProjectGitRepo[]` by `repoPath`. The old contract this replaces was shallow and fragile: only direct child repositories were visible, nested repo paths were flattened to the child name, and remote discovery had no bounded recursive scan or ignore list.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 9, 22-49, 107-125, 155-225`
Implemented project-level git topology discovery to support both `Multi-Repo Support` and `Remote SSH Support` by giving the fork a single cached service that can classify a workspace as `single`, `multi`, or `none` and describe discovered repositories in a transportable `{ repoPath, displayName }` shape. This is part of the project git topology component that sits underneath project snapshots, sidebar state, and selected-repo git actions.

#### `Lines 2, 10-20, 56-104, 107, 123-151, 191-196`
Changed project repo discovery to support `Multi-Repo Support` in a way that actually works for nested repositories, worktrees, and SSH-backed monorepos instead of only direct child repositories. This is the deeper discovery pass that makes selected repo paths stable enough to drive per-repo branch state, worktree state, and execution routing in larger projects.
- Dependency impact:
#### `Lines 9, 22-49, 107-125, 155-225`
This file is consumed first by [`apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts), which hydrates snapshot project state, and then by the orchestration or persistence chain that stores and projects `gitMode` and `gitRepos` through [`apps/server/src/orchestration/decider.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/orchestration/decider.ts), [`apps/server/src/orchestration/projector.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/orchestration/projector.ts), and [`apps/server/src/persistence/Layers/ProjectionProjects.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/persistence/Layers/ProjectionProjects.ts). ### `apps/server/src/kiroAcpManager.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 20-73, 523-676, 696-1008, 1125-1153, 1416-1658`
Upstream has no `kiroAcpManager.ts`, so this entire ACP bridge is fork-only. The core contract is `KiroSessionState`, which persists the authoritative Kiro runtime variables for a thread: `process`, `rpc`, `runtimeMode`, `cwd`, `model`, `sessionId`, `activeTurnId`, `modeState`, `turns`, `pendingPermissionRequests`, `suppressReplay`, `toolCallKinds`, and `toolPermissionBoundary`. `JsonRpcConnection` implements newline-delimited JSON-RPC over stdio with a numeric request-id map, traced request logging, stderr capture, and normalized close handling via `formatKiroProcessExitMessage(...)`. `startSession(...)` performs ACP `initialize`, then either `session/load` or `session/new`, populates `resumeCursor` from `{ sessionId }`, records `ProviderSession` state, and emits `session.started`, `thread.started`, and `thread.metadata.updated` runtime events. `sendTurn(...)` constructs ACP prompt blocks from optional text plus base64 image attachments, assigns `TurnId.makeUnsafe("kiro:${crypto.randomUUID()}")`, emits `turn.started`, dispatches `session/prompt`, and resolves completion through `completeTurn(...)`. `handleNotification(...)` is the translation layer from ACP `session/update` payloads into the repo’s provider runtime contract: `agent_message_chunk -> content.delta`, `plan -> turn.plan.updated`, `tool_call -> item.started`, `tool_call_update -> item.updated` or `item.completed`, `current_mode_update -> thread.metadata.updated`, and `_kiro.dev/compaction/status -> thread.state.changed` or `session.state.changed`. The old contract it replaces is the complete absence of a Kiro provider runtime implementation.

#### `Lines 16-17, 678-686, 1087-1123`
The manager exposes Kiro-specific process boot options through `KiroAcpStartSessionInput.binaryPath?: string` and `remote?: ProjectRemoteTarget`, then resolves them in `spawnProcess(...)`. The authoritative startup variables are `input.binaryPath ?? DEFAULT_BINARY_PATH` and `input.remote`. For SSH-backed sessions, the manager now spawns `"ssh"` with `buildSshExecArgs({ hostAlias, command: input.binaryPath, args: ["acp"], ...(input.cwd ? { cwd: input.cwd } : {}), localCwd: process.cwd() })` and returns a paired `command` string like ``ssh <hostAlias> <binaryPath> acp`` for diagnostics. The fallback path is the local spawn branch, which runs `spawn(input.binaryPath, ["acp"], { cwd: input.cwd ?? process.cwd(), ... })`. The old contract it replaces is again “none”: there was no Kiro process launcher at all upstream.

#### `Lines 285-390, 723-729, 1011-1051, 1155-1213, 1291-1414`
The Kiro session manager does more than fire prompts; it also owns Kiro-specific mode and permission-boundary semantics. `runtimeModeFromModeDescriptor(...)`, `resolveModeIdForRuntimeMode(...)`, and `resolveModeIdForSessionState(...)` derive the ACP `modeId` from the repo’s `ProviderSession["runtimeMode"]` plus `ProviderInteractionMode`. `prepareSessionForTurn(...)` became the authoritative pre-turn hook and now calls `applyRuntimeBoundary(session)` before `setSessionMode(...)`. `applyRuntimeBoundary(...)` tracks `session.toolPermissionBoundary` and invokes `_kiro.dev/commands/execute` with `tools reset` for `"approval-required"` sessions or `tools trust-all` for `"full-access"` sessions, avoiding redundant calls once the boundary is already in the desired state. Approval handling also hardened: `PendingPermissionRequest` stores `requestType`, `handleRequest(...)` derives it from the live `toolCall.kind` or the remembered `toolCallKinds` map, and `respondToRequest(...)` now resolves using that stored request type instead of recomputing it after the fact. Finally, `interruptTurn(...)` now uses `session.rpc.notify("session/cancel", { sessionId })` instead of awaiting request-response semantics. The old upstream contract is absent, but within the file’s own history these lines replaced a simpler flow where `sendTurn(...)` set interaction mode directly, tool permission boundary was not normalized up front, request type could be lost when Kiro omitted `kind` on follow-up messages, and interrupts used request-style cancel semantics.

#### `Lines 136-143, 146-262, 277-282, 573-580, 637-641, 813-905, 925-980, 1261-1344, 1421-1448`
Several follow-up commits turned this file into the authoritative Kiro diagnostics surface. `isTracedRpcMethod(...)` marks `session/prompt`, `session/set_model`, `session/set_mode`, `session/cancel`, and `_kiro.dev/commands/execute` for structured request or response logging. `formatKiroProcessExitMessage(...)` now inspects `code`, `signal`, `stderr`, and the resolved command string so missing-binary exits can suggest setting the full `kiro-cli` path. `kiroSessionStartedMessage(...)` and `kiroThreadConnectedMessage(...)` differentiate new sessions from resumes in `session.started` and `thread.started` payloads. The manager logs thread open requests, post-open model normalization, prompt dispatch and prompt resolution, plus set-model and set-mode attempts or failures. The file also still exports `readKiroTextChunk(...)`, `extractKiroCommandResultText(...)`, and `parseKiroContextWindowSnapshot(...)`, which parse Kiro `/context show` output into `ThreadTokenUsageSnapshot` fields like `usedTokens`, `usedPercentage`, `toolUses`, `inputTokens`, and `outputTokens`. One important maintenance note: later alignment work removed the runtime `refreshContextWindow()` call path, so these parsing helpers remain in the file as reusable utilities and tests, but the current manager no longer emits live `thread.token-usage.updated` or `runtime.warning` events from `/context show`. The active telemetry path that remains is `_kiro.dev/compaction/status`, which emits waiting or compacted state transitions.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 20-73, 523-676, 696-1008, 1125-1153, 1416-1658`
Implemented `Kiro Integration` by adding a full ACP-backed provider runtime manager that translates Kiro CLI session lifecycle, turn lifecycle, tool-call updates, approval requests, and mode metadata into the repository’s `ProviderSession` and `ProviderRuntimeEvent` contracts. This is the provider adapter runtime component for Kiro threads.

#### `Lines 16-17, 678-686, 1087-1123`
Changed Kiro provider startup to support both `Remote SSH Support` and `Extra Customization` by allowing a thread to launch Kiro ACP on an SSH host and by allowing settings to override the Kiro CLI binary path per session. This is part of the Kiro process-bootstrap component.

#### `Lines 285-390, 723-729, 1011-1051, 1155-1213, 1291-1414`

This is the Kiro mode and approval-boundary component.

#### `Lines 136-143, 146-262, 277-282, 573-580, 637-641, 813-905, 925-980, 1261-1344, 1421-1448`

### `apps/server/src/open.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 35-37, 58-60, 287-302`
Replaced `OpenInEditorInput.cwd: string` with the authoritative `OpenInEditorInput.target`, so launch resolution no longer assumes "open the project cwd" for every editor action. The old variable was `input.cwd`; the replacement variable is `input.target`, which is now used by `shouldUseGotoFlag`, by the normal editor command path, and by the file-manager path. The current plain-string fallback remains a local shell/editor target such as a workspace root, absolute file path, or `path:line[:column]` string. `isRemoteUriTarget(target)` now detects `ssh://` string targets, and `resolveEditorLaunch` refuses to pass those targets into `open`/`explorer`/`xdg-open` when `editorDef.id === "file-manager"`, returning `OpenError("File manager does not support remote SSH editor targets.")` instead.

#### `Lines 14, 26-37, 62-114, 284-299`
Added structured `RemoteSshEditorTarget` with authoritative fields `kind: "remote-ssh"`, `hostAlias`, `path`, `isDirectory`, `line?`, and `column?`, then widened `OpenInEditorInput.target` from string-only to `string | RemoteSshEditorTarget`. The old remote contract encoded SSH editor opens as raw `ssh://...` strings; the replacement contract preserves host, path, directory/file mode, and optional cursor position as separate fields until the final launch adapter. `isRemoteSshEditorTarget(...)` is now the discriminator, and `resolveRemoteSshLaunch(...)` is the authoritative translation layer: it uses `supportsRemoteSshEditor(editorId)` to reject unsupported editors early, emits a single `ssh://<hostAlias><path>:line:column` URI for `zed`, and emits `["--remote", "ssh-remote+<hostAlias>", ...]` plus `ensureTrailingSlash(path)` or `--goto <path>:line:column` for Cursor/VS Code style editors. The plain-string target remains the fallback path for local opens and older shell-driven calls.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 35-37, 58-60, 287-302`
Changed editor launch input from project `cwd` to a project/file `target` so `Remote SSH Support` can resolve editor opens by project identity, relative path, and optional line/column instead of assuming a local workspace root. In practice this is the contract change that lets markdown links, diff entries, terminal path matches, and git file opens point at the right file within the right project context, including remote projects whose workspace cannot be represented as a local cwd. This is part of the project-aware editor-target routing component.

#### `Lines 14, 26-37, 62-114, 284-299`
Implemented structured remote SSH editor launch translation to support `Remote SSH Support` by preserving remote project metadata from project resolution through to the detached editor command. The technical detail here is that remote editor targeting now carries `hostAlias`, `path`, `isDirectory`, `line`, and `column` as first-class fields instead of flattening them into a best-effort URI string too early, which lets the server choose the correct per-editor launch contract for Zed versus VS Code/Cursor and fail closed for unsupported editors. This is part of the remote editor capability and launch-argument adaptation component.
- Dependency impact:
#### `Lines 35-37, 58-60, 287-302`
Depends on `packages/contracts/src/project.ts` `ProjectEditorTarget` and `ProjectOpenPathInEditorInput` fields (`projectId`, `threadId`, `relativePath`, `line`, `column`), `apps/web/src/projectEditorTargets.ts` converting raw UI links into project-path inputs, `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` `resolveProjectEditorTarget(...)` choosing project-root versus file targets, and `apps/web/src/wsNativeApi.ts` routing between `projects.openPathInEditor(...)` and `shell.openInEditor(...)`. No persistence or projection fields are involved; this is a runtime-only contract. If it regresses, chat markdown links, diff file opens, terminal path opens, git action file opens, and project-root "open in editor" actions can resolve the wrong target or incorrectly fall back to shell/file-manager behavior. Retest those flows, plus the explicit remote file-manager rejection path.

#### `Lines 14, 26-37, 62-114, 284-299`
Depends on `packages/shared/src/editor.ts` `supportsRemoteSshEditor(...)` and `filterRemoteSshEditors(...)`, `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` lines 929-943 where `project.remote.hostAlias` and the resolved remote absolute path are converted into `{ kind: "remote-ssh", ... }`, `apps/web/src/editorPreferences.ts` requiring `requireRemoteSsh` for remote project targets, and `apps/web/src/components/chat/OpenInPicker.tsx` filtering editor options for remote projects before the request is sent. No persistence or projection fields are involved. ### `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/CheckpointReactor.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 155-176`
`resolveCheckpointCwd(...)` no longer expects `thread.worktreePath: string | null`; it now expects `thread.projectPath: string` and forwards that thread shape into `resolveThreadWorkspaceCwd({ thread, projects })`. The old authoritative field in this reactor was `worktreePath`, which assumed one repo/worktree path was enough to identify checkpoint location. The replacement authoritative field is `projectPath`, which can already encode the active repo/worktree selected for a thread. The fallback path is now centralized in `resolveThreadWorkspaceCwd(...)`: use trimmed `thread.projectPath` first, otherwise fall back to `projects.find((entry) => entry.id === thread.projectId)?.workspaceRoot`, then let `preferSessionRuntime` choose between that path and any active session `cwd`. This file no longer has its own direct `worktreePath` fallback logic.

#### `Lines 576-583`
Added an early `if (thread.session?.providerName === "kiro")` branch in `handleRevertRequested(...)` that calls `appendRevertFailureActivity(...)` with detail `"Checkpoint revert is not supported yet for Kiro threads."` and returns before `resolveSessionRuntimeForThread(...)`, `checkpointStore.restoreCheckpoint(...)`, `providerService.rollbackConversation(...)`, stale-ref deletion, and dispatch of `thread.revert.complete`. Upstream implicitly treated every provider as revert-capable once a thread had a session and a git workspace; the new authoritative runtime gate is `thread.session.providerName`. The fallback path is unchanged for non-Kiro threads, which still run the full filesystem restore plus provider conversation rollback flow.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 155-176`
Changed checkpoint workspace resolution to support `Multi-Repo Support` by making checkpoint capture/revert read the thread’s canonical `projectPath` instead of a single optional `worktreePath`. That detail matters because a thread in a multi-repo project can now point at a specific nested repo or prepared worktree, and checkpoint capture, baseline creation, placeholder diff replacement, and revert all need to run against that exact repo rather than the project root. This is part of the thread-session-project-repo checkpoint routing component.

#### `Lines 576-583`
Changed checkpoint revert handling to support `Kiro Integration` by failing closed for Kiro-backed threads instead of attempting a provider rollback contract that the Kiro stack does not implement. Concretely, this keeps the reactor from driving filesystem checkpoint restore and provider turn rollback under a provider whose adapter path still bottoms out in an unsupported rollback call. This is part of the provider-aware checkpoint revert guard component.
- Dependency impact:
#### `Lines 155-176`
Depends on `apps/server/src/checkpointing/Utils.ts` `resolveThreadWorkspaceCwd(...)`, `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts` `OrchestrationThread.projectPath`, `apps/server/src/orchestration/projector.ts` and `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionPipeline.ts` carrying `projectPath` into the read model, `apps/server/src/persistence/Services/ProjectionThreads.ts` plus migration `apps/server/src/persistence/Migrations/020_MultiRepoThreadPaths.ts` persisting `project_path`, and sibling checkpoint consumers such as `apps/server/src/checkpointing/Layers/CheckpointDiffQuery.ts` and `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProviderCommandReactor.ts` that rely on the same cwd contract. The old related field `worktreePath` still exists in the thread projection for repo-slot bookkeeping, but it is no longer the authoritative checkpoint cwd input here. If this contract drifts, checkpoint refs can be captured from the wrong repo, turn diffs can summarize the wrong filesystem, and revert can restore the wrong worktree. Retest baseline capture on turn start, checkpoint capture on turn completion, placeholder diff replacement, and revert for threads whose `projectPath` points at a nested repo/worktree instead of `workspaceRoot`.

#### `Lines 576-583`
Depends on projected `thread.session.providerName` in the orchestration read model, `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts` revert/activity command chain (`thread.checkpoint-revert-requested`, `thread.activity.append`, `thread.revert.complete`), `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/KiroAdapter.ts` `rollbackThread(threadId, _numTurns)`, and `apps/server/src/kiroAcpManager.ts` `rollbackThread(threadId)` which currently throws unsupported. No new persistence fields are introduced by this guard; it reads existing session projection data and changes runtime control flow only. If this guard regresses, Kiro revert requests can attempt partial filesystem rollback, emit misleading revert completion, or surface raw adapter exceptions instead of a stable `checkpoint.revert.failed` activity. Retest checkpoint revert on Kiro threads, confirm Codex/Claude revert still completes, verify `checkpoint.revert.failed` activity rendering, and confirm Kiro revert does not call provider rollback or delete checkpoint refs.

### `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/OrchestrationReactor.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 10, 16, 22`
Added the `StartupThreadReconciler` service import, resolved it with `const startupThreadReconciler = yield* StartupThreadReconciler`, and appended `yield* startupThreadReconciler.start` to the `OrchestrationReactorShape["start"]` sequence. The old startup contract in this file only started `providerRuntimeIngestion`, `providerCommandReactor`, and `checkpointReactor`. The new authoritative startup sequence is those three plus `startupThreadReconciler.start`. The important non-obvious change is that `StartupThreadReconcilerLive` can already be present in the layer graph without doing anything; this file is the contract point that actually executes its `start` effect.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 10, 16, 22`
Changed orchestration startup sequencing to support `Debugability and Stability` by ensuring the startup-thread recovery pass runs every time the orchestration reactor boots. Concretely, this is what turns disconnected-thread reconciliation from "service available in DI" into "service actually runs and marks stale startup threads disconnected, then reconciles provider state." This is part of the startup-thread recovery component.
- Dependency impact:
#### `Lines 10, 16, 22`
Depends on `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/StartupThreadReconciler.ts`, whose `start` effect forks `runInitialReconciliation`, and on `apps/server/src/serverLayers.ts`, where `StartupThreadReconcilerLive` is provided into `OrchestrationReactorLive` alongside runtime ingestion, provider command, and checkpoint layers. The old fallback behavior was effectively "no reconciliation pass runs at startup" even though the service existed. If this contract drifts, the server can boot with stale threads still marked running, disconnected startup sessions never normalized, and recoverable provider threads never reconciled. Retest cold startup with persisted running threads, crash or restart recovery, provider session state normalization to `disconnected`, and confirm the other three reactors still start in sequence.

### `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionPipeline.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 360-395`
`applyProjectsProjection(...)` now persists three additional project fields on both create and meta-update flows: `remote`, `gitMode`, and `gitRepos`. The old projection contract only wrote `projectId`, `title`, `workspaceRoot`, `defaultModelSelection`, and `scripts`. The new authoritative fields are `event.payload.remote ?? null`, `event.payload.gitMode`, and `event.payload.gitRepos` on `project.created`, plus the guarded `...(event.payload.remote !== undefined ? { remote: ... } : {})`, `gitMode`, and `gitRepos` spreads on `project.meta-updated`. The fallback path is now explicit in surrounding contracts: the decider still seeds `gitMode: "none"` and `gitRepos: null` when project discovery has not produced real topology yet, and update events preserve the existing projected values when these payload fields are omitted.

#### `Lines 424-456`
`applyThreadsProjection(...)` now writes `projectPath: event.payload.projectPath` on `thread.created` and conditionally updates `projectPath` on `thread.meta-updated`. The old projection contract persisted `branch` and `worktreePath` but not the thread’s selected repo path. The new authoritative field is `projectPath`; the old contract it replaced forced downstream readers to infer the active repo from `worktreePath[]` or from the project root. The fallback path is that `thread.meta-updated` preserves `existingRow.value.projectPath` whenever `event.payload.projectPath` is omitted.

#### `Lines 544-555, 967-1001`
The pipeline now treats `thread.turn-completed` as a first-class projected event in two places. In `applyThreadsProjection(...)`, `case "thread.turn-completed"` was added beside `thread.turn-diff-completed` so `latestTurnId` is updated as soon as the turn completes. In `applyThreadTurnsProjection(...)`, a new `case "thread.turn-completed"` upserts or creates a turn row with `assistantMessageId`, `state`, `requestedAt`, `startedAt`, `completedAt`, and null checkpoint fields. The old contract projected turn completion only through assistant-message updates and `thread.turn-diff-completed`; turns that completed before any diff event could leave `latestTurnId` or the turn row itself behind. The new authoritative event is `thread.turn-completed`. The fallback path is explicit: existing rows keep their original `startedAt` / `requestedAt`, while newly synthesized rows use `event.payload.completedAt` for both until richer timing data arrives.

#### `Lines 772-776`
`applyThreadSessionsProjection(...)` now persists `providerThreadId: event.payload.session.providerThreadId ?? null` alongside the existing `status`, `providerName`, `runtimeMode`, `activeTurnId`, and `lastError` fields. The old session projection contract had no durable provider-thread identity at all. The new authoritative field is `providerThreadId`, and the fallback path is explicit `null` when the session payload does not carry a provider-native thread id.

#### `Lines 868-872, 920-924, 958-962, 1005-1048`
Added `checkpointDiff: null` to every newly materialized turn row that previously initialized only `checkpointTurnCount`, `checkpointRef`, `checkpointStatus`, and `checkpointFiles` in the `thread.session-set`, assistant `thread.message-sent`, `thread.turn-interrupt-requested`, and `thread.turn-completed` paths. Then `thread.turn-diff-completed` started persisting `checkpointDiff: event.payload.diff ?? existingTurn.value.checkpointDiff ?? null` on updates and `checkpointDiff: event.payload.diff ?? null` on inserts. The old projection contract had no turn-level inline diff field; the replacement authoritative field is `checkpointDiff`. The fallback path is explicit: rows start with `null`, and when a later diff-completed event omits `diff`, the projection preserves any previously stored `checkpointDiff` instead of clearing it.
- Feature:
#### `Lines 360-395`
Changed project projection persistence to support both `Remote SSH Support` and `Multi-Repo Support` by storing remote host identity and discovered repo topology on the durable project row instead of forcing snapshot code to reconstruct that state from transient inputs. This is part of the project metadata projection component.

#### `Lines 424-456`
Changed thread projection persistence to support `Multi-Repo Support` by making the thread-selected repo/worktree path a first-class durable field. This is the write-side half of the thread-session-project-turn mapping that lets git, checkpoint, editor, and terminal flows resolve the exact repo attached to a thread instead of guessing from project-level state.

#### `Lines 544-555, 967-1001`
Changed turn lifecycle projection to support `Debugability and Stability` by projecting a completed turn as soon as orchestration emits `thread.turn-completed`, which is necessary for disconnected startup reconciliation and for turns that finish before any checkpoint diff is available. This is part of the turn-lifecycle recovery and projection component.

#### `Lines 772-776`
Changed session projection persistence to support `Debugability and Stability` by keeping the provider’s own thread identifier on the durable thread-session row, which is required for resume/adopt diagnostics and reconnect-state reconciliation. This is part of the provider session reconnect-metadata component.

#### `Lines 868-872, 920-924, 958-962, 1005-1048`
Changed turn projection persistence to support `Remote SSH Support` by storing the inline unified diff text emitted with `thread.turn-diff-completed` on the turn row itself, so remote/provider-backed diff flows survive restarts and can be served without re-diffing local git checkpoints. This is part of the provider-backed checkpoint diff persistence component.

### `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### `Lines 52-58, 252-270, 691-721`
The project snapshot path now decodes and reads `remote`, `gitMode`, and `gitRepos`, then runs live repo discovery before returning each `OrchestrationProject`. `ProjectionProjectDbRowSchema` gained `remote: Schema.NullOr(Schema.fromJsonString(ProjectRemoteTarget))` and `gitRepos: Schema.NullOr(Schema.fromJsonString(Schema.Array(ProjectGitRepo)))`; `listProjectRows` now selects `remote_json`, `git_mode`, and `git_repos_json`; and `getSnapshot()` no longer maps `projectRows` directly. "none", gitRepos: row.gitRepos ?? null }` if discovery throws. The old contract was “return persisted project rows as-is with no remote-aware repo discovery step.” The new authoritative snapshot fields are `row.remote`, `discovery.gitMode`, and `discovery.gitRepos`.

#### `Lines 67-72, 274-288, 723-742`
The thread snapshot path now reads `project_path`, `branch_json`, and `worktree_path_json` as first-class multi-repo fields. `ProjectionThreadDbRowSchema` gained JSON decoders for `branch` and `worktreePath`, `listThreadRows` switched from selecting scalar `branch` / `worktree_path` columns to `project_path AS "projectPath"`, `branch_json AS "branch"`, and `worktree_path_json AS "worktreePath"`, and each `OrchestrationThread` now includes `projectPath: row.projectPath` when the snapshot is assembled. The old contract hydrated thread git state from the older scalar columns and had no thread-level `projectPath` in the snapshot at all. The new authoritative thread git fields are `projectPath`, `branch`, and `worktreePath`.

#### `Lines 80-85, 122-206, 436-453, 459-468, 557-561, 673-688, 741-747`
Added a remote-runtime overlay path for session snapshots. The file now defines `ProviderSessionRuntimeDbRowSchema` for `resumeCursor` and `runtimePayload`, loads `provider_session_runtime` rows with `listProviderRuntimeRows`, tracks them in `providerRuntimeByThread`, and overlays them onto projected thread sessions with `mergeRemoteRuntimeSession({ session, runtime })`. `mergeRemoteRuntimeSession(...)` reads `readPersistedRemoteSessionMetadata(input.runtime.runtimePayload)`, derives `activeTurnId` and `lastError` from runtime metadata first, computes `runtimeStatus` via `runtimeStatusToSessionStatus(...)`, and chooses `providerThreadId` based on `shouldOverrideLifecycle` comparing `input.runtime.lastSeenAt` against `input.session.updatedAt`. A later fix also added the `case "ready"` branch so interrupted remote sessions do not incorrectly snap back to plain `ready`. When threads are assembled, only projects with `project.remote !== null` go through this merge path; local projects still use the persisted `sessionsByThread` row directly. The old contract exposed only the projected `projection_thread_sessions` row with no runtime overlay or reconnect metadata merge.

## Files 51-75

### `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProviderCommandReactor.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `135-192, 266-438, 835-850` - Provider Session Start and Reuse
The authoritative launch inputs are now `thread.modelSelection`, `options.modelSelection`, `preferredProvider`, `projectRemote`, `effectiveProviderOptions`, `threadProviderOptions`, `threadModelSelections`, and `readProviderThreadIdFromResumeCursor(session.resumeCursor)`. The old contract this replaced was `options.provider`, `options.model`, and `options.modelOptions`, with raw pass-through `options.providerOptions` and reuse keyed only off projected `thread.session.status !== "stopped"`. `ensureSessionForThread(...)` now rejects cross-provider `requestedModelSelection`, scopes provider options by provider (`claudeAgent.binaryPath`, `claudeAgent.permissionMode`, `claudeAgent.maxThinkingTokens`, `kiro.binaryPath`, `kiro.remote`, `codex.binaryPath`, `codex.homePath`, `codex.remote`), starts sessions with `modelSelection`, requires `providerService.listSessions()` to confirm a live backend session before reuse, and restarts when `providerOptionsRestartKey(effectiveProviderOptions)` changes or the cached Claude `ModelSelection` changes. `bindSessionToThread(...)` also writes `providerThreadId` and `resumeAvailable` when `session.resumeCursor` contains remote metadata. The fallback paths are explicit: if `projectRemote` is `null`, scoped options stay local-only or `undefined`; if `providerService.listSessions()` cannot find the thread, the reactor starts a fresh session instead of trusting projection state; if `sessionModelSwitch === "unsupported"`, later turn sends pin the requested provider/model pair to `activeSession.model`; and `thread.runtime-mode-set` reuses cached `threadProviderOptions` and `threadModelSelections` so mode flips do not silently drop overrides.

#### Lines `441-541, 675-804` - Turn Dispatch and Failure Surfacing
`sendTurnForThread(...)` now accepts `modelSelection?: ModelSelection` and only `interactionMode?: "default" | "plan"`. The old contract accepted separate `provider`, `model`, `modelOptions`, and temporarily allowed `"help"`. The authoritative turn payload is now `requestedModelSelection = input.modelSelection ?? threadModelSelections.get(threadId) ?? thread.modelSelection`, with `modelForTurn` falling back to `activeSession.model` when the provider reports `sessionModelSwitch === "unsupported"`. `processTurnStartRequested(...)` routes failures through `surfaceTurnStartFailure(...)`, which appends `provider.turn.start.failed` activity and rewrites `thread.session.lastError` while preserving `providerThreadId`, `resumeAvailable`, `reconnectState`, `reconnectSummary`, and `reconnectUpdatedAt`. Approval and user-input response failures also stopped synthesizing `stalePendingRequestDetail(...)`; they now surface raw `Cause.pretty(cause)` output instead of masking provider-specific failures behind a generic stale-request string.

#### Lines `124-133, 544-620, 658-672` - Worktree Branch Rename for First Turn
The authoritative worktree-rename inputs are now `gitSettings.commitPrompt`, `gitSettings.textGenerationModelSelection`, `projectRemote`, `projectPath`, `branch[activeRepoIndex]`, and `worktreePath[activeRepoIndex]`. Upstream only handled scalar `branch` and `worktreePath`, used `DEFAULT_GIT_TEXT_GENERATION_MODEL` or `gitSettings.textGenerationModel`, and wrote back a single `branch` plus `worktreePath` without keeping repo-slot alignment. The current code finds `activeRepoIndex = thread.worktreePath.findIndex((value) => value !== null)`, reads `oldBranch` and `cwd` from that slot, passes `remote` into both `textGeneration.generateBranchName(...)` and `git.renameBranch(...)`, and dispatches `thread.meta.update` with `projectPath`, `nextBranch`, and `nextWorktreePath` arrays. The fallback path is "skip rename": no active repo slot, missing `oldBranch` or `cwd`, non-temporary branch, multiple user messages, a generator failure, or a generated name equal to `oldBranch` all leave thread metadata unchanged. When `gitSettings.textGenerationModelSelection` is absent or is not `codex` or `claudeAgent`, `resolveGitTextGenerationModelSelection(...)` falls back to `{ provider: "codex", model: DEFAULT_GIT_TEXT_GENERATION_MODEL_BY_PROVIDER.codex }`.

#### Lines `884-925` - Per-Thread Reactor Workers
Replaced the single `worker` with `workersByThreadId`, `workerForThread(...)`, and `drain` over `Array.from(workersByThreadId.values())`. The old contract serialized every provider intent event through one `DrainableWorker`, so a blocked `thread.turn-start-requested` could delay unrelated approvals, interrupts, and mode changes for other threads. The fallback path is lazy worker creation per thread ID and a no-op drain when no thread workers were created.
- Feature:
#### Lines `135-192, 266-438, 835-850` - Provider Session Start and Reuse
Changed provider session launch and restart to support `Remote SSH Support`, `Kiro Integration`, and `Extra Customization` by deriving provider-specific launch options from project remote state and persisted thread model selection instead of treating every provider as a local Codex-style process. Concretely, this file now launches Codex with `providerOptions.codex.remote`, `providerOptions.codex.homePath`, and `providerOptions.codex.binaryPath`, launches Kiro with `providerOptions.kiro.remote` and `providerOptions.kiro.binaryPath`, launches Claude with `providerOptions.claudeAgent.binaryPath`, `providerOptions.claudeAgent.permissionMode`, and `providerOptions.claudeAgent.maxThinkingTokens`, and restarts when those exact launch contracts change. This is part of the thread-session-provider mapping and restart-decision component.

#### Lines `441-541, 675-804` - Turn Dispatch and Failure Surfacing
Changed turn dispatch and failure reporting to support `Kiro Integration` and `Debugability and Stability` by sending provider-tagged `ModelSelection` payloads, constraining interaction mode to the ACP-safe `default` and `plan` set, and keeping reconnect and session-health metadata intact when a turn cannot start. This is part of the provider turn dispatch and failure-surfacing component.

#### Lines `124-133, 544-620, 658-672` - Worktree Branch Rename for First Turn
Changed first-turn worktree branch naming to support `Multi-Repo Support`, `Remote SSH Support`, and `Extra Customization` by resolving the selected repo slot inside a thread, carrying the project SSH remote into both branch-name generation and git rename execution, and honoring project-level git prompt and model-selection overrides. This is part of the thread-project-repo mapping and worktree-rename component.

#### Lines `884-925` - Per-Thread Reactor Workers
Changed provider-intent scheduling to support `Debugability and Stability` by isolating each thread's provider event queue so one slow or hung session cannot starve unrelated threads. This is part of the per-thread durable work-queue component inside the orchestration reactor stack.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `135-192, 266-438, 835-850` - Provider Session Start and Reuse
This block depends on `OrchestrationThread.modelSelection`, `ThreadTurnStartRequestedPayload.modelSelection`, and `ProviderStartOptions.codex|kiro|claudeAgent` in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, on `ProviderService.startSession(...)`, `ProviderService.listSessions(...)`, and provider capability reads in `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/ProviderService.ts`, on `readProviderThreadIdFromResumeCursor(...)` in `apps/server/src/provider/remoteSessionMetadata.ts`, and on `ProjectionPipeline.ts` / `ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts` persisting and hydrating `providerThreadId`, `resumeAvailable`, and reconnect state. The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are local versus SSH session start, Kiro remote session launch, Claude override changes that should restart the session, runtime-mode flips after settings changes, and refresh or reconnect flows where a projected session exists but no live backend session exists.

The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are Kiro default-versus-plan turns, turn starts after reconnect, approval responses on recovered sessions, user-input responses on resumed sessions, and any failure path that should preserve reconnect metadata instead of overwriting the session row.

The runtime and UI flows that break first if this contract drifts are first-turn temp worktree rename in local single-repo threads, the same path in local multi-repo threads, SSH-backed worktree renames, branch toolbar state after rename, and settings flows where a saved git prompt or Claude git text-generation model should change the generated branch name.

The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are one hung or SSH-slow thread start alongside a healthy thread, approval and interrupt responsiveness under load, and reactor drain on shutdown.

### `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProviderRuntimeIngestion.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `188-205, 250-299` - Tool Approval Activity Mapping
The authoritative approval-kind mapper `requestKindFromCanonicalRequestType(...)` now returns `"tool"` for provider request types `"dynamic_tool_call"` and `"unknown"`. The old contract only returned `"command"`, `"file-read"`, or `"file-change"`, so those Kiro-originated approvals were projected as generic approvals with no stable `requestKind`. `runtimeEventToActivities(...)` now labels those requests as `"Tool approval requested"` and includes `payload.requestKind = "tool"` on both `approval.requested` and `approval.resolved` activities. The fallback path is still explicit: any request type outside the mapped set returns `undefined` and stays on the generic approval label.

#### Lines `35-46, 110-117, 208-233, 599-810, 964-992, 1085, 1225-1263, 1314-1351, 1418-1433` - Kiro Stream Segmentation and Interaction-Mode Sync
The authoritative live-stream state is now `turnAssistantStreamStateByTurnKey`, whose entries carry `nextSegmentIndex`, `activeMessageId`, and `forceNewMessage`. Upstream used `MessageId.makeUnsafe(\`assistant:${event.itemId ?? event.turnId ?? event.eventId}\`)` and forwarded live assistant deltas directly, so Kiro could merge pre-tool and post-tool text into one message and spam the UI with tiny ACP chunks. The current code adds Kiro-specific chunk thresholds `MAX_KIRO_STREAMING_COALESCE_CHARS` and `MIN_KIRO_STREAMING_COALESCE_CHARS`, `resolveAssistantMessageIdForEvent(...)`, `noteToolBoundaryForAssistantSegmentation(...)`, `appendStreamingAssistantText(...)`, and cleanup through `clearTurnAssistantStreamState(...)` on turn completion, assistant completion, and session exit. The interaction-mode parser also changed: `asProviderInteractionMode(...)` no longer accepts `"help"`, and `thread.metadata.updated` only projects `thread.interaction-mode.set` for `"default"` and `"plan"`. The fallback paths are explicit: non-Kiro providers keep the old assistant message-id pattern and return raw deltas from `appendStreamingAssistantText(...)`; buffered delivery still uses `appendBufferedAssistantText(...)`; missing `turnId` skips Kiro segmentation and falls back to the legacy message-id path; and unsupported metadata interaction-mode values are ignored instead of mutating thread state.

#### Lines `19-21, 622-642, 1436-1484` - Remote Git Eligibility and Provider Diff Projection
The authoritative git-backed check is now `project = readModel.projects.find((entry) => entry.id === thread.projectId)`, `resolveThreadWorkspaceCwd({ thread, projects: [project] })`, and `project.remote ? true : isGitRepository(workspaceCwd)`. The old contract resolved against the full `readModel.projects` set and only treated a thread as git-backed when a local `isGitRepository(...)` check succeeded. On `turn.diff.updated`, the authoritative diff fields are now `payload.unifiedDiff ?? payload.diff ?? payload.patch ?? ""`, parsed through `parseTurnDiffFilesFromUnifiedDiff(...)`, and projected into `thread.turn.diff.complete` as both `files` and `diff`. The old contract emitted a placeholder provider diff with `files: []` and no stored unified diff text. The fallback path is still explicit: missing project or missing workspace cwd returns `false`; parse failures yield `files: []`; existing checkpoints for the same `turnId` short-circuit the placeholder write; and empty provider diff text still produces an empty-string `diff` payload.

#### Lines `1194-1210, 1387-1401` - Remote Session Metadata Carry-Forward
The authoritative session fields written during runtime lifecycle and runtime-error projection now include `providerThreadId`, `resumeAvailable`, `reconnectState`, `reconnectSummary`, and `reconnectUpdatedAt`. The old contract rewrote `thread.session` with only `threadId`, `status`, `providerName`, `runtimeMode`, `activeTurnId`, `lastError`, and `updatedAt`, which meant remote identity and reconnect state could be dropped on `thread.started`, `session.state.changed`, `turn.completed`, or `runtime.error`. The current code adopts `event.payload.providerThreadId` when `thread.started` provides it and otherwise carries forward the existing remote metadata. The fallback path is explicit: if those remote fields are absent they stay omitted rather than being synthesized.
- Feature:
#### Lines `188-205, 250-299` - Tool Approval Activity Mapping
Changed runtime approval ingestion to support `Kiro Integration` and `Debugability and Stability` by classifying generic Kiro tool approvals as first-class tool approvals instead of collapsing them into opaque approval prompts. This is part of the provider approval activity projection component.

#### Lines `35-46, 110-117, 208-233, 599-810, 964-992, 1085, 1225-1263, 1314-1351, 1418-1433` - Kiro Stream Segmentation and Interaction-Mode Sync
Changed provider runtime ingestion to support `Kiro Integration` and `Debugability and Stability` by segmenting Kiro assistant output across tool boundaries, coalescing tiny ACP streaming chunks into readable deltas, and refusing to project unsupported interaction modes back into orchestration state. This is part of the assistant-stream normalization and provider-metadata sync component.

#### Lines `19-21, 622-642, 1436-1484` - Remote Git Eligibility and Provider Diff Projection
Changed runtime diff ingestion to support `Remote SSH Support` and `Multi-Repo Support` by resolving git eligibility from the thread's selected project workspace and by persisting provider-supplied unified diff text plus parsed file stats for remote turns. This is part of the checkpoint-diff projection and thread-project-workspace resolution component.

#### Lines `1194-1210, 1387-1401` - Remote Session Metadata Carry-Forward
Changed runtime session projection to support `Remote SSH Support` and `Debugability and Stability` by preserving provider-thread identity and reconnect metadata across normal lifecycle updates and runtime error transitions. This is part of the remote session health and recovery projection component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `188-205, 250-299` - Tool Approval Activity Mapping

The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are Kiro approval prompts, approval resolution history, and any UI path that distinguishes tool approvals from command or file approvals.

#### Lines `35-46, 110-117, 208-233, 599-810, 964-992, 1085, 1225-1263, 1314-1351, 1418-1433` - Kiro Stream Segmentation and Interaction-Mode Sync

The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are SSH-backed turn diff capture, multi-repo diff routing, full-thread diff reconstruction after refresh, and any provider-backed diff view that expects file-level additions or deletions instead of an empty file list.

#### Lines `1194-1210, 1387-1401` - Remote Session Metadata Carry-Forward
This block depends on `OrchestrationSession.providerThreadId`, `resumeAvailable`, `reconnectState`, `reconnectSummary`, and `reconnectUpdatedAt` in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, on remote runtime metadata persistence and hydration in `ProjectionThreadSessions.ts` and `ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts`, and on the provider health or reconnect UI that reads those fields after refresh and failure. The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are remote session start, reconnect banners, resume-after-refresh, and runtime error handling where the session must stay tied to the same provider thread instead of reverting to a generic local-looking error row.

### `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/StartupThreadReconciler.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `24-88, 271-300` - Startup Candidate Selection
Upstream had no startup reconciler, so the authoritative startup behavior was effectively "boot the other orchestration layers and leave persisted thread state untouched." This file adds `readRequestId(...)`, `hasPendingApproval(...)`, `hasPendingUserInput(...)`, `isRecoverableStartupThread(...)`, `runInitialReconciliation`, and the reconciler `start` effect. Candidate selection is now `deletedAt === null`, `isRecoverableStartupThread(thread)`, `latestTurn?.completedAt === null`, `!hasPendingApproval(thread)`, and `!hasPendingUserInput(thread)`, followed by a pre-reconciliation `thread.session.set` to `"disconnected"`. The later silent-shutdown follow-up changed the old first-pass rule `thread.session?.status === "running"` to `isRecoverableStartupThread(...)`, which also admits `status === "stopped" && thread.session?.resumeAvailable === true`. `hasPendingApproval(...)` also treats `provider.approval.respond.failed` with detail containing `"Unknown pending permission request"` as closing the tracked request, so stale shutdown-era approval failures do not block recovery forever. The fallback path is explicit: threads without matching request IDs, without recoverable session state, with a completed latest turn, or with still-open approval or user-input activity are skipped entirely, and `start` forks `runInitialReconciliation.pipe(Effect.ignore)` so startup never fails closed on reconciler errors.

#### Lines `90-269` - Session Reconstruction and Turn Settlement
This entire recovery contract is fork-added. The authoritative recovery helpers are now `toSessionFromThread(...)`, `toSessionFromProvider(...)`, `setThreadSession(...)`, `stopRecoveredSession(...)`, and `reconcileThread(...)`. `toSessionFromProvider(...)` rebuilds `providerName`, `runtimeMode`, `activeTurnId`, `lastError`, `providerThreadId`, `resumeAvailable`, `reconnectState`, `reconnectSummary`, and `reconnectUpdatedAt` from the live `ProviderSession` plus the existing projected session, using `readProviderThreadIdFromResumeCursor(providerSession.resumeCursor)` as the preferred provider-thread source. `reconcileThread(...)` now has three concrete outcomes after `ProviderService.inspectRecoverableThread({ threadId })`: if pending approval or user input is still open, dispatch `thread.session.set` with `status: "ready"` and `activeTurnId: null`; if `inspected.session.activeTurnId` exists, dispatch `thread.session.set` with `status: "running"` and that `activeTurnId`; otherwise, if `latestTurn.turnId` exists, dispatch `thread.turn.complete` with `state: "completed"`, then `stopRecoveredSession(...)`, then `thread.session.set` to `"stopped"`. The old contract this replaces was "startup leaves persisted session and turn rows alone until some later runtime event corrects them." This file briefly wrote a provisional `"starting"` session state before inspection in its initial version, but `4bd389f5` removed that transition, so recovered threads stay `"disconnected"` until inspection returns a concrete result. The fallback paths are explicit: missing or deleted thread, non-`"disconnected"` session, or already-completed latest turn return immediately; inspection timeout, failure, or `Option.none` reassert `"disconnected"` and stop the recovered session; missing projected session returns `null` from the session builders and suppresses the dispatch; and a thread deleted between the first and refreshed read-model lookup stops the recovered provider session and exits.
- Feature:
#### Lines `24-88, 271-300` - Startup Candidate Selection
Changed startup thread selection to support `Debugability and Stability` by identifying only threads whose provider session and orchestration turn state can still diverge after a restart, while excluding threads that are legitimately waiting on approval or user input. This is part of the startup thread-session health scan component.

#### Lines `90-269` - Session Reconstruction and Turn Settlement
Implemented deterministic startup recovery to support `Debugability and Stability` by reconciling persisted orchestration state against `ProviderService.inspectRecoverableThread(...)`, reconstructing provider-backed session identity from resume metadata, and closing orphaned turns when the provider is already idle after restart. This is part of the startup recovery and turn-settlement component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `24-88, 271-300` - Startup Candidate Selection
This block depends on activity kinds emitted by `ProviderRuntimeIngestion.ts` and `ProviderCommandReactor.ts` (`approval.requested`, `approval.resolved`, `provider.approval.respond.failed`, `user-input.requested`, and `user-input.resolved`), on `OrchestrationThread.session.resumeAvailable` in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, and on `OrchestrationReactor.ts` starting this reconciler during server boot. The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are cold startup with threads still marked running, silent stop-all shutdown where the thread was persisted as stopped but resumable, stale approval failures blocking recovery forever, and startup paths that should leave approval- or input-blocked threads alone.

#### Lines `90-269` - Session Reconstruction and Turn Settlement
This block depends on `ProviderService.inspectRecoverableThread(...)` and `ProviderService.stopSession(...)`, `readProviderThreadIdFromResumeCursor(...)` in `apps/server/src/provider/remoteSessionMetadata.ts`, `thread.turn.complete` handling in `apps/server/src/orchestration/decider.ts`, `apps/server/src/orchestration/projector.ts`, and `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionPipeline.ts`, plus the remote session fields carried through `ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts` and web session state. The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are restart during an active turn, restart after the provider already finished but projection still says running, refresh with a resumable remote session that must preserve `providerThreadId`, reconcile timeout handling, and deleted-thread cleanup during startup.
