### `apps/server/src/orchestration/decider.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `77-117` - Project Metadata Event Contract
The authoritative project event fields are now `remote`, `defaultModelSelection`, `gitMode`, and `gitRepos`. `project.created` now writes `remote: command.remote`, `defaultModelSelection: command.defaultModelSelection ?? null`, `gitMode: "none"`, and `gitRepos: null`, while `project.meta-updated` now forwards `remote`, `defaultModelSelection`, `gitMode`, and `gitRepos` when defined. The old contract used `defaultModel`, had no `remote`, and carried no project-level git discovery state at all. The fallback paths are explicit: newly created projects default to `gitMode: "none"` and `gitRepos: null`, and `project.meta.update` only emits each field when the command provided it.

#### Lines `163-224` - Thread Model and Project-Path Contract
`thread.created` and `thread.meta-updated` now use `modelSelection` and `projectPath`. The old contract used the scalar thread field `model` and had no `projectPath`, which meant the command layer could not point a thread at a specific repo inside a multi-repo project. The current code writes `modelSelection: command.modelSelection` on create, forwards `command.modelSelection` on meta update, and forwards `command.projectPath` when defined while keeping `branch` and `worktreePath` alongside it. The fallback path is explicit: `projectPath` is only emitted when the command provides it, so existing thread metadata remains unchanged if a caller omits the repo path.

#### Lines `253-356` - Interaction Mode Logging and Turn-Start Payload
`thread.interaction-mode.set` now reads the current thread and logs when `thread.interactionMode !== command.interactionMode`, recording `previousInteractionMode`, `nextInteractionMode`, `threadId`, and `commandId`. `thread.turn.start` now emits `payload.modelSelection` instead of the old `provider`, `model`, and `modelOptions` fields, and it forwards `gitSettings` when present. The old contract therefore lost provider-tagged model identity at the command boundary and had no path for git text-generation settings. The fallback paths are explicit: no log is emitted when the interaction mode is unchanged, `gitSettings` is only forwarded when defined, and `assistantDeliveryMode` still falls back to `DEFAULT_ASSISTANT_DELIVERY_MODE`.

#### Lines `577-622` - Completed-Turn and Inline-Diff Events
Added a new decider branch for `thread.turn.complete`, which emits the event `thread.turn-completed` with `turnId`, `state`, `assistantMessageId`, and `completedAt`. `thread.turn.diff.complete` also now forwards the optional `diff` field alongside `files`, `checkpointRef`, `status`, and `assistantMessageId`. The old contract had no `thread.turn.complete` command-to-event mapping at all, and `thread.turn-diff-completed` stopped at file metadata without carrying the unified diff text itself. The fallback paths are explicit: `assistantMessageId` is normalized to `null` when absent, and `diff` is omitted when the command does not provide it.
- Feature:
#### Lines `77-117` - Project Metadata Event Contract
Changed project command decisions to support `Remote SSH Support`, `Multi-Repo Support`, and `Extra Customization` by persisting SSH target identity, provider-tagged default model selection, and project-level repo discovery state at event creation time. This is part of the project metadata and default-contract component.

#### Lines `163-224` - Thread Model and Project-Path Contract
Changed thread creation and metadata updates to support `Multi-Repo Support` and `Extra Customization` by replacing the thread-level `model` scalar with provider-tagged `modelSelection` and by adding `projectPath` so a thread can stay bound to the selected repo within a larger project. This is part of the thread-project mapping component.

#### Lines `253-356` - Interaction Mode Logging and Turn-Start Payload
Changed turn-start command decisions to support `Kiro Integration`, `Extra Customization`, and `Debugability and Stability` by carrying provider-tagged model selection and git text-generation settings into the turn-start event while emitting explicit interaction-mode change logs for debugging mode transitions. This is part of the provider turn-start command contract component.

#### Lines `577-622` - Completed-Turn and Inline-Diff Events

This is part of the turn lifecycle and checkpoint-diff event contract component.

### `apps/server/src/orchestration/projector.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `182-225` - Project Read-Model Fields
The authoritative in-memory project fields are now `remote`, `defaultModelSelection`, `gitMode`, and `gitRepos`. `project.created` now copies `payload.remote`, `payload.defaultModelSelection`, `payload.gitMode`, and `payload.gitRepos` into the read model, and `project.meta-updated` now mutates those same fields when present. The old projector contract tracked `workspaceRoot`, `title`, and the older default-model shape, but it did not mirror SSH target identity or project-level repo discovery state into the read model. The fallback path is explicit: each field is only updated when its payload member is defined, so existing project read-model state is preserved when an update omits that member.

#### Lines `262-312` - Thread Model Selection and Project Path
The authoritative thread read-model fields are now `modelSelection` and `projectPath`. `thread.created` decodes and stores `payload.modelSelection` and `payload.projectPath`, and `thread.meta-updated` mutates `modelSelection` and `projectPath` when present while continuing to carry `branch` and `worktreePath`. The old projector contract stored the scalar thread `model` and had no `projectPath`, so the in-memory read model could not represent which repo inside a multi-repo project the thread actually targeted. The fallback path is explicit: `projectPath` only changes when the event payload includes it.

#### Lines `25, 486-518` - Completed-Turn Projection
Added the schema import `ThreadTurnCompletedPayload` and a new `case "thread.turn-completed"` that decodes the payload and updates `thread.latestTurn`. The old projector contract only moved `latestTurn` forward from running-session state or `thread.turn-diff-completed`, so a recovered or provider-completed turn could remain effectively "running" until a diff event arrived. The new handler writes `turnId`, `state`, `completedAt`, and `assistantMessageId`, while preserving `requestedAt` and `startedAt` when the incoming `payload.turnId` matches the current `thread.latestTurn?.turnId`; otherwise it falls back to `payload.completedAt` for both timestamps. The fallback path is explicit: if the target thread is missing, the projector returns `nextBase` unchanged.
- Feature:
#### Lines `182-225` - Project Read-Model Fields
Changed in-memory project projection to support `Remote SSH Support`, `Multi-Repo Support`, and `Extra Customization` by keeping SSH target identity, provider-tagged default model selection, and project-level git discovery state on the live read model. This is part of the project read-model projection component.

#### Lines `262-312` - Thread Model Selection and Project Path
Changed in-memory thread projection to support `Multi-Repo Support` and `Extra Customization` by keeping provider-tagged `modelSelection` and the selected repo `projectPath` on the thread read model instead of a single model scalar with no repo-level cwd identity. This is part of the thread-project mapping component.

#### Lines `25, 486-518` - Completed-Turn Projection
Changed in-memory turn projection to support `Debugability and Stability` by giving `thread.turn-completed` a first-class read-model update path instead of relying on later diff events to settle `latestTurn`. This is part of the turn lifecycle projection component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `182-225` - Project Read-Model Fields
This block depends on `ProjectCreatedPayload` and `ProjectMetaUpdatedPayload` in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, on `apps/server/src/orchestration/decider.ts` emitting the same fields, and on read-side consumers such as `ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts`, `ProjectionPipeline.ts`, and `ProjectionProjects.ts` expecting the in-memory and persisted project shapes to agree. The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are SSH project hydration after create or update, project default-model display, project repo discovery state in the sidebar or branch toolbar, and any read-model-driven project query that expects `remote`, `gitMode`, or `gitRepos`.

#### Lines `262-312` - Thread Model Selection and Project Path
This block depends on `ThreadCreatedPayload` and `ThreadMetaUpdatedPayload` in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, on `apps/server/src/orchestration/decider.ts` emitting `modelSelection` and `projectPath`, and on downstream read-model consumers such as `ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts`, `CheckpointReactor.ts`, `CheckpointDiffQuery.ts`, and `ProviderCommandReactor.ts`. The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are thread creation from a selected repo, repo-switch updates, checkpoint cwd resolution, and provider-session cwd selection after refresh.

#### Lines `25, 486-518` - Completed-Turn Projection
This block depends on `ThreadTurnCompletedPayload` in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, on `apps/server/src/orchestration/decider.ts` and `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/StartupThreadReconciler.ts` emitting `thread.turn-completed`, and on downstream consumers such as `ProjectionPipeline.ts`, `ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts`, web thread lists, and active-chat state reading `thread.latestTurn`. The runtime flows that break first if this contract drifts are startup recovery after a crash or restart, turns that complete without an immediate diff event, and any UI surface that uses `latestTurn.state`, `startedAt`, or `completedAt` to decide whether a thread is still running.

### `apps/server/src/persistence/Layers/ProjectionProjects.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `24, 42, 55, 68, 88, 110` - Remote Project Target Persistence
Added `remote` to `ProjectionProjectDbRow` as `Schema.NullOr(Schema.fromJsonString(ProjectRemoteTarget))`, added the `remote_json` column to every `INSERT`, `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE`, `getById`, and `listAll` SQL shape, and made `row.remote !== null ? JSON.stringify(row.remote) : null` the authoritative write path. The old upstream contract had no project-level remote field in this repository at all, so `projection_projects` could only distinguish projects by `workspace_root`. The fallback path is explicit: local projects continue to persist `remote_json = NULL`, and reads decode that back to `remote: null`.

#### Lines `22, 43, 56, 69, 89, 111, 134-145` - Canonical Default Model Selection Storage
Replaced the old scalar `default_model` persistence contract with `defaultModelSelection: Schema.NullOr(Schema.fromJsonString(ModelSelection))` and the `default_model_selection_json` column across all write and read queries. The authoritative variable is now `row.defaultModelSelection`, serialized with `row.defaultModelSelection !== null ? JSON.stringify(row.defaultModelSelection) : null`; the old variable it replaced was `row.defaultModel` stored as plain text. This same pass also removed the earlier `ProjectionProjectDbRowSchema` plus `toPersistenceSqlOrDecodeError(...)` wrapper and instead uses `Request: ProjectionProject` / `Result: ProjectionProjectDbRow` with `Effect.mapError(toPersistenceSqlError(...))`, so the repository now assumes the schema-level JSON decoding is the contract boundary. The fallback path remains `NULL` when a project has no default model selection; migration `018_CanonicalizeModelSelections.ts` backfills legacy rows and event payloads by inferring `provider` from `defaultProvider`, from provider-specific option bags, from the old model name heuristics (`%claude%` => `claudeAgent`), or finally `codex`.

#### Lines `25-26, 45-46, 58-59, 71-72, 91-92, 113-114` - Project Git Discovery State Persistence
Added `gitRepos` as `Schema.NullOr(Schema.fromJsonString(Schema.Array(ProjectGitRepo)))` and `gitMode: ProjectGitMode` to `ProjectionProjectDbRow`, then threaded `git_mode` and `git_repos_json` through all project upsert and read queries. The authoritative variables are now `row.gitMode` and `row.gitRepos`; the old upstream contract had neither field, so project-level git discovery state had to be recomputed elsewhere or was unavailable after reload. The write fallback is explicit in this file: `row.gitMode ?? "none"` persists a stable non-null mode even when older callers omit it, and `row.gitRepos !== null && row.gitRepos !== undefined ? JSON.stringify(row.gitRepos) : null` keeps absent discovery results distinct from an actual repo list. On read, the repository returns the stored values directly so downstream snapshot code can decide whether to honor persisted state or re-run discovery.
- Feature:
#### Lines `24, 42, 55, 68, 88, 110` - Remote Project Target Persistence
Changed project row persistence to store the full `ProjectRemoteTarget` object in `remote_json` so Remote SSH Support can treat `(workspaceRoot, remote)` as the authoritative project identity instead of collapsing local and SSH projects that happen to point at the same path. This is part of the project projection storage component.

#### Lines `22, 43, 56, 69, 89, 111, 134-145` - Canonical Default Model Selection Storage
Changed project default-model persistence from a plain model string to the full provider-aware `ModelSelection` object so Extra Customization can preserve provider-specific defaults, option bags, and future provider routing at the project level instead of losing that detail during projection writes. This is part of the project projection storage component.

#### Lines `25-26, 45-46, 58-59, 71-72, 91-92, 113-114` - Project Git Discovery State Persistence
Changed project persistence to store `gitMode` plus the discovered `ProjectGitRepo[]` list so Multi-Repo Support can remember whether a project is `none`, `single`, or `multi` repo and which repo paths were discovered, instead of collapsing back to a single-workspace assumption after every restart. This is part of the project projection storage component.
- Dependency impact:

The old contract it replaced was "project identity is just `workspaceRoot` plus optional UI state." If this drift is wrong, SSH and local projects alias together, remote settings pages can reopen the wrong project, runtime session metadata can bind to the wrong sidebar entry, and project refresh/reconnect flows for SSH-backed workspaces become unreliable.

#### Lines `22, 43, 56, 69, 89, 111, 134-145` - Canonical Default Model Selection Storage

#### Lines `25-26, 45-46, 58-59, 71-72, 91-92, 113-114` - Project Git Discovery State Persistence

If it drifts, `provider-diff:*` checkpoint refs become unreadable after persistence, remote turn diffs disappear after reload, and full-thread or per-turn diff views fall back to missing/empty diffs even though the provider emitted one.

### `apps/server/src/persistence/Migrations/018_CanonicalizeModelSelections.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `7-64`
`0a71c401` rewrites the persisted projection tables from scalar model fields to JSON model-selection fields. Lines `56-64` then drop the old scalar columns `projection_projects.default_model` and `projection_threads.model`. This block rewrites historical `orchestration_events.payload_json` so replayed events match the new `ModelSelection` contract. Lines `66-148` update `project.created` and `project.meta-updated` payloads by replacing `defaultProvider`, `defaultModel`, and `defaultModelOptions` with `defaultModelSelection`. The rewrite handles both `json_type(payload_json, '$.defaultModel') = 'null'` and non-null model cases. In the non-null case, the authoritative JSON patch builds `json_object('provider', ..., 'model', ...)` and then folds in `options` from either a provider-keyed object (`defaultModelOptions.codex` / `.claudeAgent`) or a flat options object. Lines `150-221` do the same for `thread.created`, `thread.meta-updated`, and `thread.turn-start-requested`, replacing `provider`, `model`, and `modelOptions` with `modelSelection`, again preferring provider-keyed option bags when present. The old contract it replaced was "historical event payloads use split scalar fields and optional provider-keyed option bags instead of one canonical `modelSelection` object."

#### Lines `223-234`
This final backfill handles the oldest `thread.created` events that predate even the scalar `model` field. Lines `223-234` run `json_set(payload_json, '$.modelSelection', json(json_object('provider', 'codex', 'model', 'gpt-5.4')))` for `thread.created` rows where both `$.modelSelection` and `$.model` are absent. The authoritative fallback payload introduced here is `{"provider":"codex","model":"gpt-5.4"}`. The old contract it replaced was "very old thread-created events have no model data at all, so replay cannot satisfy the modern thread schema."
- Feature:
#### Lines `7-64`
Changed projected project/thread storage so the persisted model contract becomes a provider-tagged JSON object instead of a loose scalar string, which lets restored projects and threads keep provider identity attached to the chosen model. This supports `Extra Customization` and `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the projection model-selection canonicalization component.

#### Lines `66-221`
Changed historical event payloads so event replay yields the same provider-aware `ModelSelection` objects that fresh writes now emit, rather than relying on decider/projector code to keep supporting legacy `provider` + `model` + `modelOptions` shapes forever. This supports `Extra Customization` and is part of the event-history model-selection canonicalization component.

#### Lines `223-234`
Changed the oldest historical thread-created events to default to one canonical Codex model-selection object so the fork can still replay very early rows into the current thread contract. This supports `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the ancient-event model-selection fallback component.

The fallback path is the SQL inference chain: session `provider_name` wins for threads, then `%claude%` name matching, then `'codex'`; project defaults infer `'claudeAgent'` from `%claude%` or `'codex'` otherwise; and `default_model IS NULL` backfills `default_model_selection_json = NULL`. - Dependency impact:

### `apps/server/src/persistence/Migrations/020_MultiRepoThreadPaths.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `7-20` - Thread Projection Columns for Selected Repo and Per-Repo Arrays
`efd5f211` added three new columns to `projection_threads`: `project_path TEXT` at lines `7-10`, `branch_json TEXT` at lines `12-15`, and `worktree_path_json TEXT` at lines `17-20`. The authoritative persisted fields introduced here are `projection_threads.project_path`, `projection_threads.branch_json`, and `projection_threads.worktree_path_json`, which later hydrate into `row.projectPath`, `row.branch`, and `row.worktreePath` in `apps/server/src/persistence/Layers/ProjectionThreads.ts`. The old contract they replaced was the scalar pair `branch` / `worktree_path`, where one nullable branch and one nullable worktree path were forced to stand in for the entire thread location model. There is no runtime fallback inside this file beyond adding the new nullable columns first and then backfilling them in the later statements.

#### Lines `22-35` - Backfill Existing Thread Rows
The row backfill at lines `22-35` converts existing `projection_threads` rows into the new location contract. `project_path` is set by `COALESCE(worktree_path, (SELECT workspace_root FROM projection_projects ...), '')`, which means the authoritative fallback order is old `worktree_path` first, owning project `workspace_root` second, and `''` only as a last-resort sentinel. The legacy scalar columns are then wrapped into arrays with `branch_json = json_array(branch)` and `worktree_path_json = json_array(worktree_path)`. The old variables this replaces are the scalar `branch` and `worktree_path` columns; after this migration, the authoritative durable values become JSON arrays even for single-repo threads. The important fallback behavior is that a legacy `NULL` branch/worktree becomes `[null]` in the projection row rather than disappearing entirely, preserving slot count for later array updates.

#### Lines `38-82` - Historical `thread.created` Event Canonicalization
Lines `38-82` rewrite `orchestration_events.payload_json` for `event_type = 'thread.created'` so replayed history matches the new thread contract. `payload_json.projectPath` is injected when missing, using the same fallback order as the row backfill: existing `$.worktreePath`, then `projection_projects.workspace_root` for the event’s `$.projectId`, then `''`. The scalar-or-array conversion for `$.branch` and `$.worktreePath` is also made authoritative here: arrays are preserved with `json(json_extract(...))`, while scalars are wrapped with `json(json_array(...))`. The migration also strips `$.updatedAt` with `json_remove(..., '$.updatedAt')`, which removes an obsolete field from replayed thread-created payloads. The old contract this replaces was "historical thread-created events may omit `projectPath` and may carry scalar `branch` / `worktreePath` values." The fallback path is explicit in the `CASE` / `COALESCE` expressions.

#### Lines `84-130` - Historical `thread.meta-updated` Event Canonicalization
Lines `84-130` rewrite `thread.meta-updated` payloads so partial updates also conform to the array-based location contract. `$.projectPath` is injected from existing `$.projectPath`, then `$.worktreePath`, then owning project `workspace_root`. `$.branch` and `$.worktreePath` are normalized into arrays when scalar, but unlike `thread.created`, missing values are written as explicit JSON `null` via `json('null')` so a partial meta-update can still mean "clear this value" rather than "leave the old array shape untouched." The old contract this replaces was meta-update payloads that mixed missing `projectPath`, scalar branch/worktree updates, and nullable single-string values. The authoritative update keys after this migration are `projectPath`, `branch` as array-or-null, and `worktreePath` as array-or-null.
- Feature:
#### Lines `7-20` - Thread Projection Columns for Selected Repo and Per-Repo Arrays
Changed the thread projection schema to persist the selected repo path separately from the per-repo branch/worktree arrays so `Multi-Repo Support` can distinguish "which repo is this thread currently pointed at?" from "what branch/worktree state do we know for each repo in the project?" This is part of the thread-location persistence component.

#### Lines `22-35` - Backfill Existing Thread Rows
Changed the migration backfill logic to normalize every existing thread into the array-based repo-location model so `Multi-Repo Support` can roll forward old single-repo rows without losing the thread’s effective cwd or first repo slot. This is part of the migration backfill component for thread-location state.

#### Lines `38-82` - Historical `thread.created` Event Canonicalization

This is part of the thread-created event canonicalization component.

#### Lines `84-130` - Historical `thread.meta-updated` Event Canonicalization
Changed historical `thread.meta-updated` payloads to preserve per-repo branch/worktree edits and selected-repo changes inside the same canonical array-based thread contract, which `Multi-Repo Support` needs so later branch rename, worktree creation, and repo switching logic all replay into the same shape. Changed the thread-session projection contract to add `providerThreadId` so `Remote SSH Support` can persist the provider-owned thread identifier that reconnect, adoption, and health surfaces need after the in-memory runtime disappears. This is part of the session projection interface component in the remote reconnect chain.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `21-29` - Thread Session Schema Includes Provider Thread Id

### `apps/server/src/projectFaviconRoute.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `98-119` - Project-ID Favicon Resolution
Replaced the old `tryHandleProjectFaviconRequest(url, res)` contract with an object input that requires `url`, `res`, and a resolver callback. The authoritative request key is now `projectId` from `input.url.searchParams`; the old request key it replaced was raw `cwd`. The first remote-aware step was `resolveProjectCwd(projectId)`, and the current contract tightens that further to `resolveProject(projectId) => { workspaceRoot, remote? } | null`. The fallback paths are now explicit and stable: missing `projectId` returns HTTP `400`, an unknown project returns HTTP `404`, and only a resolved local project continues into filesystem favicon scanning.

#### Lines `121-125` - Remote Project Fallback Icon Policy
Added an explicit remote guard: when `project.remote` is truthy, the route now immediately calls `serveFallbackFavicon(input.res)` and returns, instead of trying to stat local files under a cwd. The authoritative variables are `project.remote` and `project.workspaceRoot`; the old contract it replaced was "every project favicon request can probe the local filesystem rooted at the provided cwd." The fallback path is intentional: remote projects always get the inline SVG fallback, while local projects keep the existing ordered search through `FAVICON_CANDIDATES` and `ICON_SOURCE_FILES`.
- Feature:
#### Lines `98-119` - Project-ID Favicon Resolution
Changed favicon routing to resolve through canonical project identity instead of an arbitrary cwd string so Remote SSH Support can keep asset lookup aligned with the same project records the rest of the server and UI use. This is part of the project asset routing component.

#### Lines `121-125` - Remote Project Fallback Icon Policy
Changed favicon serving to fail open for SSH-backed projects by using a deterministic fallback icon rather than attempting unsupported local file access against a remote workspace. This is part of the project asset routing component and supports Remote SSH Support.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `98-119` - Project-ID Favicon Resolution
This subsection depends on `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` supplying `resolveProject(...)` from the projected project list, on the web sidebar constructing `/api/project-favicon?projectId=...` in `apps/web/src/components/Sidebar.tsx`, and on project identity staying consistent with the remote-aware project contracts in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`. If this contract drifts, favicon requests can target the wrong project after refresh, deleted projects can still be queried by stale urls, and sidebar project icons need retesting.

#### Lines `121-125` - Remote Project Fallback Icon Policy
This subsection depends on remote project metadata from `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts`, `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts`, and `apps/server/src/persistence/Layers/ProjectionProjects.ts`, plus the web sidebar and any other UI surface that renders project favicons. If this guard drifts, remote projects can block on local fs lookups, serve broken icons, or accidentally read the wrong local path when a remote project shares a workspace root string with a local project.

### `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/ClaudeAdapter.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `142-173, 392-427, 589-651, 1048-1057, 2476-2767, 2836-3152` - Claude SDK Session Bridge and Canonical Runtime Events
Added a complete `ClaudeAdapterLive` implementation over `@anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk` with provider-owned session state in `ClaudeSessionContext`, provider-native stream control in `ClaudeQueryRuntime`, resume parsing in `readClaudeResumeState(...)`, turn state in `ClaudeTurnState`, and request bookkeeping in `pendingApprovals`, `pendingUserInputs`, and `inFlightTools`. The authoritative variables for Claude session identity are `context.session.threadId`, `context.resumeSessionId`, and `context.session.resumeCursor`, which now carries `threadId`, `resume`, `resumeSessionAt`, and `turnCount`. `startSession(...)` creates the SDK query, stores the context in `sessions`, and emits canonical `session.started`, `session.configured`, `session.state.changed`, and later `thread.started` events; `sendTurn(...)` resolves image attachments via `resolveAttachmentPath({ attachmentsDir, attachment })`, builds an SDK `SDKUserMessage`, allocates a new `TurnId`, and queues the prompt into `context.promptQueue`. The approval contract is also implemented here: `handleAskUserQuestion(...)` turns Claude’s `AskUserQuestion` tool into pending user-input runtime events, `ExitPlanMode` is intercepted and converted into `emitProposedPlanCompleted(...)`, and all other gated tools map through `request.opened` / `request.resolved` with `classifyRequestType(...)` and `summarizeToolRequest(...)`. The old contract this replaces is upstream’s codex-only provider-adapter assumption: there was no Claude-specific session map, no Claude resume cursor parser, and no Claude-to-canonical bridge for approvals, structured user input, or plan capture. The fallback paths are explicit: synthetic Claude thread ids are ignored in `readClaudeResumeState`, unsupported image MIME types raise `ProviderAdapterRequestError`, invalid attachment ids fail the turn start, full-access mode returns `behavior: "allow"` without opening approvals, and global finalization stops sessions with `emitExitEvent: false` so shutdown does not duplicate exit events.

#### Lines `539-559, 2770-2818, 2947-3010` - Provider-Aware Claude Model and Query Configuration
This file no longer treats Claude turns as `input.model` plus `input.modelOptions?.claudeAgent`; the authoritative variable is now `modelSelection = input.modelSelection?.provider === "claudeAgent" ? input.modelSelection : undefined`. `buildPromptText(...)` reads `modelSelection.options?.effort`, `startSession(...)` derives `fastMode`, `thinking`, and `effectiveEffort` from `getModelCapabilities("claudeAgent", modelSelection?.model)`, and both `queryOptions.model` and later `context.query.setModel(...)` come from `modelSelection.model`. It also added `CLAUDE_SETTING_SOURCES = ["user", "project", "local"]`, which is now passed into the SDK as `settingSources: [...CLAUDE_SETTING_SOURCES]` so Claude loads filesystem/project settings consistently. The old contract it replaced was the earlier Claude adapter shape that read scalar `input.model`, provider-specific `input.modelOptions`, and omitted explicit Claude setting-source selection. The fallback path is deliberate: if `input.modelSelection` is absent or not for `claudeAgent`, the adapter leaves model unset, skips Claude-only option extraction, and only changes permission mode when `input.interactionMode` is explicitly `"plan"` or `"default"`.

#### Lines `160-161, 290-368, 1365-1530, 2045-2160` - Context Window and Token Usage Telemetry
Added `lastKnownContextWindow` and `lastKnownTokenUsage` to `ClaudeSessionContext`, introduced `maxClaudeContextWindowFromModelUsage(...)` and `normalizeClaudeTokenUsage(...)`, and emits canonical `thread.token-usage.updated` events from both streaming messages (`task_progress`, `task_notification`) and turn completion. The authoritative telemetry variables are now `context.lastKnownContextWindow`, `context.lastKnownTokenUsage`, and the normalized `ThreadTokenUsageSnapshot` returned from `normalizeClaudeTokenUsage(...)`. `d60b893e` changed the semantics further: `rawUsedTokens` is clamped to `contextWindow` when present, the overflow is preserved as `totalProcessedTokens`, and `compact_boundary` now emits `emitRuntimeWarning(context, "Claude emitted compact_boundary.", ...)` before the thread state change event. The old contract it replaced was "Claude usage totals can be surfaced directly as used tokens and there is no durable context-window-aware usage snapshot between events." The fallback path is explicit: when the SDK provides no valid usage object, no token usage event is emitted; when there is no context window, `usedTokens` stays unbounded; and when there is no prior good usage snapshot, completion falls back to the accumulated SDK usage snapshot.

#### Lines `149-150, 224-238, 1264-1292, 2791-2797, 2863-2889` - Resume/Open Messaging and Thread Resolution Logging
Added `threadOpenMethod` and `requestedResumeThreadId` to `ClaudeSessionContext`, plus `claudeSessionStartedMessage(...)` and `claudeThreadConnectedMessage(...)` helpers. `startSession(...)` now logs `Effect.logInfo("claude thread opening", { threadId, requestedRuntimeMode, requestedModel, requestedCwd, resumeThreadId })`, stores whether the open path was `"start"` or `"resume"`, and emits `session.started.payload.message` describing whether the adapter is starting fresh or attempting resume. When the SDK later resolves the actual provider thread id, the adapter logs `claude thread open resolved` with `threadOpenMethod`, `requestedResumeThreadId`, `resolvedThreadId`, and `requestedRuntimeMode`, and emits `thread.started.payload.message` as either `Connected to thread ...` or `Reconnected to thread ...`. The old contract it replaced was a quieter lifecycle where `session.started` only echoed `resumeCursor`, `thread.started` only carried `providerThreadId`, and there was no structured record of whether the resolved Claude thread came from `thread/start` or `thread/resume`. The fallback path is still present: if no resume thread id was requested, the messages collapse to the start-session wording and `requestedResumeThreadId` is `null`.
- Feature:
#### Lines `142-173, 392-427, 589-651, 1048-1057, 2476-2767, 2836-3152` - Claude SDK Session Bridge and Canonical Runtime Events
Implemented the Claude Agent provider adapter by translating Claude SDK sessions, turns, approvals, and plan/user-input callbacks into the repo’s canonical provider runtime contract. This supports `Claude Integration` and is part of the provider adapter component.

#### Lines `539-559, 2770-2818, 2947-3010` - Provider-Aware Claude Model and Query Configuration

This supports `Extra Customization` and is part of the provider adapter component.

#### Lines `149-150, 224-238, 1264-1292, 2791-2797, 2863-2889` - Resume/Open Messaging and Thread Resolution Logging

### `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/CodexAdapter.ts`

The authoritative shutdown option is now `emitLifecycleEvent: false`, which depends on the manager-side `CodexAppServerStopOptions` contract in `apps/server/src/codexAppServerManager.ts`. The old contract it replaced was "bulk stop always emits the normal `session/closed` lifecycle event for every in-memory Codex session," even when the server is itself shutting down and intends those sessions to be recoverable on restart. The fallback path is deliberately narrow: explicit single-session shutdown still goes through `stopSession(threadId)` and retains normal lifecycle emission; only the adapter’s global stop paths suppress that event.
- Feature:
#### Lines `1339, 1524` - Suppress Synthetic Session-Closed Events During Bulk Stop
Changed Codex bulk shutdown to pass `emitLifecycleEvent: false` so `Debugability and Stability` can distinguish "the local server process is tearing down" from "the provider session was intentionally closed," which keeps resumable Codex sessions eligible for startup recovery instead of poisoning the projection with synthetic closed events. The authoritative flag is now `emitLifecycleEvent: false`; the old behavior it replaced was unconditional lifecycle emission during bulk stop. ### `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/KiroAdapter.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `17-18, 32-67, 78-95, 111-239, 261-285` - Kiro ACP Provider Adapter Surface
Introduced an entire fork-only provider layer that wraps `KiroAcpManager` behind the shared `ProviderAdapterShape`. The authoritative variables are `managerInput.threadId`, `managerInput.runtimeMode`, `managerInput.cwd`, `managerInput.resumeCursor`, `managerInput.binaryPath`, and `managerInput.remote` in `startSession(...)`, plus the turn payload fields `threadId`, `input`, `attachments`, `model`, and `interactionMode` passed to `manager.sendTurn(...)`. Attachment lookup is now resolved through `resolveAttachmentPath({ attachmentsDir: serverConfig.attachmentsDir, attachment })`, and the adapter converts attachment bytes into the ACP payload `{ mimeType, data: Buffer.from(bytes).toString("base64") }`. Runtime failures are normalized through `toSessionError(...)` / `toRequestError(...)`, mapping `"unknown session"` and `"closed"` into `ProviderAdapterSessionNotFoundError` / `ProviderAdapterSessionClosedError` instead of leaking raw ACP errors. The old contract it replaced was "there is no Kiro provider adapter in the registry, so Kiro cannot participate in the provider-service start/turn/approval/runtime-event contract at all." The fallback paths are explicit: if `input.provider` is omitted the adapter still binds to `PROVIDER = "kiro"`; if `cwd`, `resumeCursor`, `providerOptions.kiro.binaryPath`, or `providerOptions.kiro.remote` are absent, the manager starts with its local defaults; if there are no attachments the adapter sends a text-only prompt; and if the UI attempts structured user-input replies, `respondToUserInput(...)` intentionally fails with `ProviderAdapterValidationError` because ACP has no structured answer contract to fall back to.

#### Lines `15, 19-23, 71-77, 241-259` - Native Event NDJSON Logging Hook
`6a65da42` extended `KiroAdapterLiveOptions` with `nativeEventLogPath` and `nativeEventLogger`, instantiated `makeEventNdjsonLogger(..., { stream: "native" })`, and changed the runtime listener so every `ProviderRuntimeEvent` is written through `nativeEventLogger.write(event, event.threadId)` before `Queue.offer(runtimeEventQueue, event)`. The authoritative observability variables are now `options.nativeEventLogger`, `options.nativeEventLogPath`, and the per-event `event.threadId` used as the log partition key. The old contract it replaced was a pure in-memory fanout path where Kiro events only flowed into `runtimeEventQueue` and disappeared if the queue/UI/orchestration consumer misbehaved. The fallback path remains queue-only streaming when no logger or log path is configured.

#### Lines `97-108, 160-178` - Provider-Aware Model Selection and Turn Boundary Preflight
`83a4cb1a` replaced the deprecated `input.model` field with the provider-aware `input.modelSelection?.model` in both `startSession(...)` (line `101`) and `sendTurn(...)` (lines `172-173`), making `modelSelection` the authoritative model contract for Kiro. `b65cc5bb` then inserted `await manager.prepareSessionForTurn({ threadId: input.threadId, interactionMode: input.interactionMode })` at lines `162-167` before `manager.sendTurn(...)`. The old contract it replaced was "KiroAdapter passes model overrides through `input.model` and `sendTurn(...)` can call `manager.sendTurn(...)` directly because `KiroAcpManager.sendTurn(...)` also owns mode/permission-boundary setup." After the ACP fixes in `apps/server/src/kiroAcpManager.ts`, the authoritative preflight contract moved into `prepareSessionForTurn(...)`, which applies the runtime boundary and `session/set_mode` before `session/prompt`. The fallback paths are explicit: if `modelSelection` is absent, Kiro stays on the current/default model; if `interactionMode` is absent, `prepareSessionForTurn(...)` falls back to the manager's `"default"` mode selection; and if the session is already in the correct runtime boundary, the manager-side preflight is a no-op instead of issuing redundant ACP commands.
- Feature:
#### Lines `17-18, 32-67, 78-95, 111-239, 261-285` - Kiro ACP Provider Adapter Surface
Implemented the Kiro ACP provider bridge so `Kiro Integration` can start, resume, interrupt, read, rollback, approve, and stop Kiro sessions through the same provider adapter contract used by Codex and Claude, including remote Kiro launches and attachment-backed prompts. ### `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/ProviderAdapterRegistry.ts`

`f8cf17d4` imported `KiroAdapter` at line `20` and changed the default adapter array at lines `28-31` from `[yield* CodexAdapter, yield* ClaudeAdapter]` to `[yield* CodexAdapter, yield* ClaudeAdapter, yield* KiroAdapter]`. The authoritative registry variable remains the default `adapters` array used when `options.adapters` is undefined; the old contract it replaced was "the registry only knows about Codex and Claude unless a caller manually injects something else." The fallback path is still the override hook `ProviderAdapterRegistryLiveOptions.adapters`, so tests or custom layer assembly can replace the entire default set. There is also a non-behavioral comment drift at line `4` (`codex/cursor/...`) that no longer reflects the actual default provider list.
- Feature:
#### Lines `20, 28-31` - Default Registry Includes Kiro Adapter
Changed the in-memory provider lookup registry to register Kiro by default so `Kiro Integration` becomes a first-class provider anywhere the server resolves adapters by provider kind, instead of existing in code but failing lookup as unsupported. This is part of the provider adapter registry component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `20, 28-31` - Default Registry Includes Kiro Adapter
This sits in the routing chain `ProviderService -> ProviderAdapterRegistry.getByProvider(provider) -> concrete adapter`, so it depends on `apps/server/src/provider/Services/KiroAdapter.ts` and `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/KiroAdapter.ts` being bound in the layer graph, on canonical provider ids in `packages/contracts/src/model.ts` / `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, and on provider availability/config flows that enumerate providers. If this drifts, Kiro can compile but still fail at runtime with `ProviderUnsupportedError`, and the user-visible/runtime flows to retest are provider listing, Kiro thread start, Kiro resume, and any DI overrides that pass a custom `options.adapters` array.

### `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/ProviderHealth.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `31, 68-78, 271-365, 575-680, 702-704` - Kiro CLI Availability and Authentication Probing
Added the fork-only `KIRO_PROVIDER = "kiro"` branch plus a reusable `runCliCommand(binary, args)` helper so health checks can probe `kiro-cli` with the same `CommandResult { stdout, stderr, code }` shape used elsewhere. The authoritative variables are now `runCliCommand("kiro-cli", ["--version"])`, `parseKiroAuthStatusFromOutput(result)`, `isGenericCommandMissingCause("kiro-cli", error)`, and the returned `ServerProviderStatus` fields `status`, `available`, `authStatus`, `checkedAt`, and `message`. `parseKiroAuthStatusFromOutput(...)` also changed the auth contract to look for the first JSON-looking line in `kiro-cli whoami --format json` output, because Kiro may append profile text after the JSON object. The old contract it replaced was "provider health has no Kiro status path and only provider-specific Codex/Claude command wrappers exist," which meant Kiro either looked unsupported or surfaced raw child-process failures. The fallback paths are explicit: if `kiro-cli --version` fails or times out, Kiro is marked unavailable; if the auth probe fails after version succeeds, Kiro remains `available: true` with `authStatus: "unknown"` instead of being hard-disabled; and the generic missing-binary matcher also now drives the Claude not-on-PATH message at lines `702-704` through `isGenericCommandMissingCause("claude", error)`.

#### Lines `28, 295-305, 627-643` - Kiro `whoami` Timeout and Unsupported-Flag Fallback
`7d251263` introduced `KIRO_AUTH_TIMEOUT_MS = 10_000` and `shouldRetryKiroWhoamiWithoutFormat(result)`, then changed the auth probe from a single `runCliCommand("kiro-cli", ["whoami", "--format", "json"])` call to a two-step fallback: try the JSON form first, but if it times out or returns "unknown command"/"unsupported option"/similar output, retry `runCliCommand("kiro-cli", ["whoami"])` without `--format`. The authoritative fallback variable is `shouldRetryWithoutFormat`, computed from `authProbe` before the second probe runs. The old contract it replaced was a single 4-second JSON-only probe, which misclassified older or slower Kiro CLIs as unhealthy/unknown. The fallback path is now explicit in code: plain `whoami` becomes the secondary auth source, and both probes share the longer `KIRO_AUTH_TIMEOUT_MS` budget.

#### Lines `33-41, 781-795` - Resolved Health Snapshot Logging
`d64d85e6` added `logProviderHealthStatus(status)` and changed `ProviderHealthLive` from returning a lazily joined fiber effect each time `getStatuses` is called to eagerly collecting `statuses = yield* Effect.all([Fiber.join(codexStatusFiber), Fiber.join(claudeStatusFiber), Fiber.join(kiroStatusFiber)])`, logging each resolved status once, and then exposing `getStatuses: Effect.succeed(statuses)`. The authoritative variables are the materialized `statuses` array and each `status.provider/status.available/status.status/status.authStatus/status.message` field logged through `Effect.logInfo(...)`. The old contract it replaced was "health probes are joined on demand with no structured record of the final resolved statuses." The fallback path is simply the cached snapshot itself: once the layer boots, subsequent readers get the same resolved status array without rerunning probes.
- Feature:
#### Lines `31, 68-78, 271-365, 575-680, 702-704` - Kiro CLI Availability and Authentication Probing
Implemented a dedicated Kiro CLI health/status probe, including resilient `kiro-cli whoami` parsing and generic binary-missing detection, so `Kiro Integration` can tell the difference between "Kiro is unavailable", "Kiro is installed but unauthenticated", and "Kiro is reachable but auth state is unclear" during server bootstrap. This is part of the provider health component.

#### Lines `28, 295-305, 627-643` - Kiro `whoami` Timeout and Unsupported-Flag Fallback
Changed the Kiro auth probe to fall back from `whoami --format json` to plain `whoami` so `Debugability and Stability` does not mark slow or older Kiro installs as broken when they only reject the JSON flag or need more time to answer. This is part of the provider health component.

#### Lines `33-41, 781-795` - Resolved Health Snapshot Logging
Changed provider health startup to materialize and log the resolved provider-status snapshot so `Debugability and Stability` has a stable, inspectable record of what the server believed about Codex, Claude, and Kiro at boot. This is part of the provider health snapshot and logging component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `31, 68-78, 271-365, 575-680, 702-704` - Kiro CLI Availability and Authentication Probing
This feeds the server config/bootstrap health snapshot consumed by provider-selection UI and availability banners, so it depends on the local `kiro-cli` binary, the shared `ServerProviderStatus` contract in `@t3tools/contracts`, and the config/web surfaces that render provider availability (`server.getConfig`, provider health banners, provider pickers, settings). No persistence tables are changed here, but if the contract drifts the UI can incorrectly hide Kiro, mark it healthy when login is missing, or misclassify missing binaries as auth failures. Retest cold start with Kiro absent, Kiro installed but logged out, Kiro installed and logged in, and Claude missing from PATH to confirm the generic missing-command path still produces the correct message.

#### Lines `28, 295-305, 627-643` - Kiro `whoami` Timeout and Unsupported-Flag Fallback
This depends on Kiro CLI command-line compatibility rather than any local schema, but it directly affects the `ServerProviderStatus.message/authStatus` values that drive provider availability UX and operator diagnosis. If it regresses, Kiro can flap between unknown and unavailable on startup, especially on older CLI builds, so retest slow startup, unsupported `--format` output, and the warning-path copy shown in the UI.

#### Lines `33-41, 781-795` - Resolved Health Snapshot Logging
This depends on server bootstrap ordering, the provider-health layer being created once per process, and any logs/operators that diagnose bootstrap failures. It also changes when `getStatuses` resolves from "join fibers now" to "return cached snapshot now", which affects any consumer expecting deterministic one-time startup health. No persistence fields are involved, but if this drifts you lose the log breadcrumb that ties UI provider availability back to a concrete boot-time decision. Retest startup logs, repeated `getStatuses` calls, and config/bootstrap flows that read provider health after the server is already running.

### `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/ProviderService.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `99-143, 207-225, 313-323, 459-507, 538-555` - Persisted Provider-Aware Model Selection and Resume-Cursor Reuse
`0a71c401` replaced the old loose `modelOptions` runtime-payload contract with the canonical `ModelSelection` schema. The authoritative variables are now `extra.modelSelection` in `toRuntimePayloadFromSession(...)`, `readPersistedModelSelection(...)`, `persistedModelSelection`, `input.modelSelection`, and `input.modelSelection?.model` in analytics. `startSession(...)` also now computes `effectiveResumeCursor = input.resumeCursor ?? persistedBinding.resumeCursor` when the persisted binding belongs to the same provider, so a thread can restart without the caller explicitly resending the cursor. `sendTurn(...)` writes `modelSelection` back into the directory runtime payload each turn at line `544`, instead of only tracking `activeTurnId` and last runtime event. The old contract it replaced was "persist opaque `modelOptions`, require the caller to resupply any resume cursor, and let follow-up turns lose the canonical provider/model selection choice." The fallback paths are explicit: if the persisted binding belongs to a different provider, `effectiveResumeCursor` is ignored; if `modelSelection` is absent or fails `Schema.is(ModelSelection)`, the adapter gets no model override and falls back to its current/default model; and if the caller does pass an explicit `resumeCursor`, it still wins over the persisted one.

#### Lines `39-42, 108-115, 247-456, 680-700` - Remote Reconnect Metadata, Recovery Strategies, and Recoverable Thread Inspection
`47dcf0c0` wired `ProviderService` into `buildRemoteSessionRuntimeMetadataPatch(...)` and `readProviderThreadIdFromResumeCursor(...)`, making `providerThreadId`, `resumeAvailable`, `reconnectState`, `reconnectSummary`, and `reconnectUpdatedAt` durable runtime-payload fields. `recoverSessionForThread(...)` now has explicit recovery branches: `adopt-existing` when the adapter already has a live session for the thread, `resume-unavailable` when no persisted cursor exists, `resume-thread` when the adapter resumes successfully, and `resume-failed` when resume throws. `7d034cc6` then propagated `recovered: boolean` through `resolveRoutableSession(...)` and added `inspectRecoverableThread(...)`, which recovers the thread if needed, returns the active `session`, reads the provider `threadSnapshot`, and tells startup reconciliation whether the service had to reopen the provider session. The current code also adds a Kiro-specific fallback inside `Effect.catchTags(...)`: `ProviderAdapterSessionNotFoundError` and `ProviderAdapterSessionClosedError` now trigger `startFreshAfterResumeUnavailable()` for provider `"kiro"`, yielding strategy `"resume-fallback-fresh-start"` and reconnect state `"fresh-start"` instead of hard-failing. The old contract it replaced was "recovery either reuses a live session or blindly tries `startSession(resumeCursor)` with no durable reconnect-state metadata and no inspectable post-recovery thread snapshot." The fallback paths are explicit in code: active in-memory sessions are adopted, no cursor becomes `resume-unavailable`, Kiro can fall back to a fresh session when ACP resume is gone, and any other resume failure is persisted as `resume-failed`.

#### Lines `146-167, 728-759` - Remote-Aware `stopAll` State Preservation
`6a21989b` added `hasPersistedRemoteTarget(runtimePayload)`, which inspects `providerOptions.codex.remote.kind === "ssh"` inside the persisted binding to decide whether the thread is backed by a remote SSH session. `runStopAll()` no longer does a blind `directory.getProvider(threadId)` + `status: "stopped"` write for every thread. Instead it loads the full binding, preserves `provider`, `runtimeMode`, and `resumeCursor`, and only forces `status: "stopped"` plus `activeTurnId: null` for non-remote sessions. For remote bindings it leaves the status unset, clears `lastError`, sets `lastRuntimeEvent = "provider.stopAll"` / `lastRuntimeEventAt = stoppedAt`, and explicitly nulls `reconnectState`, `reconnectSummary`, and `reconnectUpdatedAt` so shutdown does not create misleading reconnect noise. The old contract it replaced was "global stop marks every persisted binding stopped and surfaces a reconnect summary even for reconnectable remote threads." The fallback path is the local-session branch: non-remote bindings still become stopped and clear their active turn immediately.
- Feature:
#### Lines `99-143, 207-225, 313-323, 459-507, 538-555` - Persisted Provider-Aware Model Selection and Resume-Cursor Reuse
Changed provider-session persistence to store and restore the canonical `modelSelection` contract, plus same-provider resume cursors, so `Extra Customization` keeps per-thread provider/model choices and resumes across restarts instead of dropping back to provider defaults. This is part of the thread-session model-selection and resume-binding component.

#### Lines `39-42, 108-115, 247-456, 680-700` - Remote Reconnect Metadata, Recovery Strategies, and Recoverable Thread Inspection
Changed provider recovery to persist `providerThreadId` and reconnect-state metadata, and to expose `inspectRecoverableThread(...)`, so `Remote SSH Support` can reattach or diagnose persisted remote provider sessions across restarts while `Kiro Integration` can degrade to a fresh ACP session when resume is no longer possible. This is part of the thread-session reconnect metadata and startup-recovery component.

#### Lines `146-167, 728-759` - Remote-Aware `stopAll` State Preservation
Changed provider-service bulk shutdown to preserve reconnectable remote bindings while clearing stale reconnect summaries so `Remote SSH Support` survives local app shutdown without the session model pretending the remote thread was irrecoverably stopped. This is part of the provider service stop-all and remote thread-management component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `99-143, 207-225, 313-323, 459-507, 538-555` - Persisted Provider-Aware Model Selection and Resume-Cursor Reuse
This depends on `@t3tools/contracts` `ModelSelection`, all provider adapters consuming `input.modelSelection`, `ProviderSessionDirectory` runtime payload storage, and the web-side model-selection flows that expect a thread to reopen with the same provider/model/options (`apps/web/src/modelSelection.ts`, composer/provider pickers, thread restore paths). No new SQL columns are introduced here, but the runtime payload keys `modelSelection` and `resumeCursor` become authoritative for restart behavior. Retest model switching, fast/reasoning options, refresh/reopen of an active thread, provider changes on an existing thread, and first-turn versus subsequent-turn model persistence.

#### Lines `39-42, 108-115, 247-456, 680-700` - Remote Reconnect Metadata, Recovery Strategies, and Recoverable Thread Inspection
This depends on `apps/server/src/provider/remoteSessionMetadata.ts`, `ProviderSessionDirectory` bindings, `apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/StartupThreadReconciler.ts`, and the orchestration/web session projections that render `providerThreadId`, `resumeAvailable`, `reconnectState`, `reconnectSummary`, and `reconnectUpdatedAt`. The user-visible/runtime flows tied to this chain are remote session banners, startup thread reconciliation, reconnect diagnostics after refresh/restart, and Kiro resume behavior when ACP has forgotten the session. If this drifts, remote threads can lose their provider-thread mapping, startup recovery can stop completing or resuming disconnected turns correctly, Kiro can hard-fail instead of reopening, and the reconnect-status UI becomes misleading. Retest remote thread restart/reload, disconnected startup recovery, inspect-recoverable-thread reads, Kiro resume-unavailable fallback, and recovery when approvals or user-input requests were pending.

#### Lines `146-167, 728-759` - Remote-Aware `stopAll` State Preservation
This depends on `providerOptions.codex.remote` being persisted in the binding runtime payload, `ProviderSessionDirectory` retaining `resumeCursor` and `runtimeMode`, and the remote reconnect metadata readers that interpret shutdown state (`remoteSessionMetadata.ts`, orchestration session snapshots, remote banners). If this contract drifts, a normal app shutdown can turn remote threads into local "stopped" dead ends or leave stale reconnect copy in the UI. Retest server shutdown, restart of remote SSH threads, local-thread stop-all behavior, and any UI surface that distinguishes reconnectable remote sessions from locally stopped sessions.

### `apps/server/src/provider/remoteSessionMetadata.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `35-50` - Canonical Provider Thread Id Extraction
`47dcf0c0` introduced `PersistedRemoteSessionMetadata` plus `readProviderThreadIdFromResumeCursor(...)`, which now treats `resumeCursor.threadId` as the canonical provider-owned thread identifier when the resume cursor is an object. The authoritative runtime-payload key introduced by this helper is `providerThreadId`; the old contract it replaced was ad hoc inference of backend thread identity from loosely shaped `resumeCursor` payloads scattered across provider/orchestration code. The fallback path is explicit: non-object cursors return `undefined`, empty strings are trimmed away, and callers can still omit `providerThreadId` entirely when no backend thread id is available.

#### Lines `52-118` - Runtime-Payload Builder and Parser for Reconnect State
The main fork contract in this file is the pair `buildRemoteSessionRuntimeMetadataPatch(...)` and `readPersistedRemoteSessionMetadata(...)`. The authoritative runtime-payload keys are now `activeTurnId`, `lastError`, `providerThreadId`, `resumeAvailable`, `reconnectState`, `reconnectSummary`, and `reconnectUpdatedAt`. `buildRemoteSessionRuntimeMetadataPatch(...)` prefers an explicit `input.providerThreadId`, then falls back to `input.session.resumeCursor.threadId`; it normalizes `reconnectSummary`, infers `resumeAvailable` from `input.session.resumeCursor !== undefined` when not explicitly provided, and falls back for `reconnectUpdatedAt` from explicit input to `session.updatedAt` to `new Date().toISOString()`. `readPersistedRemoteSessionMetadata(...)` is the inverse validator: it only accepts reconnect states in `RECONNECT_STATE_VALUES`, preserves explicit `null` for `activeTurnId` and `lastError`, ignores malformed strings or timestamps, and returns `{}` for non-object payloads. The old contract it replaced was ad hoc read/write logic spread across provider and orchestration code with no single validator for reconnect metadata keys or fallback order.
- Feature:
#### Lines `35-50` - Canonical Provider Thread Id Extraction
Changed remote session metadata handling to centralize how the fork extracts the backend provider thread id so `Remote SSH Support` can keep reconnect/adoption logic keyed to one canonical provider-thread field instead of re-parsing resume cursors differently in different layers. This is part of the provider session metadata component.

#### Lines `52-118` - Runtime-Payload Builder and Parser for Reconnect State
Implemented a single runtime-payload parser/builder for reconnect metadata so `Remote SSH Support` and `Debugability and Stability` can consistently surface provider thread ids, resume availability, reconnect strategy (`fresh-start`, `adopt-existing`, `resume-thread`, `resume-unavailable`, `resume-failed`), and reconnect timestamps across persistence, recovery, and UI projection layers. This is part of the provider session metadata component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `35-50` - Canonical Provider Thread Id Extraction

If it drifts, reconnect banners and recovery logic can refer to the wrong backend thread or lose the id entirely. Retest persisted remote sessions, startup recovery, and any UI that displays provider thread identity.

#### Lines `52-118` - Runtime-Payload Builder and Parser for Reconnect State
This helper sits on the contract chain `apps/server/src/provider/Layers/ProviderService.ts -> ProviderSessionDirectory runtimePayload -> apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProjectionSnapshotQuery.ts / apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/StartupThreadReconciler.ts / apps/server/src/orchestration/Layers/ProviderCommandReactor.ts -> apps/web/src/store.ts` and related remote-session banner UI. The authoritative persisted keys are the seven runtime-payload fields above; the older contract it replaced was "each layer reads and writes reconnect metadata on its own." If this drifts, provider-thread ids can disappear, reconnect state can deserialize inconsistently, invalid timestamps can leak into projections, and startup/session projections can disagree about whether a session is recoverable. ### `apps/server/src/remote/validateRemoteProject.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `9-49` - Remote Validation Shell Contract
`f2ebfbee` introduced a dedicated SSH validation script builder with three authoritative framing constants: `REMOTE_PROJECT_VALIDATION_SENTINEL = "__T3_REMOTE_PROJECT_VALIDATE__"`, `REMOTE_PROJECT_VALIDATION_TIMEOUT_MS = 10_000`, and `REMOTE_PROJECT_VALIDATION_OUTPUT_FIELDS = 7`. `buildRemoteProjectValidationScript(...)` expands `~` / `~/`, verifies the path exists and is a directory, `cd`s into it, resolves `pwd -P`, and emits a NUL-delimited payload with exactly seven fields: `workspaceRoot`, `directoryName`, `hostname`, `gitAvailable`, `gitRepositoryRoot`, `codexCliAvailable`, and `codexCliVersion`. The old contract it replaced was "accept the remote host/path input optimistically and discover path or tooling problems later during project creation or provider launch." The fallback paths are built into the script: missing `git` and missing `codex` do not fail validation and instead return `gitAvailable = 0` / `codexCliAvailable = 0`; empty `directory_name` falls back to `resolved_path`; and path existence/type failures exit with typed codes `10`, `11`, or `12`.

#### Lines `56-117` - Output Parsing and Typed Failure Mapping
`parseRemoteProjectValidationOutput(...)` and `describeRemoteValidationFailure(...)` define the inverse contract for the SSH script. Parsing now uses `stdout.lastIndexOf(REMOTE_PROJECT_VALIDATION_SENTINEL)` so SSH banners or MOTD noise before the sentinel are ignored, then slices exactly `REMOTE_PROJECT_VALIDATION_OUTPUT_FIELDS` NUL-delimited values. `normalizeOptionalValue(...)` trims string fields into `string | null`; `workspaceRoot` is required and throws if empty; `directoryName` falls back to `workspaceRoot`; and `gitAvailable` / `codexCliAvailable` are decoded from `"1"` flags. Failure mapping translates exit codes `10`, `11`, and `12` into path-specific user-facing errors, while all other failures surface trimmed `stderr` or `"SSH validation failed."` The old contract it replaced was generic SSH/process failure handling with no stable parser for noisy output and no typed mapping from remote path failures to UI-safe messages.

#### Lines `119-150` - SSH Execution Wrapper and Timeout Policy
`validateRemoteProjectOverSsh(...)` became the single execution entry point. It runs `ssh` through `runProcess(...)` with `buildSshExecArgs(...)`, `allowNonZeroExit: true`, `outputMode: "truncate"`, and `timeoutMs = REMOTE_PROJECT_VALIDATION_TIMEOUT_MS`, then either throws `describeRemoteValidationFailure(...)` or returns `parseRemoteProjectValidationOutput(result.stdout)`. The authoritative runtime variables are `input.remote.hostAlias`, `input.workspaceRoot`, `options.localCwd ?? process.cwd()`, and the `runProcess` result fields `timedOut`, `code`, `stdout`, and `stderr`. The old contract it replaced was direct optimistic remote project creation with no dedicated validation RPC. The fallback path is explicit: `localCwd` defaults to `process.cwd()` when the caller does not supply one.
- Feature:
#### Lines `9-49` - Remote Validation Shell Contract
Implemented a remote shell preflight that resolves the actual workspace path and probes Git/Codex availability before the project record is created so `Remote SSH Support` can reject bad host/path combinations early and store the canonical remote workspace root. This is part of the remote project onboarding component.

#### Lines `56-117` - Output Parsing and Typed Failure Mapping
Changed remote validation parsing and error translation so `Remote SSH Support` can distinguish invalid path input from generic SSH transport failures and can survive noisy SSH login output without losing the real validation payload. This is part of the remote project onboarding component.

#### Lines `119-150` - SSH Execution Wrapper and Timeout Policy
Implemented a dedicated SSH validation RPC/workflow entry point so `Remote SSH Support` validates the host/path combination before creating the project and before later remote git/terminal/provider flows assume the workspace is reachable and canonical. This is part of the remote project onboarding component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `9-49` - Remote Validation Shell Contract
This depends on `quotePosixShell(...)` and `buildSshExecArgs(...)` in `apps/server/src/sshCommand.ts`, plus the UI/server contracts that consume `workspaceRoot`, `directoryName`, `hostname`, `gitRepositoryRoot`, and `codexCliVersion`. If the field order, sentinel, or exit-code meanings drift, onboarding and subsequent remote routing can misread the validation result. Retest remote add-project with `~`, nested repo paths, non-directory paths, and hosts where Git or Codex is not installed.

#### Lines `56-117` - Output Parsing and Typed Failure Mapping
This depends on `RemoteProjectValidationResult` in `packages/contracts/src/remote.ts` / the shared contracts package, on the Sidebar/UI that surfaces validation errors, and on downstream code assuming the parsed fields are already normalized. If this drifts, remote project creation can accept malformed output, mis-handle login banners, or show useless generic errors for simple path mistakes. Retest noisy SSH banner cases, empty-hostname cases, and each path-specific failure mode.

#### Lines `119-150` - SSH Execution Wrapper and Timeout Policy
This sits on the onboarding chain `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts serverValidateRemoteProject -> validateRemoteProjectOverSsh(...) -> apps/web/src/components/Sidebar.tsx` and then feeds the stored remote project record plus later remote session/project setup. No persistence tables are changed here directly, but the returned validation payload shapes what the UI shows and what downstream remote session routing assumes is true. If this drifts, remote add-project can accept nonexistent paths, mis-handle `~` expansion, lose repo-root detection, or break on SSH banner noise. Retest remote add-project end to end, especially with custom `localCwd`, missing Git, missing Codex, and slow SSH responses.

### `apps/server/src/serverLayers.ts`

- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `11, 24, 79-90` - Kiro Provider Layer Wiring
`makeServerProviderLayer()` now imports `makeKiroAdapterLive` at line `24`, constructs `kiroAdapterLayer` at lines `79-81`, and injects it into `ProviderAdapterRegistryLive` at line `85` alongside Codex and Claude. The authoritative composition variables are `nativeEventLogger`, `kiroAdapterLayer`, and the `adapterRegistryLayer` pipeline that provides all concrete adapters before `makeProviderServiceLive(...)` is layered. The old contract it replaced was "the server provider layer only instantiates Codex and Claude adapters," which left the Kiro codepath present in source but unreachable from the runtime layer graph. #### Lines `11, 104-117` - Projection Turn Repository for Checkpoint Diff Query

The authoritative dependency chain is `CheckpointDiffQueryLive -> ProjectionTurnRepositoryLive -> projection_turns.checkpoint_diff_text`, replacing the old contract where checkpoint diff queries only depended on snapshot/query state plus `CheckpointStoreLive`. This wiring is required because forked `CheckpointDiffQueryLive` can short-circuit provider-diff checkpoints by reading persisted `checkpointDiff` text from the turn repository instead of reconstructing a filesystem diff from checkpoint refs. The fallback path remains the upstream store-backed diff path when the checkpoint ref is not a `provider-diff:` ref or no persisted `checkpointDiff` exists.

#### Lines `20, 129-133` - Startup Thread Reconciler Bootstrap
`StartupThreadReconcilerLive` is imported at line `20` and provided into `OrchestrationReactorLive` at line `133` via `StartupThreadReconcilerLive.pipe(Layer.provideMerge(runtimeServicesLayer))`. The authoritative bootstrap contract is now "orchestration reactor startup includes the reconciler service in the same runtime-services graph as ingestion, command reaction, checkpoint reaction, and projection snapshot access." The old contract it replaced was a reactor stack with no startup recovery worker, so stale running threads were left untouched after process restart. The fallback path is limited to normal live event ingestion; without this layer, only new runtime activity can repair thread state.

#### Lines `11, 24, 79-90` - Kiro Provider Layer Wiring
Changed server provider composition so `Kiro Integration` is actually instantiated and registered in the live Effect graph, with the same native-event logging path as the other providers. This is part of the server composition component.

#### Lines `20, 129-133` - Startup Thread Reconciler Bootstrap
