### `apps/server/src/sshCommand.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `8-95, 120-173` - Shared SSH Command and Remote PATH Bootstrap
Added a fork-only SSH execution helper that centralizes four authoritative primitives: `quotePosixShell(...)` at lines `26-28`, `buildSshShellInvocation(...)` at lines `30-32`, `readRemoteEnvironmentFromLoginShell(...)` at lines `34-72`, and `buildSshExecArgs(...)` at lines `148-173`. `readRemoteEnvironmentFromLoginShell(...)` shells into `ssh -T <hostAlias> sh -lc 'shell_bin=${SHELL:-/bin/sh}; exec "$shell_bin" -ilc ...'`, captures named environment variables via `buildEnvironmentCaptureCommand(...)` / `extractEnvironmentFromShellOutput(...)`, and returns `{}` on any spawn error or non-zero status instead of failing the caller. `readRemotePathEnv(...)` then caches the remote `PATH` under the authoritative key `${hostAlias}\0${localCwd}` for `REMOTE_PATH_ENV_CACHE_TTL_MS = 15_000`, and `buildRemoteExecCommand(...)` prepends `cd`, `export PATH=...`, and any caller-supplied env vars before `exec`ing the quoted command/args. The old contract it replaced was repeated ad hoc SSH argument and quoting logic in each remote-aware subsystem. The fallback path is explicit: if login-shell env capture fails, `buildSshExecArgs(...)` omits `pathEnv` entirely and still returns a valid `ssh -T <hostAlias> sh -lc ...` invocation.

#### Lines `18-24, 97-117` - Remote HOME Discovery for Worktree Prep
`0b6e734c` added `remoteHomeEnvCache` and `readRemoteHomeDir(...)`, mirroring the PATH cache but specifically capturing `HOME` from the remote login shell. The authoritative variables are `remoteHomeEnvCache`, the same cache key `${hostAlias}\0${localCwd}`, and the returned trimmed `HOME` value or `undefined`. The old contract it replaced was "only remote PATH is discoverable from the shared SSH helper," which forced remote worktree prep to guess or reconstruct home-relative paths elsewhere. The fallback path is the same as PATH capture: if login-shell env capture fails or `HOME` is empty, callers receive `undefined` and must choose their own fallback behavior.
- Feature:
#### Lines `8-95, 120-173` - Shared SSH Command and Remote PATH Bootstrap
Implemented a shared remote command builder that bootstraps the remote login-shell `PATH`, quotes every command/arg/env assignment consistently, and emits one canonical SSH invocation shape so `Remote SSH Support` can run git, terminal, workspace, validation, and provider-side commands against the same remote execution contract. This is part of the SSH execution component.

#### Lines `18-24, 97-117` - Remote HOME Discovery for Worktree Prep
Changed the shared SSH helper to resolve remote `HOME` so `Remote SSH Support` can create and clean up SSH-backed worktree paths relative to the actual remote user home directory instead of assuming a local-style path layout. This is part of the SSH execution component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `8-95, 120-173` - Shared SSH Command and Remote PATH Bootstrap
This helper is used by `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitCore.ts`, `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitHubCli.ts`, `apps/server/src/git/projectRepos.ts`, `apps/server/src/terminal/Layers/Manager.ts`, `apps/server/src/workspaceEntries.ts`, `apps/server/src/remote/validateRemoteProject.ts`, `apps/server/src/kiroAcpManager.ts`, and `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts`. Notably, `apps/server/src/codexAppServerManager.ts` still carries its own remote shell builder, so changes here do not automatically update remote Codex launch behavior. If this contract drifts, retest remote git commands, remote terminals, workspace entry enumeration, SSH project validation, Kiro remote launch, and any WebSocket handler that shells out over SSH.

#### Lines `18-24, 97-117` - Remote HOME Discovery for Worktree Prep
This is consumed by `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitCore.ts` and `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` for remote worktree prep and synthetic path handling. If it regresses, SSH worktree creation/removal can target the wrong base directory or fail only on hosts whose home path is not inferable from the workspace path. Retest remote worktree creation, cleanup, and any flow that synthesizes SSH worktree parents under the remote home directory.

### `apps/server/src/sshHosts.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `19-101` - SSH Config Path, Quote, and Glob Expansion Helpers
`84e0f5b7` added the helper layer that makes SSH config discovery deterministic: `GLOB_META_PATTERN`, `WILDCARD_HOST_PATTERN`, `stripQuotes(...)`, `splitDirectiveArguments(...)`, `parsePort(...)`, `isConcreteHostAlias(...)`, `expandHomePath(...)`, `wildcardSegmentToRegExp(...)`, and `expandGlobPattern(...)`. The authoritative parsing decisions are now: quoted directive values are stripped, ports that are non-numeric or `<= 0` become `null`, host aliases containing `*`, `?`, or `!` are rejected as non-concrete, `~` and `~/...` are expanded against `homeDir`, and `Include` glob patterns are expanded manually through `expandGlobPattern(...)`. The old contract it replaced was "there is no server-side SSH config parsing at all," so none of these normalization rules existed in the product. The fallback paths are explicit: non-glob paths are returned as-is, unreadable directories inside glob expansion are skipped with `readdir(...).catch(() => [])`, and malformed ports never throw.

#### Lines `104-198` - Recursive `ssh_config` Parser with First-Wins Precedence
`parseSshConfigFile(...)` is the core parser contract. It resolves `filePath`, tracks `visitedFiles` to avoid include loops, treats missing files as empty via the `ENOENT -> null` fallback, lowercases directives, processes `Include` recursively relative to the including file, and opens a new alias set on each `Host` directive. Within a `Host` block, only concrete aliases are recorded, and the first seen `HostName`, `User`, and `Port` win because assignments only happen while `existing.hostname`, `existing.user`, or `existing.port` are still `null`. The authoritative per-record fields are `alias`, `hostname`, `user`, `port`, and `sourcePath`. The old contract it replaced was "there is no server-owned source of SSH host metadata." The fallback behavior is explicit: if a config file is absent, parsing stops quietly; directives outside a `Host` block are ignored; and duplicate aliases across included files keep the first discovered values.

#### Lines `200-222` - Stable Host Listing Surface
`listSshHosts(options)` is the exported server contract. It defaults `homeDir` to `os.homedir()`, `configPath` to `~/.ssh/config`, parses into a `Map<string, SshHostRecord>`, sorts by `alias`, and returns `SshHostSummary { alias, hostname, user, port, sourcePath }`. The authoritative API surface is now this sorted `SshHostSummary[]`; the old contract it replaced was "there is no server-side SSH host listing endpoint, so the UI must rely on manual host entry." The fallback path is an empty array when the config tree is absent or contains no concrete hosts.
- Feature:
#### Lines `19-101` - SSH Config Path, Quote, and Glob Expansion Helpers
Implemented the normalization layer needed for SSH config discovery so `Remote SSH Support` can consume real OpenSSH config files, including quoted values, `Include` paths, and wildcard filtering, instead of forcing manual host entry. This is part of the SSH configuration component.

#### Lines `104-198` - Recursive `ssh_config` Parser with First-Wins Precedence
Changed host discovery to parse the real OpenSSH config graph, including `Include` chains and per-host defaults, so `Remote SSH Support` can populate a host picker from the same host aliases users already rely on in their shell config. This is part of the SSH configuration component.

#### Lines `200-222` - Stable Host Listing Surface
Implemented a stable SSH host listing API so `Remote SSH Support` can drive a real host picker from local OpenSSH configuration instead of forcing every remote project to be typed from scratch. This is part of the SSH configuration component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `19-101` - SSH Config Path, Quote, and Glob Expansion Helpers
These helpers feed `parseSshConfigFile(...)` and therefore every downstream host listing surface. If any of the normalization rules drift, the UI can show invalid aliases, mis-parse quoted `HostName` or `User` values, or miss included config files. Retest globbed includes, quoted directive values, invalid `Port` directives, and wildcard `Host` entries.

#### Lines `104-198` - Recursive `ssh_config` Parser with First-Wins Precedence
This depends on the on-disk SSH config tree and on the product assuming first-wins precedence for duplicate host metadata. It feeds `listSshHosts()` and ultimately the remote project add flow. If this drifts, included hosts can disappear, duplicate aliases can override in the wrong direction, or source-file attribution can point at the wrong config file. Retest duplicate aliases, nested includes, missing include targets, and configs that mix wildcard and concrete `Host` blocks.

#### Lines `200-222` - Stable Host Listing Surface
This depends on the `SshHostSummary` contract in `@t3tools/contracts` and is consumed by `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` (`server.listSshHosts`), `apps/web/src/wsNativeApi.ts`, `apps/web/src/lib/serverReactQuery.ts`, and the remote add-project flow in `apps/web/src/components/Sidebar.tsx`. If this contract drifts, the UI can miss hosts, surface wildcard aliases that cannot actually be selected, or lose source-file attribution needed for debugging config precedence. Retest end-to-end host listing in the remote add-project flow after changes to sorting, field names, or parser precedence.

### `apps/server/src/terminal/Layers/Manager.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `44-54, 498-510` - Remote-Aware Session Identity
`0ae86206` replaced the decode path for open/restart with `TerminalOpenExecutionInputSchema` and `TerminalRestartExecutionInputSchema`, each extending the terminal input contract with optional `remote: ProjectRemoteTarget`. The same change set added `normalizeRemoteTarget(...)` and `remoteTargetsEqual(...)`, making `TerminalSessionState.remote` the authoritative routing field and treating two remote targets as the same session only when both `kind` and `hostAlias` match. The old contract it replaced was "terminal session identity is just local `cwd` plus env/dimensions." The fallback path remains `remote ?? null`, so local callers still normalize into the original local-terminal behavior.

#### Lines `564-767` - Open/Restart Retargeting and History Reset
Open and restart now both thread `input.remote` through session resolution. `assertValidCwd(input.cwd, input.remote)` runs before attach, newly created sessions persist `remote`, and an existing session is torn down and its history cleared when any of `cwd`, normalized `runtimeEnv`, or `remote` changes. The authoritative retarget fields are now `input.cwd`, `normalizeRuntimeEnv(input.env)`, and `normalizeRemoteTarget(input.remote)`. The old contract it replaced was "session reuse depends only on local cwd plus env," which meant switching a reused terminal id from local to SSH or from one SSH host to another could keep the old PTY attached.

#### Lines `823-897` - Remote PTY Launch via SSH
`startSession(...)` now forks on `session.remote`. For remote sessions it spawns `ssh` using `buildSshExecArgs({ hostAlias, command: candidate.shell, args, cwd: session.cwd, env: session.runtimeEnv, localCwd: process.cwd() })`; local sessions keep the original PTY spawn path. This also changes which environment is authoritative: local PTYs still use `createTerminalSpawnEnv(process.env, session.runtimeEnv)`, while remote PTYs only use sanitized local env for the SSH client and pass `session.runtimeEnv` inside the SSH command so the variables are applied on the remote shell instead of leaking into the local client process. The old contract it replaced was "all terminals are local PTYs and env overrides are always applied to the local child process."

#### Lines `1337-1363` - Remote `cwd` Validation
The old local-only `fs.promises.stat(cwd)` guard was replaced with an SSH-side `test -d` probe when `remote.kind === "ssh"`, surfacing `Remote terminal cwd does not exist: <host>:<cwd>` if the remote path is wrong. The authoritative validation branch is now `assertValidCwd(cwd, remote)`, which decides whether to check the local filesystem or ask the remote host. The fallback path is explicit: local cwd validation still uses `fs.promises.stat`, and `remote ?? null` keeps local behavior.
- Feature:
#### Lines `44-54, 498-510` - Remote-Aware Session Identity
Changed terminal session identity so `Remote SSH Support` treats one terminal id on `host-a` as different from the same terminal id on `host-b` or on the local machine, rather than reusing the wrong PTY because the `cwd` string happens to match. This is part of the terminal manager runtime component.

#### Lines `564-767` - Open/Restart Retargeting and History Reset
Changed terminal open/restart reuse rules so `Remote SSH Support` can hard-retarget a terminal when the execution machine changes, instead of preserving the old shell and mixing local/remote history together. This is part of the terminal manager runtime component.

#### Lines `823-897` - Remote PTY Launch via SSH
Changed terminal process launch so `Remote SSH Support` starts an SSH-backed shell with remote cwd and remote env overrides, instead of trying to model a remote shell as a local PTY. This is part of the terminal manager runtime component.

#### Lines `1337-1363` - Remote `cwd` Validation
Changed terminal cwd validation so `Remote SSH Support` fails early with a host-aware path error when the remote directory is wrong, rather than surfacing a generic local spawn failure or incorrectly validating the path on the local machine. This is part of the terminal manager runtime component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `44-54, 498-510` - Remote-Aware Session Identity
This depends on the widened service contract in `apps/server/src/terminal/Services/Manager.ts`, the `ProjectRemoteTarget` contract in `packages/contracts/src/project.ts`, and the WS/native API callers that now pass remote project context. If it drifts, terminals can silently attach to the wrong machine or preserve history/state across a host switch.

#### Lines `564-767` - Open/Restart Retargeting and History Reset
This depends on WS/native API terminal open/restart payloads from `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts` and the web terminal UX. If this drifts, remote terminal open/restart can land on a local shell, same-id terminals can incorrectly reuse a PTY after switching hosts, and history can survive across what should have been a full retarget. Retest local terminal open/restart, SSH terminal open/restart, switching one terminal id between local and remote, and switching between two SSH hosts.

#### Lines `823-897` - Remote PTY Launch via SSH
This depends on `apps/server/src/sshCommand.ts`, shell resolution, and the runtime env contract from the service layer. If this drifts, remote env overrides get dropped or applied to the wrong machine, and remote shells can start in the wrong directory or under the wrong shell invocation. Retest SSH terminal spawn, env overrides, shell selection, and resize/write after reconnect.

#### Lines `1337-1363` - Remote `cwd` Validation
This depends on `runProcess(...)`, `buildSshExecArgs(...)`, and the remote project routing from `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts`. If it drifts, invalid remote directories get reported as generic spawn errors or slip through until the shell fails later. Retest invalid remote directories, valid remote directories, and local cwd validation unchanged.

### `apps/server/src/workspaceEntries.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `49-60` - Remote-Aware Cache Key and Path Normalization
`0ae86206` introduced `normalizeWorkspaceRelativePath(...)` and `workspaceCacheKey(...)`. The authoritative cache identity is no longer plain `cwd`; for SSH projects it is now `ssh:${input.remote.hostAlias}:${input.cwd}`, and returned relative paths are normalized by stripping leading `./` and leading `/` before ranking or caching. The old contract it replaced was "workspace search results are keyed only by local cwd and git/find output is trusted as-is." The fallback path is explicit: when `remote` is absent, the cache key remains local and normalization still produces plain relative paths.

#### Lines `264-306` - Single Execution Path for Local and SSH Workspace Commands
`runWorkspaceProcess(...)` became the authoritative command runner for workspace indexing. Local calls still use `runProcess(input.command, input.args, { cwd: input.cwd, ... })`, but SSH calls now shell out through `ssh` using `buildSshExecArgs({ hostAlias, command, args, cwd, localCwd: process.cwd() })`. The old contract it replaced was a purely local process runner path. The fallback path is still the original local `runProcess(...)` branch whenever `input.remote` is absent.

#### Lines `308-550` - Remote Git Indexing and Non-Git `find` Fallback
Optional `remote` is now threaded through `isInsideGitWorkTree(...)`, `filterGitIgnoredPaths(...)`, and `buildWorkspaceIndexFromGit(...)`, so `git rev-parse`, `git check-ignore`, and `git ls-files` all run against the remote project when `remote.kind === "ssh"`. The fork also adds the remote-only non-git fallback `buildRemoteWorkspaceIndex(...)`: if git indexing cannot produce an index for an SSH workspace, it enumerates directories and files with `find . -mindepth 1 -type d|f -print0`, deduplicates and sorts them, and throws `Unable to scan remote workspace entries at '<host>:<cwd>'` if the remote scan fails entirely. The old fallback it replaced was local-only `fs.readdir(...)` recursion, which cannot see a remote filesystem. The fallback paths are explicit: local workspaces still use the upstream filesystem walk, git-ignore chunk failures still return the original `relativePaths`, and remote projects prefer git-based indexing first and only fall back to `find` when git discovery is unavailable.

#### Lines `690-718` - Search Input Contract and Cache/Dedupe Scope
`searchWorkspaceEntries(...)` now takes local `WorkspaceEntrySearchInput { cwd, remote?, query, limit }` instead of the upstream `ProjectSearchEntriesInput`, and `getWorkspaceIndex(...)` / `clearWorkspaceIndexCache(...)` both key cache and in-flight dedupe by `{ cwd, remote }`. The authoritative search target is now `input.remote` plus `input.cwd`, not just a browser-supplied cwd string. The old contract it replaced was project search keyed purely by local cwd. The fallback path is unchanged local behavior when `remote` is absent.
- Feature:
#### Lines `49-60` - Remote-Aware Cache Key and Path Normalization
Changed workspace search caching and path normalization so `Remote SSH Support` can distinguish `/repo` on the local machine from `/repo` on `ssh:prod`, and can keep mention insertion stable even when the remote shell emits `./foo.ts` or `/foo.ts`. This is part of the workspace entry indexing component.

#### Lines `264-306` - Single Execution Path for Local and SSH Workspace Commands
Changed workspace indexing execution so `Remote SSH Support` can run discovery commands against the remote filesystem instead of accidentally inspecting the same path on the local machine. This is part of the workspace entry indexing component.

#### Lines `308-550` - Remote Git Indexing and Non-Git `find` Fallback
Changed workspace indexing so `Remote SSH Support` can reuse git-aware indexing on the remote host when available, but still return entries for non-git remote directories through a remote `find` fallback instead of returning nothing. This is part of the workspace entry indexing component.

#### Lines `690-718` - Search Input Contract and Cache/Dedupe Scope
Changed workspace search routing so `Remote SSH Support` scopes indexing and invalidation by both path and host, which is what keeps remote mention search, cache invalidation after turn completion, and local-vs-remote reuse from fighting each other. This is part of the workspace entry indexing component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `49-60` - Remote-Aware Cache Key and Path Normalization
This affects cache identity and result formatting consumed by `projects.searchEntries`, `apps/web/src/wsNativeApi.ts`, and composer/path-mention UI. If it drifts, identical `cwd` strings on different hosts can contaminate each other’s cache, and inserted path mentions can carry the wrong prefix.

#### Lines `264-306` - Single Execution Path for Local and SSH Workspace Commands
This depends on `apps/server/src/sshCommand.ts` and `apps/server/src/processRunner.ts`. If it drifts, remote search silently falls back to the local filesystem or fails to respect host-specific cwd context. Retest local and SSH workspace searches against the same path string.

#### Lines `308-550` - Remote Git Indexing and Non-Git `find` Fallback
This depends on remote command execution, `.gitignore` filtering, and the `ProjectEntry` shape consumed by the composer/path-mention flows. If it drifts, `.gitignore` filtering can stop matching remote results, or non-git remote workspaces can return nothing because the `find` fallback no longer maps into `ProjectEntry`. #### Lines `690-718` - Search Input Contract and Cache/Dedupe Scope
This is called by `projects.searchEntries` in `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts`, then by `apps/web/src/wsNativeApi.ts` and the web mention/search flows that consume `ProjectEntry[]`. If it drifts, cache invalidation after turn completion can clear the wrong host, remote project search can silently fall back to the wrong workspace, and mention insertion can resolve against stale entries. Retest local search, SSH search, cache invalidation after turn completion, and composer `@path` insertion.

### `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `161-272, 655-752, 866-959, 1390-1447` - Project-Scoped Path, Editor, Favicon, and Attachment Routing
Lines `161-198` rename the old `resolveWorkspaceWritePath(...)` helper into `resolveWorkspaceRelativePath(...)` and make `label` plus `allowWorkspaceRoot` explicit inputs, so `"."` can be a valid resolved target and error messages can say `Project path` / `Workspace file path` instead of one generic string. Lines `201-235` add a separate `resolveRemoteWorkspaceRelativePath(...)` path that uses `nodePath.posix` instead of local `path`, which becomes the authoritative resolver whenever `project.remote?.kind === "ssh"`. Lines `238-272` replace the old global attachment-path contract built around `ATTACHMENTS_ROUTE_PREFIX`, `normalizeAttachmentRelativePath(...)`, and `resolveAttachmentRelativePath(...)` with `PROJECT_THREAD_ATTACHMENT_ROUTE_PARTS` and `parseProjectThreadAttachmentPath(...)`, so attachment URLs are now expected to be `/api/projects/<projectId>/threads/<threadId>/attachments/<attachmentId>`. Lines `655-752` then enforce that contract at request time: the server loads the projection snapshot, confirms the project exists, confirms the thread belongs to that project, confirms `thread.messages[].attachments[].id` actually contains the requested attachment id, and only then resolves the file with `resolveAttachmentPathById(...)`. The old contract it replaced was "a global attachment id or relative path can be fetched without proving project/thread ownership." Lines `662-677` also change `tryHandleProjectFaviconRequest(...)` so favicon lookup resolves project metadata from the projection snapshot and passes both `workspaceRoot` and optional `remote`, instead of assuming a purely local project root. Lines `892-959` add `resolveProjectPathBase(...)` and `resolveProjectEditorTarget(...)`; the authoritative base path is now `thread.projectPath` when a `threadId` is supplied, not always `project.workspaceRoot`, and remote editor targets are returned as structured `{ kind: "remote-ssh", hostAlias, path, isDirectory, line?, column? }` objects instead of local `"/abs/path:line:column"` strings. Lines `1390-1447` wire those helpers into `projectsWriteFile`, `projectsOpenInEditor`, and `projectsOpenPathInEditor`. `projectsWriteFile` now deliberately calls `resolveLocalProjectWorkspaceRoot(...)`, so remote projects fail closed for server-side writes instead of writing to a guessed local path. The fallback paths are explicit: local editor/file resolution still uses the original `path`-based resolver, `relativePath ?? "."` opens the project or thread root, and invalid attachment/project/thread combinations return `404`.

#### Lines `432-474, 1681-1702` - Remote Project Onboarding and SSH Validation
Lines `432-474` widen `normalizeProjectWorkspaceRoot(...)` from a single `workspaceRoot: string` input into `{ workspaceRoot, remote }`. For local projects, the old contract remains in place: `expandHomePath(...)`, `path.resolve(...)`, and `fileSystem.stat(...)` still canonicalize and verify the directory. For SSH projects, the authoritative value is now `input.workspaceRoot.trim()` and the server explicitly skips local filesystem resolution and stat checks. The old contract it replaced was "every `project.create` and `project.meta.update` workspace root is a local path that must exist on this machine." Lines `1681-1688` add `WS_METHODS.serverListSshHosts`, which returns `{ hosts: await listSshHosts() }`, and lines `1690-1702` add `WS_METHODS.serverValidateRemoteProject`, which calls `validateRemoteProjectOverSsh(body, { localCwd: cwd })`. The fallback paths are also explicit: local project create/update still resolve and validate locally, SSH host listing wraps failures in `Failed to list SSH hosts: ...`, and remote validation surfaces the validator’s own message instead of collapsing everything into a generic transport error.

#### Lines `308-356, 568-652, 1743-1748` - Desktop Runtime Control and Route Error Formatting
Lines `308-319` add `formatRouteFailureMessage(...)`, which squashes the Effect cause and prefers `Error.message` before falling back to `Cause.pretty(...)`; lines `321-330` add `hasAuthorizedDesktopRequest(...)`; lines `332-356` add `readJsonRequestBody(...)` with a hard `16 * 1024` byte limit. Lines `568-652` then introduce `/api/desktop/runtime`. `GET` returns `{ ok: true, mode: serverConfig.mode, pid: process.pid }`. `POST` accepts an `action` field and supports exactly two commands: `"stop-local-sessions"` and `"shutdown-server"`. For `"stop-local-sessions"`, the authoritative filter is `project.remote == null` plus `thread.session !== null` and `thread.session.status !== "stopped"`, so only active local threads are stopped; the route dispatches `thread.session.stop` commands with fresh `commandId`s and returns `stoppedThreadIds`. For `"shutdown-server"`, the server responds first and then sends itself `SIGTERM`. The old contract it replaced was "there is no authenticated HTTP control surface for the desktop app, and WS route failures are reported as raw `Cause.pretty(...)` dumps." Lines `1743-1748` complete the change by switching WS request failures to `error: { message: formatRouteFailureMessage(result.cause) }`. The fallback paths are explicit: if `authToken` is unset the desktop route is open, token mismatch yields `401`, invalid JSON yields `400`, unsupported actions yield `400`, and unsupported methods yield `405`.

#### Lines `866-993, 1372-1388, 1454-1662` - Project-Aware Workspace, Git, and Terminal Routing
Lines `866-993` add `resolveProject(...)`, `resolveThread(...)`, `resolveProjectRemote(...)`, and `resolveGitOperationTarget(...)`, making persisted project state the authoritative source for routing rather than whatever `cwd` the browser sends. `resolveGitOperationTarget(...)` now derives `{ cwd, remote }` from `body.repoPath` plus optional `body.projectId`; the old contract it replaced was "forward the request body and trust the caller-provided cwd/local repo path." Lines `1372-1388` use that same project lookup for workspace search: `projectsSearchEntries` no longer calls `searchWorkspaceEntries(body)`, but instead loads the project and calls `searchWorkspaceEntries({ cwd: project.workspaceRoot, remote: project.remote ?? null, query, limit })`. Lines `1454-1629` fan that routing through every git method: `gitStatus`, `gitPull`, `gitRunStackedAction`, `gitResolvePullRequest`, `gitPreparePullRequestThread`, `gitListBranches`, `gitCreateWorktree`, `gitRemoveWorktree`, `gitCreateBranch`, `gitCheckout`, and `gitInit` all replace body-level cwd forwarding with resolved `{ cwd, remote }`, and `gitPull` now calls `git.pullCurrentBranch(cwd, remote)` directly. Lines `1632-1662` do the same for the terminal contract: `terminalOpen` and `terminalRestart` inject `remote` from `resolveProjectRemote(body.projectId)` before invoking the terminal manager. The fallback path is still explicit: when `projectId` is omitted, `resolveGitOperationTarget(...)` returns `{ cwd: repoPath, remote: null }`, preserving local ad hoc repo operations; terminal write/resize/clear/close remain unchanged.

#### Lines `995-1227, 1292-1303, 1543-1618` - Multi-Repo Worktree Synthesis and Bootstrap Thread Shape
Lines `995-1014` add `resolveProjectRepoRelativePath(...)`, which maps an absolute `body.repoPath` back to the persisted `repo.repoPath` inside `project.gitRepos`; that relative repo path is now the authoritative identifier for multi-repo worktree prep. Lines `1016-1214` add `resolveSyntheticParentPath(...)`, `ensureLocalSyntheticParentExtras(...)`, `ensureRemoteSyntheticParentExtras(...)`, and `ensureSyntheticParentExtras(...)`. Before `gitCreateWorktree`, the server now checks whether the target project is `gitMode === "multi"`, whether the requested repo exists in `project.gitRepos`, computes the synthetic parent directory above the nested repo path, and copies non-repo-root siblings from `project.workspaceRoot` into that synthetic parent. Local projects do this with `fs.mkdir(...)`, `fs.readdir(...)`, and `fs.cp(...)`; SSH projects do it with `readRemoteHomeDir(...)`, `quotePosixShell(...)`, `buildSshExecArgs(...)`, and an inline `sh -lc` copy script. The old contract it replaced was "create the worktree directly inside the selected repo and assume the surrounding project skeleton does not matter." Lines `1543-1565` wire that prep into `WS_METHODS.gitCreateWorktree`, and lines `1612-1618` add a new failure path for `gitInit`: multi-repo projects now fail with `Git init is unavailable for multi-repo projects.` instead of pretending a project-wide init still makes sense. Lines `1292-1303` also change the welcome bootstrap thread defaults from scalar `branch: null` and `worktreePath: null` to `projectPath: existingProject?.workspaceRoot ?? cwd`, `branch: [null]`, and `worktreePath: [null]`. The old bootstrap contract it replaced was "a thread has one implicit branch/worktree slot and no explicit `projectPath`." The fallback paths are explicit: worktree synthesis is a no-op when `projectId`, `requestedWorktreePath`, or a matching repo path is missing, and it is skipped entirely for non-multi projects.
- Feature:
#### Lines `161-272, 655-752, 866-959, 1390-1447` - Project-Scoped Path, Editor, Favicon, and Attachment Routing
Changed server-side file, editor, favicon, and attachment routing so the authoritative path base is `thread.projectPath` when a thread is pinned to a specific repo/worktree, remote opens use structured `remote-ssh` targets, and attachment bytes are only served after verifying project-thread ownership in the read model. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the project-scoped transport component.

#### Lines `432-474, 1681-1702` - Remote Project Onboarding and SSH Validation
Changed project create/update normalization and added SSH host discovery plus remote preflight validation so remote projects persist the remote `workspaceRoot` verbatim, can be selected from the local SSH config, and can be rejected before storage if the host alias, remote path, git repo, or Codex CLI contract is wrong. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and is part of the remote onboarding transport component.

#### Lines `308-356, 568-652, 1743-1748` - Desktop Runtime Control and Route Error Formatting
Changed the server transport to expose an authenticated desktop runtime endpoint and cleaner route-failure messages, so the desktop app can inspect backend mode, stop only local sessions on close, and shut down the detached backend without killing SSH-backed work or surfacing unreadable Effect causes. This supports `Debugability and Stability` and `Extra Customization` and is part of the desktop runtime control component.

#### Lines `866-993, 1372-1388, 1454-1662` - Project-Aware Workspace, Git, and Terminal Routing
Changed request normalization so workspace search, git operations, and terminal open/restart are routed by persisted project identity, `body.repoPath`, and `project.remote` instead of a naked cwd from the browser. That is what keeps a repo path attached to the correct SSH host, keeps search scoped to the project root, and makes terminal sessions inherit the project’s remote target automatically. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and is part of the transport routing component.

#### Lines `995-1227, 1292-1303, 1543-1618` - Multi-Repo Worktree Synthesis and Bootstrap Thread Shape
Changed worktree creation and default thread bootstrap so multi-repo projects carry repo-relative identity, preserve shared non-repo files in synthetic worktree parents, and start new threads with explicit `projectPath` plus array-shaped branch/worktree state. That is the contract that keeps thread-to-project-to-repo mapping stable when one project contains several repos and several worktree slots. This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the thread-session-project-turn mapping and worktree synthesis component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `161-272, 655-752, 866-959, 1390-1447` - Project-Scoped Path, Editor, Favicon, and Attachment Routing
This subsection depends on `apps/server/src/open.ts`, `apps/server/src/projectFaviconRoute.ts`, `apps/server/src/attachmentStore.ts`, the projection snapshot contract in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, and the web-side consumers that build editor/attachment URLs such as `apps/web/src/projectEditorTargets.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/ChatMarkdown.tsx`, `apps/web/src/terminal-links.ts`, and `apps/web/src/store.ts`. If it drifts, the first breakages are thread-relative links opening against the project root instead of `thread.projectPath`, remote editor launches degrading back to local path strings, attachment preview URLs bypassing project/thread scoping, remote project favicons resolving against the wrong machine, and write-file flows targeting the wrong root. Retest project-root open, thread-relative open inside a non-root repo/worktree, remote editor open, remote write-file rejection, favicon lookup for local and SSH projects, and attachment previews for valid, missing, and cross-thread attachment ids.

#### Lines `432-474, 1681-1702` - Remote Project Onboarding and SSH Validation
This subsection depends on `apps/server/src/sshHosts.ts`, `apps/server/src/remote/validateRemoteProject.ts`, the WebSocket/native API method definitions in `packages/contracts/src/ws.ts`, project create/update orchestration commands in `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, and the web onboarding flows that call these methods through `apps/web/src/wsNativeApi.ts` and React Query wrappers. If it drifts, SSH projects can be normalized as bogus local paths, host pickers can go empty, validation errors lose the signal needed to debug the remote environment, and remote project edits can silently persist unusable roots. Retest SSH host listing, remote validation success/failure, remote project creation, remote project edit, bad host aliases, bad remote paths, and local project creation unchanged.

#### Lines `308-356, 568-652, 1743-1748` - Desktop Runtime Control and Route Error Formatting
This subsection depends on detached-backend lifecycle handling in `apps/server/src/main.ts`, the Electron bridge in `apps/desktop/src/preload.ts`, and the web settings/root flows that trigger close-behavior sync. If it drifts, desktop close actions can stop remote sessions by mistake, shutdown can fail to reach the detached backend, auth-token checks can block legitimate desktop calls, and transport errors become too opaque to diagnose. Retest desktop runtime `GET`, authenticated `POST stop-local-sessions` with a mix of local and remote projects, `POST shutdown-server`, and WS route failures from invalid project ids or bad remote validation input.

#### Lines `866-993, 1372-1388, 1454-1662` - Project-Aware Workspace, Git, and Terminal Routing
This subsection depends on `apps/server/src/workspaceEntries.ts`, `apps/server/src/terminal/Services/Manager.ts`, `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitManager.ts`, `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitCore.ts`, `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitHubCli.ts`, and the request/response contracts in `packages/contracts/src/git.ts`, `packages/contracts/src/terminal.ts`, and `packages/contracts/src/ws.ts`. If it drifts, remote git commands can run against the local filesystem, search entries can point at the wrong workspace, terminal open/restart can attach to the wrong machine, and progress events can still stream while mutating the wrong repo. Retest project search entries, local and SSH git status/pull, stacked git actions with progress, PR resolution, branch listing/checkout, git init on local projects, and terminal open/restart on local and SSH projects.

#### Lines `995-1227, 1292-1303, 1543-1618` - Multi-Repo Worktree Synthesis and Bootstrap Thread Shape
This subsection depends on multi-repo discovery in `apps/server/src/git/projectRepos.ts`, remote home and SSH shell helpers in `apps/server/src/sshCommand.ts`, git worktree operations in `apps/server/src/git/Layers/GitCore.ts`, and the projected thread shape consumed by `apps/web/src/store.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbar.tsx`, and other repo-selection UI. If it drifts, worktrees created from nested repos lose sibling project files, remote synthetic parents land under the wrong home/root, bootstrap threads start with the wrong repo-slot shape, and the branch/worktree UI stops matching the actual repo layout. Retest multi-repo worktree create/remove on local and SSH projects, nested repo path resolution, welcome bootstrap thread creation, repo selection after refresh, and git init rejection for multi-repo projects.

### `apps/server/vitest.config.ts`

#### Lines `8-11` - Server Test Timeout and Worker Cap
`cb8bb598` changed the server Vitest override block from `testTimeout: 15_000` / `hookTimeout: 15_000` to `testTimeout: 30_000` / `hookTimeout: 30_000`, and added `maxWorkers: 4`. The authoritative runner limits are now `30_000` ms for both tests and hooks with worker parallelism capped at `4`; the old contract it replaced was the shorter `15_000` ms timeouts with no server-local worker cap beyond whatever the root config provided. There is no fallback path inside this file beyond the shared `../../vitest.config` for settings not overridden here.

#### Lines `8-11` - Server Test Timeout and Worker Cap

If it drifts, the symptom is flaky or timing-sensitive tests rather than runtime behavior. ### `apps/web/src/appSettings.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `52-96, 170-376` - Host-Scoped Provider Launch Overrides
Lines `52-78` replace the older small set of global binary-path settings with `SettingsPathSchema`, `CodexHostOverrideSchema`, `ClaudeHostOverrideSchema`, and `KiroHostOverrideSchema`. The authoritative persisted override fields are now `codexRemoteOverrides`, `claudeRemoteOverrides`, `kiroRemoteOverrides`, plus local fallbacks `codexBinaryPath`, `codexHomePath`, `claudeBinaryPath`, and `kiroBinaryPath`. Lines `80-96` add those remote-override records to `AppSettingsSchema`; the old contract they replaced was "settings only persist one local `codexBinaryPath`, one local `codexHomePath`, and one local `claudeBinaryPath` for the entire app." Lines `170-309` then add `getCodexHostOverride(...)`, `buildCodexHostOverridePatch(...)`, `getClaudeHostOverride(...)`, `buildClaudeHostOverridePatch(...)`, `getKiroHostOverride(...)`, and `buildKiroHostOverridePatch(...)`. The authoritative routing input is `hostAlias`; when it is missing the helpers read and update the local top-level fields, and when it is present they read and update only the corresponding remote override record. Empty override objects are pruned by deleting the map entry instead of persisting blank records. Lines `333-376` widen `getProviderStartOptions(...)` so it now takes `hostAlias?: string | null`, resolves provider settings through those helper functions, and emits `ProviderStartOptions` for `claudeAgent`, `codex`, and `kiro`. The old contract it replaced was `getProviderStartOptions(settings)` with only local Codex/Claude fields and no Kiro provider branch. The fallback paths are explicit: missing `hostAlias` uses local settings, missing remote overrides fall back to empty defaults, and `getProviderStartOptions(...)` still returns `undefined` when every provider override is empty.

#### Lines `32-50, 101-106, 139-167, 311-330` - Git Defaults and Canonical Text-Generation Model Selection
Lines `32-39` add `GIT_DEFAULT_ACTION_OPTIONS` and `DEFAULT_GIT_DEFAULT_ACTION`, making `gitDefaultAction` a first-class persisted setting instead of an implicit UI-only choice. Lines `47-50` define `DEFAULT_GIT_TEXT_GENERATION_MODEL_SELECTION`, and lines `101-106` add `gitDefaultAction`, `gitCommitPrompt`, and `gitHubBinaryPath` to `AppSettingsSchema`. Lines `139-154` expand the stored custom-model lists with `customKiroModels` and keep `textGenerationModelSelection` under the shared `ModelSelection` schema. Lines `160-167` change `normalizeAppSettings(...)` so it no longer just slug-normalizes `customCodexModels` and `customClaudeModels`; the authoritative model resolution step is now `resolveAppModelSelectionState(settings)`, which rewrites `textGenerationModelSelection` against the currently valid custom model lists for Codex, Claude, and Kiro. The old contract it replaced was "persist whatever `textGenerationModelSelection` says and normalize only some provider model slug lists." Lines `311-330` add `buildGitRequestSettings(...)`, which trims `gitHubBinaryPath` and `gitCommitPrompt`, drops empty strings, and emits canonical `GitRequestSettings { githubBinaryPath?, commitPrompt?, textGenerationModelSelection }`. The fallback paths are explicit: blank GitHub binary path and commit prompt are omitted from the request, and when the stored model selection is invalid or incomplete `resolveAppModelSelectionState(...)` falls back to the default Codex git text-generation model.

#### Lines `18-45, 97-138, 378-401` - General Persisted App Preferences
Lines `18-45` export `APP_SETTINGS_STORAGE_KEY` and replace schema-literal value types with exported option arrays such as `TIMESTAMP_FORMAT_OPTIONS`, `SIDEBAR_PROJECT_SORT_ORDER_OPTIONS`, `SIDEBAR_THREAD_SORT_ORDER_OPTIONS`, `THREAD_ID_DISPLAY_MODE_OPTIONS`, and `DEFAULT_DESKTOP_APP_CLOSE_BEHAVIOR`. Lines `97-138` then rebuild the schema defaults explicitly with `Schema.withConstructorDefault(...)` and `Schema.withDecodingDefault(...)` instead of the old shared `withDefaults(...)` helper. The authoritative preference fields here are `defaultThreadEnvMode`, `confirmThreadDelete`, `diffWordWrap`, `enableAssistantStreaming`, `sidebarProjectSortOrder`, `sidebarThreadSortOrder`, `desktopAppCloseBehavior`, `threadIdDisplayMode`, and `timestampFormat`. The old contract it replaced was a smaller schema that imported `EnvMode` from `BranchToolbar.logic`, did not expose option arrays for settings UIs, and did not include desktop close behavior, thread-id display mode, sidebar sort orders, or diff word-wrap as first-class settings. Lines `378-401` keep `useAppSettings()` as the authoritative read/write hook, but now every update is normalized through the expanded schema and `normalizeAppSettings(...)`. The fallback path is the schema itself: missing or invalid persisted fields decode back to the explicit defaults declared here, so older localStorage values still hydrate into a complete settings object.
- Feature:
#### Lines `52-96, 170-376` - Host-Scoped Provider Launch Overrides
Changed the browser settings contract so provider launch configuration is keyed by SSH host when needed, with `hostAlias` deciding whether Codex, Claude, or Kiro should use local binaries/home paths or per-host remote overrides. That is what lets one machine launch different provider binaries for local work versus a specific SSH project without forking the UI state model. This supports `Remote SSH Support`, `Kiro Integration`, and `Extra Customization` and is part of the provider launch settings component.

#### Lines `32-50, 101-106, 139-167, 311-330` - Git Defaults and Canonical Text-Generation Model Selection

That keeps git text generation aligned with the same provider/model selection rules the rest of the app uses. ### `apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbar.logic.ts`

#### Lines `1-15` - Shared Remote-Aware Env-Mode Resolution

The fallback path lives in `resolveEffectiveThreadEnvMode(...)`, which still resolves to local behavior when `projectRemote` is absent.

This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the branch toolbar state component.

### `apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbar.tsx`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `24-230` - Repo-Indexed Branch and Worktree State
Lines `24-44` add `deriveMultiRepoProjectPathFromChildWorktreePath(...)`, which walks back up from a repo-local `childWorktreePath` using the selected `repoPath` segments to recover the parent `projectPath`. Lines `46-65` widen `BranchToolbarProps` with `projectRemote`, `selectedRepoPath`, `onSelectedRepoPathChange`, and `providerThreadId`. Lines `75-108` then make the toolbar state repo-aware: `isMultiRepo`, `gitRepos`, `selectedRepoIndex`, and `resolvedSelectedRepoIndex` become the authoritative selectors; for multi-repo threads `activeThreadBranch` and `activeWorktreePath` now read `serverThread?.branch[index]` / `worktreePath[index]` instead of a single scalar field, while single-repo threads fall back through `getSingleRepoBranch(...)` and `getSingleRepoWorktreePath(...)`. The old contract it replaced was "one toolbar manages one scalar `branch` and one scalar `worktreePath`." Lines `117-230` push that repo-indexed contract through writes as well: `setThreadBranch(...)` now builds `nextBranch` and `nextWorktreePath` arrays, computes `nextProjectPath`, sends `thread.meta.update` with `projectPath`, `branch`, and `worktreePath` arrays, and updates local draft state with `branchIndex` plus `projectPath`. The old contract it replaced was a scalar `thread.meta.update` branch/worktree patch with no repo index and no `projectPath` recalculation. The fallback path remains explicit: when the project is not multi-repo, the toolbar still behaves like the old single-repo flow and treats `projectPath` as `worktreePath ?? activeProjectRoot`.

#### Lines `109-115, 236-323` - Remote Env Gating, Repo Picker, and Provider Thread Visibility
Lines `109-115` change effective env-mode handling so `resolveEffectiveEnvMode(...)` now receives `projectRemote`, and `supportsDraftWorktreeEnv({ projectRemote })` becomes the authoritative gate for whether the user may choose `"worktree"` at all. The old contract it replaced was "show the env-mode selector whenever the toolbar is not locked and there is no active worktree," even for SSH projects where worktree-mode drafting is not supported. Lines `236-323` then change the rendered surface: the left side now shows the env-mode control or a forced `Local`/`Worktree` badge based on `supportsWorktreeEnv`, renders `providerThreadId` when available, and the right side adds a repo selector for `gitRepos` in multi-repo projects. `BranchToolbarBranchSelector` now also receives `activeProjectId`, which is required for project-scoped git queries. The fallback paths are explicit: if `providerThreadId` is absent the debug label disappears, if `gitRepos.length === 0` the repo selector is not shown, and if worktree env is unsupported the toolbar falls back to the non-interactive badge instead of rendering a broken mode picker.
- Feature:
#### Lines `24-230` - Repo-Indexed Branch and Worktree State
Changed the branch toolbar so branch/worktree edits are applied to the selected repo slot, `projectPath` is recomputed from the selected repo’s worktree path, and single-repo threads still flow through shared helpers instead of the array path. This is what keeps one thread’s branch/worktree state aligned with the correct repo inside a multi-repo project. This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the branch/worktree state component.

#### Lines `109-115, 236-323` - Remote Env Gating, Repo Picker, and Provider Thread Visibility
Changed the toolbar surface so SSH-backed projects do not advertise unsupported draft worktree mode, multi-repo projects expose an explicit repo picker, and provider-backed threads can show the current `providerThreadId` inline for diagnostics. This supports `Remote SSH Support`, `Multi-Repo Support`, and `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the branch toolbar presentation component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `24-230` - Repo-Indexed Branch and Worktree State
This subsection depends on the array-shaped thread fields in `apps/web/src/store.ts`, shared single-repo helpers in `@t3tools/shared/threadGit`, thread meta updates sent through the native API, and any server-side consumer of `projectPath`, `branch[]`, and `worktreePath[]`. If it drifts, switching repos can overwrite the wrong branch slot, `projectPath` can point at the wrong worktree parent, session restarts can happen against the wrong cwd, and draft-thread branch changes can stop matching the selected repo. Retest branch/worktree changes in single-repo threads, multi-repo repo switching, switching a repo into and out of a worktree, and refreshing after a `thread.meta.update`.

#### Lines `109-115, 236-323` - Remote Env Gating, Repo Picker, and Provider Thread Visibility
This subsection depends on `apps/web/src/threadEnvMode.ts`, selected-repo state owned by chat/store layers, provider-thread metadata projected into the client store, and [`BranchToolbarBranchSelector.tsx`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbarBranchSelector.tsx). If it drifts, remote projects can expose a worktree-mode toggle that the backend cannot honor, repo switching can stop driving branch queries, and provider thread ids can disappear from the only toolbar surface that exposes them. Retest the env-mode picker on local versus SSH projects, repo selection in multi-repo projects, provider thread id display, and branch selector queries after changing the selected repo.

### `apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbarBranchSelector.tsx`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `44-112` - Project-Scoped Branch Query Identity
`b200dc0b` added `activeProjectId: ProjectId` to the selector props and changed the authoritative query identity from a bare `branchCwd` string to `gitTarget = { repoPath: branchCwd, projectId: activeProjectId }`. Both `gitBranchesQueryOptions(...)` and `gitStatusQueryOptions(...)` now use that object, and `defaultBranchName = branches.find((branch) => branch.isDefault)?.name ?? null` is threaded into `resolveBranchToolbarValue(...)`. The old contract it replaced was "branch query cache and status lookup are keyed only by cwd." The fallback path is explicit: if no default branch is present, the selector still falls back to `currentGitBranch`.

#### Lines `198-256` - Project-Scoped Checkout, Status, and Branch Creation
Every mutation path now sends `repoPath` plus `projectId` instead of `cwd`: `api.git.checkout(...)`, `api.git.status(...)`, and `api.git.createBranch(...)` all switched to the project-scoped git contract. The authoritative mutation target is `selectionTarget.checkoutCwd` or `branchCwd` paired with `activeProjectId`; the old contract it replaced was a local-looking git mutation surface that could not disambiguate the same repo path across projects or carry remote-project identity. The fallback path is unchanged early bailout when `branchCwd` or the native API is missing.

#### Lines `280-305` - Initial Branch Seeding from Default Branch
The automatic branch seeding effect now calls `onSetThreadBranch(currentGitBranch ?? defaultBranchName, null)` whenever there is no active worktree and no thread branch, instead of depending on `effectiveEnvMode === "worktree"` and `currentGitBranch` only. The authoritative fallback order is now `currentGitBranch` first, then `defaultBranchName`. The old contract it replaced was "only seed from the currently checked-out branch, and only under the narrower worktree-mode condition."
- Feature:
#### Lines `44-112` - Project-Scoped Branch Query Identity
Changed branch query plumbing so the authoritative git target is `{ projectId, repoPath }`, which is what lets the selector distinguish the same repo path across projects and keep remote or multi-repo branch queries scoped to the right project. This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and `Remote SSH Support` and is part of the branch selector component.

#### Lines `198-256` - Project-Scoped Checkout, Status, and Branch Creation
Changed branch checkout and branch creation so every git mutation is routed by the selected repo plus project identity instead of a naked cwd, which is required for multi-repo and remote projects where path strings alone are not unique enough. This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and `Remote SSH Support` and is part of the branch selector component.

#### Lines `280-305` - Initial Branch Seeding from Default Branch
Changed empty-thread branch seeding so a new thread can initialize from the repo’s default branch when no explicit thread/worktree branch exists yet. This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the branch selector component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `44-112` - Project-Scoped Branch Query Identity
This depends on project-scoped git query keys in `apps/web/src/lib/gitReactQuery.ts`, default-branch fallback logic in `apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbar.logic.ts`, and selected-repo state coming from `BranchToolbar.tsx`. If it drifts, branch lists can be cached under the wrong repo or show the wrong default branch after repo switches.

#### Lines `198-256` - Project-Scoped Checkout, Status, and Branch Creation
This depends on `apps/web/src/wsNativeApi.ts`, server git routing in `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts`, and the repo-target git contract in `packages/contracts/src/git.ts`. If it drifts, create/checkout can mutate the wrong repository or the right repository on the wrong host. Retest local and remote branch checkout, create-branch flows, and repo switching before opening the branch picker.

#### Lines `280-305` - Initial Branch Seeding from Default Branch
This depends on `defaultBranchName` being available from the branch query and on `BranchToolbar.logic.ts` using the same fallback order. If it drifts, a new thread can fail to pick up the repo default branch, especially in repos where the current branch is absent or delayed. Retest initial branch seeding when a repo only has a default branch and after switching selected repos.

### `apps/web/src/components/ChatMarkdown.tsx`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `19-28, 51-55, 241-291` - Project-Aware Markdown File Links
`77d03367` replaced the old `openInPreferredEditor(...)` plus `resolveMarkdownFileLinkTarget(...)` pair with `openResolvedEditorTargetInPreferredEditor(...)` and `resolveProjectEditorTargetFromMarkdownHref(...)`, and introduced `ProjectLinkContext` as the new authoritative input type for link resolution. The component prop changed from `cwd: string | undefined` to `linkContext: ProjectLinkContext`, and anchor handling now resolves `const target = resolveProjectEditorTargetFromMarkdownHref(href, linkContext)` before deciding whether to intercept the click. If the target resolves, `onClick` opens the already-resolved editor target through `openResolvedEditorTargetInPreferredEditor(api, target)` instead of opening a plain local path string. The old contract it replaced was "markdown file links can only be resolved against one cwd and always open as local editor paths." The fallback path is explicit: when `resolveProjectEditorTargetFromMarkdownHref(...)` returns `null`, the link still renders as a normal external anchor with `target=\"_blank\"` and `rel=\"noreferrer\"`.
- Feature:
#### Lines `19-28, 51-55, 241-291` - Project-Aware Markdown File Links
Changed markdown link handling so the authoritative resolution input is `ProjectLinkContext`, not a bare cwd, which means file links inside chat can resolve against the project root, a thread-specific `projectPath`, or a structured remote SSH editor target before the editor is opened. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the chat markdown rendering component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `19-28, 51-55, 241-291` - Project-Aware Markdown File Links
This depends on `apps/web/src/projectEditorTargets.ts`, `apps/web/src/editorPreferences.ts`, and the project-aware editor-open transport behind the native API. If it drifts, markdown links can open the wrong repo root, fail to open remote files in the preferred editor, or degrade back to browser navigation for paths that should stay inside the app/editor flow. Retest markdown links for project-root files, thread-relative files in multi-repo threads, remote SSH file links, and ordinary external URLs.

### `apps/web/src/components/ChatView.logic.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `23-49` - Draft Thread Projection Includes `projectPath`
`buildLocalDraftThread(...)` now copies `projectPath: draftThread.projectPath` into the synthetic local `Thread` object. The authoritative field added here is `projectPath`; the old contract it replaced was "a locally materialized draft thread only carries `branch` and `worktreePath`, so the view layer must infer the effective project root later." The fallback path remains the draft-thread state itself: if `draftThread.projectPath` still points at the project root, the synthetic thread behaves like the old single-root flow.

#### Lines `171-182` - Visible Provider Thread Id Resolution
Added `resolveVisibleProviderThreadId(thread)`, which makes `thread.session?.providerThreadId` the authoritative visible id and only falls back to `thread.codexThreadId` when the new session field is blank. The old contract it replaced was "the UI can only show `codexThreadId`," which does not generalize to other providers and misses the canonical session field once the provider runtime is attached. The fallback path is explicit: if `session.providerThreadId` is empty or absent, a trimmed legacy `codexThreadId` is still shown.

#### Lines `185-327` - Remote Session Health and Error Suppression
Added the `VisibleProviderHealthStatus` union and the helper chain `isSuppressedRemoteThreadManagementMessage(...)`, `isOlderThanOrEqualToDismissedAt(...)`, `buildRemoteProviderHealthStatus(...)`, `resolveVisibleProviderHealthStatus(...)`, and `resolveVisibleThreadError(...)`. The authoritative suppression list is `SUPPRESSED_REMOTE_THREAD_MANAGEMENT_MESSAGES`, plus the prefix check for `Reconnected to provider thread `. The old contract it replaced was "surface provider status and thread error strings directly," which meant remote reconnect bookkeeping messages and already-dismissed local Codex health errors were rendered as if they were actionable failures. The new remote path is stricter: when `projectRemote` is present, `resolveVisibleProviderHealthStatus(...)` uses remote-specific copy such as `Remote Codex launcher status` / `Remote Codex session status`, suppresses reconnect-management noise, and only surfaces real remote launcher/session failures. The local path now checks `localCodexErrorsDismissedAfter` against `status.checkedAt` or `session.updatedAt`, so dismissed local Codex failures stay hidden until a newer error appears. The fallback paths are explicit: if there is no session and the local provider status is `ready`, remote health returns `null`; non-Codex local errors still render immediately; and unsuppressed remote `thread.error` strings still pass through untouched.
- Feature:
#### Lines `23-49` - Draft Thread Projection Includes `projectPath`
Changed local draft-thread projection to carry `projectPath` alongside `branch[]` and `worktreePath[]`, so a draft thread opened against a repo-specific worktree can render and mutate against the same project path before it exists on the server. This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the local draft-thread projection component.

#### Lines `171-182` - Visible Provider Thread Id Resolution
Changed visible thread-id derivation so the UI prefers the canonical provider-runtime thread id and only falls back to the legacy Codex-specific field when necessary. This supports `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the provider session visibility component.

#### Lines `185-327` - Remote Session Health and Error Suppression
Changed provider-health and thread-error visibility so remote launcher/session failures are rendered with remote-specific status copy, reconnect-management noise is suppressed, and dismissed local Codex health checks stay hidden until a genuinely newer failure arrives. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the chat runtime status filtering component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `23-49` - Draft Thread Projection Includes `projectPath`
This field is consumed immediately by `apps/web/src/components/ChatView.tsx`, branch/worktree controls, project-link resolution, and any draft-thread logic that needs the effective repo/worktree root before a server snapshot arrives. If it drifts, new draft threads can open links, git controls, or terminal state against the wrong repo root. Retest draft-thread creation, multi-repo draft repo switching, and sending the first turn from a draft thread with a non-root `projectPath`.

#### Lines `171-182` - Visible Provider Thread Id Resolution
This helper feeds thread-id display modes in chat/composer surfaces and depends on the expanded `ThreadSession` shape in `apps/web/src/types.ts` plus provider-thread persistence from the server read model. If it drifts, the UI can show a stale Codex-only id, hide Kiro/Claude provider thread ids, or surface nothing when a valid session id exists. Retest thread-id display with Codex, Kiro, and legacy sessions.

#### Lines `185-327` - Remote Session Health and Error Suppression
This subsection depends on provider status snapshots from `serverGetConfig`, reconnect/session metadata in `apps/web/src/store.ts` and `apps/web/src/types.ts`, dismissal timestamps stored in app state, and the top-level chat shell that renders banners and inline errors. If it drifts, remote reconnect bookkeeping starts showing up as false error banners, local Codex health errors reappear after dismissal, and real remote launcher failures may be hidden behind the wrong copy. Retest remote session start/reconnect/failure, dismissed local Codex health errors, unsuppressed provider errors, and chat banners after a remote thread transitions between `starting`, `running`, `disconnected`, and `error`.

### `apps/web/src/components/DiffPanel.tsx`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `4`, `192-199`
`activeCwd` no longer reads `activeThread?.worktreePath` directly. It now resolves through `getSingleRepoWorktreePath(activeThread) ?? activeProject?.cwd ?? null`, which is the single-repo fallback extracted from the fork's array-based thread git state. The old git query contract `{ cwd, projectId }` was then replaced with `gitTarget = { repoPath: activeCwd, projectId: activeProject?.id ?? null }`, and `gitBranchesQueryOptions` now reads that project-aware repo target instead of a raw cwd string.

#### Lines `22`, `27`, `329-344`
Old editor opening logic `openInPreferredEditor(resolvePathLinkTarget(filePath, activeCwd))` was replaced by `resolveProjectEditorTargetFromRawPath(filePath, { projectId, threadId, referenceRoot: activeCwd, remote })` and `openResolvedEditorTargetInPreferredEditor(api, target)`. The old remote fallback was to block editor opening entirely when `activeProject?.remote` existed; now the resolver is authoritative and decides whether the path becomes a local project-relative open, a shell/editor target, or an SSH-aware target.

#### Lines `12`, `172-175`, `183`, `312-317`, `542-550`, `628`, `645-647`
Added `TextWrapIcon`, local state `diffWordWrap`, and `previousDiffOpenRef`. `diffWordWrap` is seeded from `settings.diffWordWrap`, reset from settings only when the panel transitions from closed to open, toggled inline with a dedicated button, and then applied to both renderer branches: `FileDiff.options.overflow` flips between `"wrap"` and `"scroll"`, while the raw `<pre>` fallback flips between `whitespace-pre-wrap wrap-break-word` and plain scrolling. The old behavior had no per-panel wrap state and always used the renderer defaults.
- Feature:
#### Lines `4`, `192-199`
Changed DiffPanel's authoritative git-root resolver to support `Multi-Repo Support` and `Remote SSH Support`: the panel now derives the diff repo root from the thread's single-repo worktree helper and passes `repoPath` plus `projectId` through the same git-target contract used elsewhere in the fork. This is part of the diff git-target routing component, where the panel must distinguish the real repo root from thread-level multi-repo state and from SSH-backed project roots.

#### Lines `22`, `27`, `329-344`
Changed DiffPanel's file-open path resolution to support `Remote SSH Support`: diff header clicks no longer assume a local filesystem path rooted at `activeCwd`, and instead resolve a project-aware editor target using `projectId`, `threadId`, `referenceRoot`, and `remote`. This is part of the project editor-target resolution component that lets diff files open correctly from SSH projects and from project-relative paths emitted by git diffs.

#### Lines `12`, `172-175`, `183`, `312-317`, `542-550`, `628`, `645-647`
Changed DiffPanel's rendering controls to support `Extra Customization`: users can keep a persisted default wrap preference in settings while still toggling line wrapping inside the open diff panel without permanently mutating that default until the panel is reopened. This is part of the diff rendering preference component.
- Dependency impact:

### `apps/web/src/components/GitActionsControl.logic.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `181-290` - Quick Action Respects User Git Default
`be9f7119` added `preferredAction: GitStackedAction | "auto" = "auto"` to `resolveQuickAction(...)` and immediately normalizes it into `effectivePreferredAction`, where `"auto"` falls back to `"commit_push_pr"`. The old upstream behavior was purely status-driven after `gitStatus`, `isBusy`, `isDefaultBranch`, and `hasOriginRemote`; the fork now lets `preferredAction` override the primary CTA in three places: dirty branches (`"commit"` vs `"commit_push"` vs `"commit_push_pr"`), ahead branches without an upstream (`"Push"` vs `"Push & create PR"`), and ahead branches with an upstream (return `"Push"` whenever `effectivePreferredAction !== "commit_push_pr"`). The origin-remote and default-branch safeguards remain in place, but the quick-action label and returned `action` are no longer fixed by branch state alone.
- Feature:
#### Lines `181-290` - Quick Action Respects User Git Default
Changed git quick-action resolution to support `Extra Customization`: the user’s configured default git action now feeds directly into the primary CTA without removing the existing branch-safety checks for missing `origin`, default branches, open PRs, or diverged state. This is part of the git action recommendation component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `181-290` - Quick Action Respects User Git Default
This depends on `apps/web/src/appSettings.ts` (`gitDefaultAction`), `apps/web/src/components/GitActionsControl.tsx` (which passes the preference and renders the returned label/action), `packages/contracts` git action enums, and the git status fields `branch`, `hasUpstream`, `aheadCount`, `behindCount`, and `pr.state` returned by the server git pipeline. If this changes, retest dirty branches, ahead branches with and without upstreams, repositories without an `origin` remote, open-PR branches, default branches, and each preference mode: `"auto"`, `"commit"`, `"commit_push"`, and `"commit_push_pr"`.

### `apps/web/src/components/GitActionsControl.tsx`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `45-62`, `212-287`, `805-808`
The component no longer accepts a single `gitCwd: string | null`. It now takes `gitTarget: GitQueryTarget`, `projectRemote: ProjectRemoteTarget | null`, and later `disableGitActions?: boolean`. The authoritative repo root is `gitRepoPath = gitTarget.repoPath`, and every query or mutation now keys off that project-scoped target: `gitStatusQueryOptions(gitTarget, ...)`, `gitBranchesQueryOptions(gitTarget)`, `gitInitMutationOptions({ target: gitTarget })`, `gitRunStackedActionMutationOptions({ target: gitTarget, ... })`, `gitPullMutationOptions({ target: gitTarget })`, and `gitMutationKeys.*(gitTarget)`. The old fallback was "render whenever `gitCwd` exists"; the current file hard-stops on `if (!gitTarget.repoPath) return null`, which means the caller must supply the exact selected repo root.

#### Lines `11-12`, `218-235`, `253-285`, `300-331`
Added `gitRequestSettings = buildGitRequestSettings(settings)` and `gitActionModelSelection = gitRequestSettings.textGenerationModelSelection ?? resolveAppModelSelectionState(settings)`. The old mutation path passed `modelSelection: settings.textGenerationModelSelection` directly and did not consistently thread the rest of the git request settings into every query. The fork now calls `gitStatusQueryOptions(gitTarget, gitRequestSettings)` so status reads share the same request-settings cache key, and `gitRunStackedActionMutationOptions` now receives both `settings: gitRequestSettings` and `modelSelection: gitActionModelSelection`. `resolveQuickAction(...)` also now receives `settings.gitDefaultAction`, so the visible CTA follows the user's configured default action.

#### Lines `62`, `300-331`, `468-475`
Added `disableGitActions?: boolean` and threaded it through both menu derivation and execution. When `disableGitActions` is true, `buildMenuItems(...)` is forced into a busy state, `quickAction` is replaced with a fixed disabled hint (`"Git actions are disabled for multi-repo projects right now."`), and `runGitActionWithToast(...)` returns early with an error toast instead of dispatching a mutation. Upstream assumed that if a git target existed, actions were runnable; the fork explicitly gates the control when higher-level multi-repo project state would make the action ambiguous.

#### Lines `356-408`
Progress-event filtering now compares `event.cwd` to `gitRepoPath` instead of the older `gitCwd`, which matters once repo selection can point at absolute per-repo roots. More importantly, the handler no longer clears progress state on WebSocket `action_finished` or `action_failed`; those cases now intentionally return early and let the HTTP mutation completion path finalize the toast. The old behavior could blank the "running for Xs" description between the WS event and the HTTP response.

#### Lines `43`, `56`, `771-805`
Changed file opening from `openInPreferredEditor(resolvePathLinkTarget(filePath, gitCwd))` to `resolveProjectEditorTargetFromRawPath(filePath, { projectId: gitTarget.projectId, threadId: activeThreadId, referenceRoot: gitTarget.repoPath, remote: projectRemote })` plus `openResolvedEditorTargetInPreferredEditor(api, target)`. The old remote fallback was a generic "unavailable" path; the resolver is now authoritative and can decide whether the changed file can be opened for the current project and host context. The reference root also moved from the old `gitCwd` field to the selected repo root `gitTarget.repoPath`.
- Feature:
#### Lines `45-62`, `212-287`, `805-808`
Changed the main git action surface to support `Multi-Repo Support` and `Remote SSH Support`: every action is now bound to a project-scoped repo target instead of a single cwd string, so the control can operate against the selected repo inside a project and against SSH-backed projects without guessing which root the action should hit. This is part of the repo-target git action routing component.

#### Lines `11-12`, `218-235`, `253-285`, `300-331`
Changed git-action configuration plumbing to support `Extra Customization`: generated commit and branch text now uses the resolved git text-generation settings and the resolved app model-selection fallback, and the primary CTA respects the user's configured git default action. This is part of the git text-generation and quick-action preference component.

#### Lines `62`, `300-331`, `468-475`
Changed the git action surface to support `Multi-Repo Support`: project-level multi-repo discovery can now disable the generic single-repo action control until the caller has narrowed the action to a concrete repo target. This is part of the multi-repo action gating component.

#### Lines `356-408`
Changed git action progress handling to support `Debugability and Stability`: toast progress remains attached to the active action until the authoritative HTTP completion arrives, even if WebSocket progress events finish first. This is part of the git action progress and toast reconciliation component.

#### Lines `43`, `56`, `771-805`
Changed changed-file editor opening to support `Remote SSH Support`: file paths coming from git status are now resolved against project identity, thread identity, selected repo root, and remote metadata before the editor is invoked. This is part of the project editor-target resolution component for git UIs.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `45-62`, `212-287`, `805-808`
This depends on `apps/web/src/components/ChatView.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/chat/ChatHeader.tsx`, `apps/web/src/lib/gitReactQuery.ts`, `apps/server/src/wsServer.ts`, and the server git layers that translate `projectId` plus `repoPath` into the actual git command target. If this changes, retest selected-repo actions from the chat header, git init, pull, commit, commit-and-push, and PR creation on both local and SSH-backed projects.

#### Lines `11-12`, `218-235`, `253-285`, `300-331`
This depends on `apps/web/src/appSettings.ts`, `apps/web/src/modelSelection.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/GitActionsControl.logic.ts`, `apps/server/src/git/Layers/RoutingTextGeneration.ts`, `apps/server/src/git/Layers/CodexTextGeneration.ts`, `apps/server/src/git/Layers/ClaudeTextGeneration.ts`, and the shared `GitRequestSettings` contract. #### Lines `62`, `300-331`, `468-475`

### `apps/web/src/components/PlanSidebar.tsx`

#### Lines 55-59, 65-69, 93-122, 161-166 - Save Proposed Plans Through Project Identity
Upstream accepted `markdownCwd: string | undefined` and wrote plan files with `api.projects.writeFile({ cwd: workspaceRoot, relativePath, contents })`. The fork adds `projectId: ProjectId | undefined` to `PlanSidebarProps`, threads it into the component signature, guards `handleSaveToWorkspace` with `!projectId`, sends `projectId` instead of `cwd` into `api.projects.writeFile`, extends the `useCallback` dependency list to `[planMarkdown, projectId, workspaceRoot]`, and disables the menu action unless `projectId`, `workspaceRoot`, and `!isSavingToWorkspace` are all true. Upstream carried a raw `markdownCwd` prop down to `<ChatMarkdown cwd={markdownCwd} />`. The fork imports `ProjectLinkContext`, replaces the prop with `linkContext: ProjectLinkContext`, and renders `<ChatMarkdown linkContext={linkContext} />`. That swaps the old contract of "markdown links are resolved relative to a cwd string" for "markdown links are resolved from project identity plus remote/local host context," which is required once a displayed path can belong to an SSH-backed project.
- Feature:
#### Lines 55-59, 65-69, 93-122, 161-166 - Save Proposed Plans Through Project Identity
Changed the plan export path from `cwd`-addressed writes to `projectId`-addressed writes so the sidebar can save generated plan markdown into the correct project even when the project lives on a remote SSH host and `workspaceRoot` is only display context. This supports the `Remote SSH Support` user feature by making "Save to workspace" use the project registry and server-side project resolution contract instead of assuming the browser can identify the target solely from a local absolute path, and it is part of the plan-sidebar-to-project-file-write component.

#### Lines 31, 55-60, 65-70, 243-247 - Resolve Plan Markdown Links Through ProjectLinkContext
Changed embedded plan markdown rendering to resolve file references through `ProjectLinkContext` so links inside a proposed plan can open the right project-relative file target for local projects, SSH-backed projects, and future shell/editor-target fallbacks. This supports the `Remote SSH Support` user feature by replacing a local-only `cwd` assumption with the same project-aware editor-target contract used elsewhere in the app, and it is part of the project link-resolution/open-in-editor component.

The old contract it replaced was `cwd`-only file writes. If this entry drifts, retest saving proposed plans for local projects, SSH projects, and threads whose displayed `workspaceRoot` differs from the canonical project path; failures usually show up as disabled save actions, writes landing in the wrong repo, or server-side "project not found" errors.

#### Lines 31, 55-60, 65-70, 243-247 - Resolve Plan Markdown Links Through ProjectLinkContext
