### `apps/web/src/components/ThreadTerminalDrawer.tsx`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `184-187`, `200-203`, `406-416`, `488-495`, `657-662`, `709-714`, `1023-1054`
The remote terminal/editor-target change set started in `0ae86206 feat(remote): enable git, diff, terminal, and workspace flows over SSH` and was then narrowed by `77d03367 feat(remote): resolve editor paths by project and host context`. `TerminalViewportProps` and `ThreadTerminalDrawerProps` now carry `projectId: ProjectId | null` and `projectRemote: ProjectRemoteTarget | null` instead of the old local-only `cwd` plus `allowPathLinkOpen?: boolean` gate. The terminal link activation path no longer checks `allowPathLinkOpen` and then opens `resolvePathLinkTarget(match.text, cwd)` through `openInPreferredEditor(...)`; it now resolves `resolveProjectEditorTargetFromRawPath(match.text, { projectId: projectId ?? undefined, threadId, referenceRoot: cwd, remote: projectRemote })` and opens the returned `ResolvedEditorTarget` through `openResolvedEditorTargetInPreferredEditor(...)`. `api.terminal.open(...)` also now includes `projectId` whenever present, so the authoritative terminal-open payload is `{ threadId, terminalId, cwd, projectId?, cols, rows, env? }` instead of the old `{ threadId, terminalId, cwd, cols, rows, env? }`.

#### Lines `30`, `109-170`, `189`, `215-230`, `261-333`, `439-469`, `521-539`, `653`, `677`, `729`, `1026-1054`
`f068afee Give Agents access to Terminal output (#1032)` added the terminal-context capture flow. The file now defines `MULTI_CLICK_SELECTION_ACTION_DELAY_MS`, `getTerminalSelectionRect(...)`, `resolveTerminalSelectionActionPosition(...)`, `terminalSelectionActionDelayForClickCount(...)`, and `shouldHandleTerminalSelectionMouseUp(...)`. `TerminalViewportProps` gained the authoritative selection metadata inputs `terminalLabel` and `onAddTerminalContext`, then stores them in `terminalLabelRef` and `onAddTerminalContextRef`. The drawer now tracks `selectionPointerRef`, `selectionGestureActiveRef`, `selectionActionRequestIdRef`, `selectionActionOpenRef`, and `selectionActionTimerRef`; `readSelectionAction()` normalizes the selected text, computes `lineStart` / `lineEnd` from `getSelectionPosition()`, and builds a `TerminalContextSelection` payload `{ terminalId, terminalLabel, lineStart, lineEnd, text }`; `showSelectionAction()` opens a context menu with the single action id `"add-to-chat"`; and successful selection insertion clears the xterm selection and refocuses the terminal. Output lifecycle events `output`, `started`, `restarted`, and `cleared` now all call `clearSelectionAction()` so stale selection menus do not survive terminal mutations, and the viewport container class changed from `h-full w-full` to `relative h-full w-full` so the selection-position logic has a stable geometry root.
- Feature:
#### Lines `184-187`, `200-203`, `406-416`, `488-495`, `657-662`, `709-714`, `1023-1054`
Changed terminal path opening and terminal-session startup to resolve by `projectId`, `threadId`, `referenceRoot`, and `projectRemote` so `Remote SSH Support` can open terminal-emitted file paths inside the correct SSH-backed project and keep terminal startup bound to the same project identity used by the rest of the fork. This is part of the project-thread-remote editor-target and terminal-routing component. Concretely, the old local-only `allowPathLinkOpen` contract is gone; the authoritative resolver is now `resolveProjectEditorTargetFromRawPath(...)`, which can return a project-relative editor target for remote projects, fall back to a shell path only for local projects, and reject unresolved/out-of-root paths with the explicit runtime fallback message `"Unable to resolve path for editor opening."`

#### Lines `30`, `109-170`, `189`, `215-230`, `261-333`, `439-469`, `521-539`, `653`, `677`, `729`, `1026-1054`
Changed terminal selection handling so exact terminal output ranges can be lifted into the composer as structured terminal context blocks with stable terminal labels and line ranges, which supports `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the composer terminal-context ingestion component. Concretely, the old contract was "terminal output is only visual"; the new contract is "selected terminal output becomes a `TerminalContextSelection` record that can be inserted into the draft, rendered inline, and preserved with line numbers." The multi-click delay is also intentional: double-click and triple-click selection gestures wait `MULTI_CLICK_SELECTION_ACTION_DELAY_MS` before showing the action menu so word/line selection settles before the drawer snapshots the text.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `184-187`, `200-203`, `406-416`, `488-495`, `657-662`, `709-714`, `1023-1054`
This block depends directly on [projectEditorTargets.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/projectEditorTargets.ts), where `resolveProjectEditorTargetFromRawPath(...)` converts raw terminal text into either `{ kind: "project-path", input: { projectId, threadId?, relativePath, line?, column? }, isRemoteProject }` or a local `{ kind: "shell", target }`; on [editorPreferences.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/editorPreferences.ts), where `openResolvedEditorTargetInPreferredEditor(...)` picks a remote-SSH-capable editor when `isRemoteProject` is true; on [terminal.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/packages/contracts/src/terminal.ts), where `TerminalOpenInput.projectId` is the authoritative optional field; and on the server terminal/open chain in [wsServer.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/wsServer.ts), [open.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/open.ts), and [terminal/Layers/Manager.ts](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/server/src/terminal/Layers/Manager.ts). If this contract drifts, the visible failures are remote terminal links trying to open as local shell paths, local out-of-root links opening the wrong file, terminal sessions starting without the project context needed for remote path resolution, or remote projects silently losing editor-open support. ### `apps/web/src/components/chat/OpenInPicker.tsx`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `1-18`, `20-60`, `65-77`, `79-185`, `206-211`
The open-in picker divergence is the combined result of `0ae86206 feat(remote): enable git, diff, terminal, and workspace flows over SSH`, `77d03367 feat(remote): resolve editor paths by project and host context`, and `3d99bd12 Add structured remote SSH editor targets`. `OpenInPicker` now accepts `projectId`, `threadId`, `openInProjectRoot`, and `isRemoteProject`; imports `filterRemoteSshEditors` and `toastManager`; and computes `eligibleEditors` separately from the full `availableEditors` list. The old contract was `openInCwd` only: both the click path and the keyboard shortcut always called `api.shell.openInEditor(openInCwd, editor)`, and remote mode merely hid `file-manager` from the menu. The authoritative contract is now three-way: `api.projects.openInEditor({ projectId, editor })` for project-root opens, `api.projects.openPathInEditor({ projectId, threadId?, relativePath: ".", editor })` for thread/worktree-relative opens, and `api.shell.openInEditor(openInCwd, editor)` only as the local fallback when there is no project id. Remote editor eligibility now comes from `filterRemoteSshEditors(...)`, and failures are surfaced through `showOpenError(...)` toast payloads rather than failing silently.
- Feature:
#### Lines `1-18`, `20-60`, `65-77`, `79-185`, `206-211`
Changed the open-in picker so editor launches are routed by `projectId`, `threadId`, `openInProjectRoot`, and `isRemoteProject` instead of by a bare local path string, which supports `Remote SSH Support` and is part of the project-scoped editor-launch component. Concretely, the old fallback path was "open the cwd in the shell editor and hope it is local"; the new fallback chain is project-root open, then project-relative `"."`, then local shell open, with remote-only editor filtering applied before any preferred editor is chosen.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `1-18`, `20-60`, `65-77`, `79-185`, `206-211`

### `apps/web/src/composerDraftStore.ts`

""`, `envMode` now normalizes against `normalizedWorktreePath[0]`, and synthetic placeholder draft threads default to `projectPath: ""`, `branch: [null]`, and `worktreePath: [null]`. This is the Kiro-aware provider draft normalization change set. Lines `584-604` make `legacyReplaceProviderModelOptions(...)` a no-op for `provider === "kiro"`, and lines `1777-1791` enforce the same rule at runtime by returning early from `setProviderModelOptions(...)` when `normalizedProvider === "kiro"`.

More concretely, `setProjectDraftThreadId(...)` and `setDraftThreadContext(...)` now accept `branchIndex` and update only that repo slot, while `projectPath` becomes the authoritative synthetic parent/root path that the rest of the chat stack uses when one thread spans multiple repos. This is part of the draft-thread project/repo context mapping component.

#### Lines `239`, `282-292`, `419-423`, `526-540`, `557-604`, `1777-1791`

### `apps/web/src/hooks/useHandleNewThread.ts`

- Status: `Modified`

`efd5f211` is the multi-repo follow-up layered on top of the remote env-mode fix. The authoritative read path for stored and active draft worktree state changed from `storedDraftThread.worktreePath` / `latestActiveDraftThread.worktreePath` to `storedDraftThread.worktreePath[0] ?? null` / `latestActiveDraftThread.worktreePath[0] ?? null`, because draft thread worktree data is now array-shaped. The same change set also starts backfilling `projectPath` during every draft mutation: lines `84-86` and `124-126` write `projectPath: storedDraftThread.projectPath || project.cwd` / `latestActiveDraftThread.projectPath || project.cwd`, and lines `140-145` seed brand-new drafts with `projectPath: project.cwd` when the project root is known. The old contract it replaced was "worktreePath is scalar and projectPath does not need to be written here."
- Feature:
#### Lines `11`, `38`, `55-89`, `110-129`, `139-156`
Changed new-thread draft reuse and creation so env mode is resolved from actual project remote state plus actual worktree presence instead of from a simple "remote means local" override. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and is part of the draft-thread env-mode normalization component. Concretely, a remote draft thread that no longer has a valid worktree path is forced back onto the authoritative local-mode path before navigation or reuse, while a real worktree-backed draft can still preserve worktree mode.

#### Lines `71-88`, `111-128`, `140-145`
Changed new-thread handling so reused and newly created draft threads carry the same `projectPath` and array-based `worktreePath[0]` contract that the multi-repo draft store expects. This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the draft-thread creation and repo-root seeding component. More concretely, the hook now seeds the thread-level `projectPath` before the server thread exists, so the rest of the chat stack can distinguish the synthetic parent/root from the concrete repo worktree path as soon as the draft opens.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `11`, `38`, `55-89`, `110-129`, `139-156`
This subsection depends on [`apps/web/src/threadEnvMode.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/threadEnvMode.ts), [`apps/web/src/composerDraftStore.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/composerDraftStore.ts), and the project metadata projection in [`apps/web/src/store.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/store.ts) that supplies `project.remote`. If this logic drifts, `mod+n` or any other "new thread" path can reopen a stale remote draft in unsupported worktree mode, which then cascades into wrong terminal cwd, wrong script runtime cwd, or a chat view that renders a worktree badge the backend cannot honor. Retest new-thread creation on local projects, SSH projects, existing stored drafts, and active route drafts with and without a live worktree path.

#### Lines `71-88`, `111-128`, `140-145`
This subsection depends on the array and `projectPath` contract in [`apps/web/src/composerDraftStore.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/composerDraftStore.ts), local draft-thread projection in [`apps/web/src/components/ChatView.logic.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/components/ChatView.logic.ts), and repo-aware consumers such as [`apps/web/src/components/ChatView.tsx`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/components/ChatView.tsx) and [`apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbar.tsx`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbar.tsx). ### `apps/web/src/lib/contextWindow.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines 43-61 - Prefer Provider-Reported Usage Percentage
The fork adds `const explicitUsedPercentage = asFiniteNumber(payload?.usedPercentage);` inside `deriveLatestContextWindowSnapshot(...)` and changes `usedPercentage` from a pure `usedTokens / maxTokens` calculation into a two-step fallback: use `payload.usedPercentage` when it is finite and non-negative, otherwise derive from `usedTokens` and `maxTokens` as upstream did. The returned `ContextWindowSnapshot` object now also emits `usedPercentage` immediately after `usedTokens`, but the substantive contract change is that provider-emitted utilization is authoritative when present.
- Feature:
#### Lines 43-61 - Prefer Provider-Reported Usage Percentage
Changed context-window snapshot normalization so Kiro and other providers can publish an exact `usedPercentage` value and have the web layer preserve it instead of recomputing a potentially different number from token counts. This supports the `Kiro Integration` user feature by keeping the UI aligned with provider-native context-window telemetry, including cases where the provider reports percentage directly or applies provider-specific accounting rules, and it is part of the activity-to-context-window projection component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines 43-61 - Prefer Provider-Reported Usage Percentage
This depends on `context-window.updated` payloads carrying `usedPercentage` through `packages/contracts/src/orchestration.ts`, on server-side telemetry emission from the provider/Kiro context snapshot path, and on `apps/web/src/components/chat/ContextWindowMeter.tsx` trusting this derived snapshot as its display source. The old contract was "web recomputes the percent from token counts"; the new contract is "web honors provider percentage first, then falls back to local math." If this logic changes, retest context window updates for providers that send both `usedTokens` and `usedPercentage`, providers that only send `usedTokens/maxTokens`, and Kiro payloads that omit `maxTokens` but still provide a percentage, because otherwise the meter, remaining-percentage display, and any warnings keyed off utilization can drift from the provider’s actual state.

### `apps/web/src/projectEditorTargets.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `1-205`
`77d03367` adds this entire contract file. The authoritative input is `ProjectLinkContext { projectId, threadId, referenceRoot, remote }` at lines `10-15`, and the authoritative output is `ResolvedEditorTarget` at lines `17-23`, which can be either `kind: "project-path"` with `ProjectOpenPathInEditorInput` data or `kind: "shell"` with a local shell/editor path string. The core path machinery is all here: `isWindowsPathStyle(...)`, `normalizeAbsolutePath(...)`, and `joinResolvedPath(...)` normalize POSIX, drive-letter, and UNC-style paths; `relativePathWithinRoot(...)` only accepts resolved targets that stay within `referenceRoot`; `toProjectPathInput(...)` converts `path[:line[:column]]` into `{ projectId, threadId?, relativePath, line?, column? }`; and `resolveEditorTargetFromResolvedPath(...)` chooses between project-path and shell fallback. The old contract it replaced across the UI was "each caller resolves a raw path string against one cwd and then opens it directly." The important fallback paths are explicit: if a resolved path lives under `referenceRoot`, it becomes a project-relative target; if it falls outside the project root and the project is local, it falls back to `kind: "shell"`; if it falls outside the project root and `context.remote` is present, the resolver returns `null` instead of inventing a remote shell path the editor-open stack cannot safely support.

#### Lines `17-23`, `146-156`
`3d99bd12` is the remote metadata follow-up. It extends `ResolvedEditorTarget.kind === "project-path"` with `isRemoteProject: boolean` and sets that flag from `Boolean(context.remote)` inside `resolveEditorTargetFromResolvedPath(...)`. The old contract it replaced was "project-path targets do not tell the next layer whether the project is remote." The `context.remote => return null` branch remains authoritative for out-of-root remote paths; the new metadata only applies when a project-relative target was successfully resolved.
- Feature:
#### Lines `1-205`
Implemented a project-aware editor target resolver so markdown links, terminal paths, diff file paths, and git file paths all pass through one contract that understands `projectId`, `threadId`, `referenceRoot`, Windows path normalization, and remote-project restrictions. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the link-to-editor target resolution component. Concretely, `resolveProjectEditorTargetFromMarkdownHref(...)` and `resolveProjectEditorTargetFromRawPath(...)` now convert raw paths into project-relative opens when the path stays inside the selected project/worktree root, which is what lets multi-repo and SSH flows share one resolver instead of scattering cwd math across the UI.

#### Lines `17-23`, `146-156`
Changed resolved editor targets so the next layer can tell whether a valid `project-path` target belongs to a remote SSH project and can therefore restrict editor choice to remote-capable editors. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and is part of the remote-capable editor selection handshake between path resolution and preferred-editor dispatch.
- Dependency impact:

### `apps/web/src/routes/__root.tsx`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `16`, `55`, `327-359`
This block is the merged `fa638304` plus `64173a3e` watcher series. Line `16` adds `useAppSettings`, line `55` mounts `AppSettingsWatcher`, and lines `327-359` define the watcher itself. The watcher computes `settingsSignature = JSON.stringify(settings)`, tracks `previousSettingsSignatureRef`, and calls `dismissLocalCodexErrors(new Date().toISOString())` whenever the effective settings payload changes after first render. It also tracks `syncedDesktopCloseBehaviorRef` and calls `window.desktopBridge?.setAppCloseBehavior(settings.desktopAppCloseBehavior)` when the desktop close-behavior setting changes, resetting the synced ref on bridge failure. The old contract it replaced was "root route does not react to app settings changes at all."

`e9468191` adds one explicit startup ordering call: `void syncSnapshot();` immediately after domain-event subscription is established and before terminal events / `server.welcome` handling proceed. The old contract it replaced was "initial snapshot hydration waits for later event traffic or the welcome path," which allowed bootstrap navigation to race thread hydration.

Changed root-route lifecycle wiring so settings changes now have two side effects: stale local Codex launcher errors are dismissed after a successful settings change, and desktop builds push `desktopAppCloseBehavior` over the Electron bridge as soon as the setting changes. ### `apps/web/src/session-logic.ts`

- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `22-42`

### `apps/web/src/store.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines 25-53, 57-111, 135-204 - Persist Project UI State by Remote-Aware Project Key
Upstream persisted expansion and ordering as raw cwd lists under older renderer-state keys. The fork changes the persisted schema to `PERSISTED_STATE_KEY = "t3code:renderer-state:v10"`, renames the stored arrays from `expandedProjectCwds` / `projectOrderCwds` to `expandedProjectKeys` / `projectOrderKeys`, and introduces `projectPersistenceKey({ cwd, remote })` that serializes projects as `local:${cwd}` or `ssh:${remote.hostAlias}:${cwd}`. `readPersistedState()` and `persistState()` now read and write those key arrays, `mapProjectsFromReadModel()` matches existing projects by either `project.id` or `projectPersistenceKey(...)`, and project ordering/expanded state are resolved through `previousByKey`, `previousOrderByKey`, and `persistedOrderByKey` instead of cwd-only maps. The old contract it replaces was "two projects with the same cwd are the same persisted sidebar entry"; the new contract is "local and SSH projects with the same workspaceRoot remain distinct."

#### Lines 154-173 - Carry Remote and Multi-Repo Project Topology into the Browser Store
When projecting `readModel.projects`, the fork adds `remote: project.remote ?? null`, `gitMode: project.gitMode ?? "none"`, and `gitRepos: project.gitRepos?.map((repo) => ({ ...repo })) ?? null` to the stored `Project` object. Upstream only carried the basic project identity/script fields. The authoritative project-level git topology now lives in the browser store, and the old fallback is explicit: absent server data becomes `gitMode = "none"` and `gitRepos = null`.

#### Lines 207-216, 298-318 - Preserve Disconnected and Reconnect Session Metadata
`toLegacySessionStatus(...)` now accepts the orchestration status `"disconnected"` and maps it through instead of collapsing everything into `"connecting" | "ready" | "running" | "error" | "closed"`. In `syncServerReadModel(...)`, the fork also copies `providerThreadId`, `resumeAvailable`, `reconnectState`, `reconnectSummary`, and `reconnectUpdatedAt` from `thread.session` into the browser session object when present. Upstream dropped all of those fields, so the browser lost the persisted provider thread identity and reconnect-health chain even if the server had it.

#### Lines 228-232 - Normalize Kiro Provider Names in Legacy Session Mapping
`toLegacyProvider(providerName)` now recognizes `"kiro"` in addition to `"codex"` and `"claudeAgent"`, and the fallback path is `DEFAULT_PROVIDER_KIND` rather than a hard-coded `"codex"`. The old contract was effectively "unknown provider names become Codex"; the new contract keeps Kiro sessions correctly typed and centralizes the default-provider fallback.

#### Lines 262-269, 325-333 - Scope Attachment Preview URLs by Project and Thread
Upstream built preview URLs with `attachmentPreviewRoutePath(attachmentId)` returning `/attachments/:attachmentId`. The fork changes the helper signature to `(projectId, threadId, attachmentId)` and generates `/api/projects/:projectId/threads/:threadId/attachments/:attachmentId`, with `syncServerReadModel(...)` now passing `thread.projectId` and `thread.id` when materializing `message.attachments[].previewUrl`. The old global attachment path is no longer authoritative.

#### Lines 18-22, 39-43, 461-485, 522-553 - Dismiss Local Codex Errors Without Touching Remote Threads
The fork adds `localCodexErrorsDismissedAfter: string | null` to `AppState`, initializes it to `null`, exposes `dismissLocalCodexErrors(dismissedAt)`, and wires that action into `AppStore` / `useStore`. The dismissal logic builds `localProjectIds` from `state.projects.filter((project) => !project.remote)`, clears `thread.error` only for threads whose `thread.session?.provider === "codex"` and whose project is local, and records the dismissal watermark in `localCodexErrorsDismissedAfter`. Upstream had no dismissal watermark and no selective clearing path, so stale launcher/configuration errors could linger across settings changes.

#### Lines 360-362, 488-557 - Move Thread Git Location from Scalar Branch/Worktree to Indexed Repo State
`syncServerReadModel(...)` now stores `projectPath: thread.projectPath` alongside `branch` and `worktreePath`. More importantly, `setThreadBranch(...)` expands from `(threadId, branch, worktreePath)` to `(threadId, branch, worktreePath, branchIndex = 0, projectPath?)`, uses `setBranchAtIndex(...)` and `setWorktreePathAtIndex(...)` from `@t3tools/shared/threadGit`, derives `nextProjectPath = projectPath ?? worktreePath ?? t.projectPath`, and compares/updates `t.branch` and `t.worktreePath` as indexed multi-repo values rather than scalar strings. The old contract it replaces was "a thread has one branch and one worktree path"; the new contract is "a thread can track per-repo branch/worktree arrays plus a selected `projectPath`."
- Feature:
#### Lines 25-53, 57-111, 135-204 - Persist Project UI State by Remote-Aware Project Key
Changed the top-level browser project registry so sidebar expansion and ordering are keyed by `projectPersistenceKey({ cwd, remote })` instead of by bare cwd strings. This supports the `Remote SSH Support` user feature by differentiating a local checkout from an SSH-backed checkout that resolves to the same path text, and it is part of the thread-session-project persistence and sidebar ordering component.

#### Lines 154-173 - Carry Remote and Multi-Repo Project Topology into the Browser Store
Changed project hydration to store `project.remote`, `project.gitMode`, and `project.gitRepos` from the orchestration read model so the UI can tell whether a project is local vs SSH-backed and whether Git discovery found zero, one, or many repositories under the same project root. This supports both the `Remote SSH Support` and `Multi-Repo Support` user features, and it is part of the project projection and project-to-repo topology component.

#### Lines 207-216, 298-318 - Preserve Disconnected and Reconnect Session Metadata
Changed session hydration to preserve the exact disconnected/reconnect state exported by orchestration instead of flattening it away. This supports `Debugability and Stability` by exposing `providerThreadId`, resumability, reconnect state, reconnect summary text, and reconnect timestamps to the web layer, and it is part of the provider-session health and recovery-status projection component.

#### Lines 228-232 - Normalize Kiro Provider Names in Legacy Session Mapping
Changed provider normalization so a hydrated session with `providerName === "kiro"` remains a Kiro session all the way through the browser store instead of being misclassified as the default provider. This supports the `Kiro Integration` user feature and is part of the browser provider-kind normalization component.

#### Lines 262-269, 325-333 - Scope Attachment Preview URLs by Project and Thread
Changed attachment materialization to build preview URLs with `projectId` and `threadId`, so attachment fetches resolve through the owning project/thread namespace instead of a global attachment endpoint. This supports the `Remote SSH Support` user feature by making attachment retrieval compatible with project-scoped routing and future remote-aware attachment serving, and it is part of the thread-message attachment preview routing component.

#### Lines 18-22, 39-43, 461-485, 522-553 - Dismiss Local Codex Errors Without Touching Remote Threads
Changed error cleanup so a local Codex launcher/configuration failure can be dismissed after a settings change or successful restart without erasing unrelated remote-project or non-Codex provider errors. This supports `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the provider-health error lifecycle component.

#### Lines 360-362, 488-557 - Move Thread Git Location from Scalar Branch/Worktree to Indexed Repo State
Changed thread branch mutation to accept `branchIndex` and `projectPath`, update per-repo `branch` / `worktreePath` arrays through shared helpers, and reset the live session only when the selected repo/worktree actually changes. This supports the `Multi-Repo Support` user feature by letting one thread distinguish the selected repository from sibling repositories inside the same project, and it is part of the thread-session-project-turn mapping and selected-repo state component.

### `apps/web/src/terminalStateStore.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines 10, 30-56, 570-573 - Guard Persisted Terminal Storage Behind a StateStorage Adapter
The fork imports `StateStorage` from `zustand/middleware`, adds `createMemoryStorage()` and `isStateStorage(storage)`, and introduces `terminalStateStorage` as the authoritative persistence backend. Instead of unconditionally doing `createJSONStorage(() => localStorage)`, the persisted store now does `createJSONStorage(() => terminalStateStorage)`, where `terminalStateStorage` is `localStorage` only if it exists and implements `getItem` / `setItem` / `removeItem`; otherwise it falls back to a private in-memory `Map<string, string>`. The terminal UI state model itself is unchanged; the delta is entirely in how persistence is bootstrapped.
- Feature:
#### Lines 10, 30-56, 570-573 - Guard Persisted Terminal Storage Behind a StateStorage Adapter
Changed terminal UI persistence so the store can initialize safely in browsers, tests, and setup phases where `localStorage` is absent or mocked with the wrong shape. This supports `Debugability and Stability` by preventing terminal-store hydration from crashing the app before any terminal UI renders, and it is part of the persisted terminal state bootstrap component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines 10, 30-56, 570-573 - Guard Persisted Terminal Storage Behind a StateStorage Adapter
This depends on Zustand `persist` middleware semantics and every consumer of `apps/web/src/terminalStateStore.ts`, especially `apps/web/src/components/ThreadTerminalDrawer.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/ChatView.tsx`, and any test harness or browser shell that loads the store before stable Web APIs are available. The old contract was "global `localStorage` is always safe"; the new one is "use validated storage or degrade to memory." If this drifts, the first failures will be store-construction exceptions, missing terminal state across refreshes, or flaky tests that only fail under mocked browser environments. Retest initial app load, terminal open/close persistence through refresh, and any fixture or desktop/web embedding environment that lacks a fully compliant `localStorage`.

### `apps/web/src/threadEnvMode.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `1-54`
`bb77342f` adds this file as the shared draft-thread env-mode contract. The authoritative input type is `ThreadEnvInput { projectRemote }`, and the authoritative helpers are `supportsDraftWorktreeEnv(...)`, `resolveRequestedThreadEnvMode(...)`, `resolvePersistedThreadEnvMode(...)`, and `resolveEffectiveThreadEnvMode(...)`. The old contract it replaced was scattered inline env-mode logic across ChatView, new-thread handling, sidebar logic, and branch-toolbar code. The key behavior encoded here is: `worktreePath` wins and yields `"worktree"` immediately; otherwise `requestedEnvMode ?? defaultEnvMode ?? "local"` is normalized through `supportsDraftWorktreeEnv(...)`.

#### Lines `8-10`
`0b6e734c` is a distinct follow-up that changes one decision point: `supportsDraftWorktreeEnv(input)` originally returned `input.projectRemote == null`, but the current file ignores the input and returns `true`. The old contract it replaced was "remote SSH projects cannot keep draft worktree mode." The rest of the file still preserves the higher-priority rule that a real `worktreePath` forces `"worktree"`.

#### Lines `1-54`

This supports `Remote SSH Support` and `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the draft-thread env-mode normalization component. Concretely, `resolvePersistedThreadEnvMode(...)` is the authoritative fallback path for stale drafts: if there is no real worktree path, the mode is recomputed instead of trusting old persisted state blindly.

#### Lines `8-10`
Changed the shared env-mode gate so remote SSH projects are once again allowed to advertise and preserve worktree env mode when the rest of the stack can actually prepare and use remote worktrees. This supports `Remote SSH Support` and is part of the remote worktree-prep capability gate.

### `apps/web/src/wsNativeApi.ts`

- Status: `Modified`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines 126-135 - Add Project-Scoped Editor RPCs and Replace Raw `cwd` Shell Opens
The fork extends the `projects` API block with `openInEditor(input)` and `openPathInEditor(input)`, both routed through `WS_METHODS.projectsOpenInEditor` / `WS_METHODS.projectsOpenPathInEditor`. In the same change chain, `shell.openInEditor` stops taking `(cwd, editor)` and now takes `(target, editor)`, sending `{ target, editor }` over `WS_METHODS.shellOpenInEditor`. The old contract it replaced was "editor opening is either project-agnostic or keyed by a raw cwd string"; the new contract is "editor opening goes through typed project-aware or shell-target-aware payloads."

#### Lines 181-186 - Add SSH Host Discovery and Remote Project Validation RPCs
Upstream only exposed `server.getConfig()` and `server.upsertKeybinding(...)` in this block. Those methods make the remote-project bootstrap path first-class at the browser API layer instead of forcing the UI to infer SSH viability indirectly.

#### Lines 188-195 - Remove Client Timeout from Orchestration Command Dispatch
`orchestration.dispatchCommand(command)` now calls `transport.request(..., { command }, { timeoutMs: null })` instead of using the transport default timeout. The old contract it replaced was "turn dispatch can fail client-side on timeout even while the server is still processing"; the new contract leaves orchestration command duration bounded by the server/runtime flow rather than a client request timer.

#### Lines 126-135 - Add Project-Scoped Editor RPCs and Replace Raw `cwd` Shell Opens
Changed the browser RPC adapter so file-opening flows can address files by `projectId`/project-relative path or by a richer shell editor target instead of by a raw cwd string. - Feature:
#### Lines `1-3`, `32-69`

This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the thread-session-project-repo mapping / multi-repo thread-state component.

#### Lines `419-453`, `750-756`
Changed turn-start dispatch so each turn can persist the exact git-writing settings resolved in the UI, including `githubBinaryPath`, `commitPrompt`, and `textGenerationModelSelection`, instead of letting downstream reactors guess from current app settings at execution time. This supports `Debugability and Stability` and is part of the turn finalization / checkpoint-diff projection component.

### `packages/shared/src/threadGit.ts`

- Status: `Added`
- Changes vs upstream:
#### Lines `1-39`
`efd5f211` adds this file as the shared array-based thread git adapter. `ThreadGitStateLike` at lines `1-5` fixes the minimum thread git shape as `{ projectPath, branch[], worktreePath[] }`; `getSingleRepoBranch(...)` and `getSingleRepoWorktreePath(...)` at lines `7-13` explicitly treat slot `0` as the single-repo compatibility view; and `setBranchAtIndex(...)` / `setWorktreePathAtIndex(...)` at lines `15-39` grow the target array with `null` placeholders until the requested repo index exists before assigning the new value. The old contract it replaced was "each caller reads `branch` / `worktreePath` arrays directly or still assumes one scalar branch/worktree field."
- Feature:
#### Lines `1-39`
Added one shared adapter for reading and updating multi-repo thread git state, with an explicit slot-`0` fallback for single-repo flows and index-aware setters for repo-selection UI. This supports `Multi-Repo Support` and is part of the thread git array compatibility component.
- Dependency impact:
#### Lines `1-39`
This subsection depends on [`apps/web/src/store.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/store.ts), [`apps/web/src/composerDraftStore.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/composerDraftStore.ts), [`apps/web/src/routes/_chat.tsx`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/routes/_chat.tsx), [`apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbar.tsx`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/components/BranchToolbar.tsx), and cleanup helpers such as [`apps/web/src/worktreeCleanup.ts`](/Users/ashvinn/.t3/worktrees/t3code/t3code-11837d0b/apps/web/src/worktreeCleanup.ts). The fallback behavior matters: single-repo callers read slot `0`, and setters fill missing slots with `null` instead of leaving sparse arrays. If this block drifts, repo switching can write the wrong index, shortcut/new-thread flows can read the wrong branch, or cleanup logic can misidentify which worktree belongs to which repo slot. Retest selected-repo switching, new-thread inheritance, branch/worktree updates, and worktree cleanup in both single-repo and multi-repo threads.
